Hensler v. City of Davenport


No. 1-681 / 11-0443


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


807 N.W.2d 297; 2011 Iowa App. LEXIS 1007



October 5, 2011, Filed


NOTICE: PUBLISHED IN TABLE FORMAT IN THE NORTH WESTERN REPORTER.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Scott County, Gary McKendrick, Judge. Defendant appeals the district court's order requiring it to pay plaintiff's attorney fees in an action challenging a city ordinance under 42 U.S.C. §§ 1983 and 1988.
Hensler v. City of Davenport, 790 N.W.2d 569, 2010 Iowa Sup. LEXIS 111 (Iowa, 2010)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff mother received a citation for a second violation of a city parental responsibility ordinance. She filed a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 civil rights petition against defendant city. The trial court found the ordinance violated her state and federal substantive due process rights, and awarded attorney fees. The state supreme court found the ordinance was invalid only to a limited extent. The trial court on remand awarded her the full attorney fee amount it previously ordered. The appellate court found it should have awarded 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988 attorney fees according to her level of success.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and case remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

Trs. of the Iowa Laborers Dist. Council Health & Welfare Trust v. Ankeny Cmty. Sch. Dist.


No. 1-398 / 10-1880


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


807 N.W.2d 158; 2011 Iowa App. LEXIS 924



September 21, 2011, Filed


NOTICE: PUBLISHED IN TABLE FORMAT IN THE NORTH WESTERN REPORTER.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Polk County, Carla T. Schemmel, Judge. A general contractor and its bonding company appeal the ruling of the district court in favor of the plaintiffs.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Defendants general contractor and bonding company argued, inter alia, that the district court erred in failing to rule that plaintiff unions had not submitted an itemized statement of their claims for labor as required by Iowa Code § 573.7 (2007). The court of appeals disagreed. Unions' notice of claim listed in detail five union trusts/funds to which they claimed fringe benefits and dues were owed and unpaid. The amount claimed due for each trust/fund was set forth, and those amounts were totaled.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Lopez-Penaloza v. State


No. 1-596 / 10-1205


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


804 N.W.2d 537; 2011 Iowa App. LEXIS 893



September 8, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 11, 2011.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Woodbury County, Gary Wenell, Judge. Erika Lopez-Penaloza appeals the district court's dismissal of her application for postconviction relief.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: The trial court dismissed defendant's postconviction relief request, which she filed to challenge her trial counsel's failure to adequately advise her about the deportation consequences of her guilty plea to tampering with records. It found her claims were untimely under Iowa Code § 822.3 (2009) and without merit. The appellate court found that her request filed nearly six years after her conviction was entered was barred by that statute's three-year limitations period, no exception applied, and the written guilty plea form and sentencing order adequately informed her of such consequences.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. Medved


No. 1-487 / 10-1053


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


805 N.W.2d 397; 2011 Iowa App. LEXIS 820



August 10, 2011, Filed


NOTICE: PUBLISHED IN TABLE FORMAT IN THE NORTH WESTERN REPORTER.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Black Hawk County, Kellyann M. Lekar (suppression) and Jon Fister (trial, sentencing), Judges. Defendant appeals his conviction and sentence for ongoing criminal conduct and delivery of a controlled substance.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: The four witnesses testified to purchasing marijuana from defendant. Also, in defendant's bedroom, police found an open safe containing pipes used for smoking marijuana. Defendant's closet contained more glass pipes for smoking marijuana. Other items discovered in defendant's bedroom included: his billfold, his driver's license, a beverage can with a hidden compartment, a digital gram scale, a marijuana grinder, a box of unused plastic sandwich bags, and a large sum of cash. Thus, the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's drug-related convictions.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. Ennenga


No. 1-572 / 10-1490


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


805 N.W.2d 398; 2011 Iowa App. LEXIS 851



August 10, 2011, Filed


NOTICE: PUBLISHED IN TABLE FORMAT IN THE NORTH WESTERN REPORTER.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Polk County, Richard G. Blane II, Judge. The defendant appeals from the order denying his motion to correct an illegal sentence.
State v. Ennenga, 2001 Iowa App. LEXIS 51 (Iowa Ct. App., Jan. 24, 2001)



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Defendant filed a motion to correct an illegal sentence that attacked the factual basis of his guilty plea. The district court denied defendant's motion because the grounds alleged went beyond the scope of a motion for correction of an illegal sentence under Iowa R. Crim. P. 2.24(5)(a). On review, the court held that, because defendant's sentence expired before he filed his motion, any decision would have no practice effect upon the controversy. As such, defendant's appeal was moot.


OUTCOME: Defendant's appeal was dismissed as moot.

 

406 of 583 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kehoe


No. 1-324 / 09-1896


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


804 N.W.2d 302; 2011 Iowa App. LEXIS 642



July 13, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 23, 2011.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Buchanan County, Bruce B. Zager, Judge. Michelle Kehoe appeals from her convictions for first-degree murder, attempted murder, and child endangerment resulting in serious injury.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Legislature's adoption of the M'Naghten rule under Iowa Code § 701.4 did not violate the prohibition against cruel and unusual punishment under U.S. Const. amend. VIII and Iowa Const. art. I, § 17; as such, counsel was not ineffective for failing to challenge the constitutionality of that statute under the state and federal constitutions. Further, counsel was not ineffective for failing to request a jury instruction informing the jury of the consequences of a verdict of not guilty by reason of insanity because such an instruction was inappropriate and unnecessary.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions of first-degree murder, attempted murder, and child endangerment resulting in serious injury were affirmed.

408 of 583 DOCUMENTS


Nance v. State


No. 1-453 / 10-0810


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


803 N.W.2d 129; 2011 Iowa App. LEXIS 494



June 29, 2011, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO IOWA RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Scott County, Mary E. Howes, Judge. Applicant appeals the denial of his application for post-conviction relief.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Appellant's sentence did not amount to cruel and unusual punishment because the state supreme court held that Iowa Code § 903B.2 was not grossly disproportionate as applied to a defendant convicted of misdemeanor indecent exposure, which carried a penalty of up to one year in the county jail; thus, it clearly was not grossly disproportionate when applied to a defendant convicted of the aggravated misdemeanor of assault with the intent to commit sexual abuse, which carried a penalty of up to two years in prison. Appellant's claim of cruel and unusual punishment thus had no merit.


OUTCOME: The denial of appellant's application for postconviction relief was affirmed.

413 of 583 DOCUMENTS


Morales v. Iowa DOT


No. 0-324 / 09-1642


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2011 Iowa App. LEXIS 143



February 23, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Morales v. Iowa DOT, 798 N.W.2d 349, 2011 Iowa App. LEXIS 700 (Iowa Ct. App., 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Adams County, Gregory A. Hulse, Judge. Morales appeals the district court's order affirming his driver's license revocation based on his refusal of chemical testing.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Failure to give the complete implied consent advisory precluded revocation of the driver's ordinary driver's license, as well as precluding disqualification of his commercial driver's license (CDL). The duty to provide the information found in Iowa Code § 321J.8 was mandatory. Not fully informing the driver about the CDL consequences rendered his refusal to chemical testing while operating his personal vehicle involuntary and not a viable basis for either disqualifying his CDL or revoking his ordinary driver's license.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and remanded.

In the Interest of J.D.P.


No. 0-900 / 10-0115


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2011 Iowa App. LEXIS 102



February 9, 2011, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNTIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at In the Interest of J.D.P., 797 N.W.2d 623, 2011 Iowa App. LEXIS 527 (Iowa Ct. App., 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Johnson County, Sylvia A. Lewis, Judge. J.D.P. appeals the juvenile court's order requiring him to register as a sex offender.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: The juvenile was a juvenile offender who was required to be on the sex offender registry as of June 30, 2009, because as of June 30, 2009, the juvenile court had not exercised its discretion to excuse the juvenile from registration. The amendments to Iowa Code ch. 692A, effective July 1, 2009, retroactively applied to the juvenile's registration as a sex offender. Iowa Code ch. 692A was regulatory or remedial, not punitive, and therefore not ex post facto when applied retroactively.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

415 of 583 DOCUMENTS


State v. Casper


No. 0-839 / 09-1528


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2011 Iowa App. LEXIS 13



January 20, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Casper, 797 N.W.2d 622, 2011 Iowa App. LEXIS 563 (Iowa Ct. App., 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Cedar County, Paul L. Macek, Judge. Jamie Vernon Casper appeals following a jury trial from a conviction of indecent exposure in violation of Iowa Code section 709.9 (2007).



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE VACATED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Iowa District Court for Cedar County, which convicted him of indecent exposure, in violation of Iowa Code § 709.9 (2007).


OVERVIEW: A victim called 911 to report that she had observed a man standing on the side of the road with his pants down moving his penis in a circular motion. An officer then stopped a vehicle matching the description given. The victim later identified defendant as the man she had seen earlier. At trial, defendant made a hearsay objection to a deputy's testimony regarding the victim's identification. The trial court overruled the objection, defendant was convicted, and this appeal followed. In partially affirming, the appellate court determined that the descriptions of defendant and his truck provided by the victim were non-hearsay under Iowa R. Evid. 5.801(d)(1)(B) or (C). Evidence of a prior out-of-court identification of an accused was usually permitted. The victim testified before the deputy, and there was an implied suggestion that the identification of defendant and his truck were the result of improper influence or motive or her memory was not clear. However, the trial court erred by prohibiting defendant from having no contact with minors for a period of five years. This portion of the sentence was unconstitutionally excessive.


OUTCOME: The portion of the sentence imposing a five-year no-contact order was vacated. In all other respects, the decision was affirmed.

417 of 583 DOCUMENTS


Chang Ming Lin v. State


No. 0-788 / 10-0141


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2010 Iowa App. LEXIS 1571



December 22, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Chang Ming Lin v. State, 797 N.W.2d 131, 2010 Iowa App. LEXIS 1873 (Iowa Ct. App., 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Polk County, Glenn E. Pille, Judge. The applicant appeals from the district court's order dismissing his application for postconviction relief.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant applicant appealed from an order of the Polk County District Court, Iowa, dismissing his application for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Appellant asserted that his trial attorneys were ineffective for: (1) failing to procure an interpreter prior to a guilty plea proceeding, and (2) for failing to advise him that a conviction could result in deportation. The court found that appellant's trial counsel was not ineffective. The transcript of the guilty plea hearing, and the testimony and other evidence demonstrated that appellant did not need an interpreter and meaningfully participated in the guilty plea that was tendered to the trial court. Although appellant testified that he did not speak English well enough to understand and effectively participate in the guilty plea proceedings, the evidence demonstrated otherwise. Appellant communicated with his friends and family members in English and prior to his arrest, he was involved in running a business at a shopping mall Appellant could not prevail on his ineffective-assistance-of-counsel claim based upon his trial attorneys' failure to advise him of the immigration consequences of a conviction. The transcript at the plea hearing demonstrated that appellant's trial attorneys had advised him of the immigration consequences, including the possibility of deportation.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

 

418 of 583 DOCUMENTS


Dohmen v. Iowa Dep't for the Blind


No. 0-491/09-1108


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


794 N.W.2d 295; 2010 Iowa App. LEXIS 1372



November 10, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 20, 2011.
Reported at Dohmen v. Iowa Dep't for the Blind, 791 N.W.2d 710, 2010 Iowa App. LEXIS 1613 (Iowa Ct. App., 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Polk County, Carla T. Schemmel, Judge. Plaintiff appeals the court's denial of her motion for a new trial. Defendant cross-appeals contending the court erred in denying its motion for summary judgment.
Dohmen v. Iowa Dep't for the Blind, 755 N.W.2d 144, 2008 Iowa App. LEXIS 1429 (Iowa Ct. App., 2008)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff disabled student sought review of an order entered by the Iowa District Court for Polk County, which denied her motion for a new trial in the student's action against defendant, the Iowa Department for the Blind, alleging discrimination under the Americans with Disabilities Act (ADA), the Federal Rehabilitation Act, and the Iowa Civil Rights Act. The Department cross-appealed the denial of its motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The student, who was legally blind, sought training in Braille and computer skills but was not permitted to participate with her guide dog; she was offered, inter alia, individual instruction at her home. The student was not entitled to a new trial because the jury instructions given incorporated the law on providing services in a segregated setting outside of the Department's regular training program. A requested instruction on offering alternative training correctly stated the law under 28 C.F.R. § 35.130(d), (e), but the law did not apply to the facts of the case as the student was admitted to full participation but rejected it; all other blind participants were not permitted to use a guide dog either. Summary judgment was properly denied to the Department as Congress had validly abrogated its immunity as a State entity with respect to the ADA claims under 42 U.S.C.S. § 12202. Congress acted within its authority under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 5 because the limited remedies available under the ADA were congruent and proportional to the goal of preventing unconstitutional discrimination against disabled individuals in public education.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders on both appeal and cross-appeal.

420 of 583 DOCUMENTS


State v. Adams


No. 0-494 / 09-1499


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2010 Iowa App. LEXIS 1163



October 6, 2010, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNTIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Adams, 791 N.W.2d 429, 2010 Iowa App. LEXIS 1765 (Iowa Ct. App., 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Clarke County, Monty W. Franklin, District Associate Judge. Joseph Allan Adams appeals his convictions and sentence for violating a sex offender residency restriction and failing to register a change of residence.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an appeal from the Clarke County District Court, Iowa, defendant appealed his convictions and sentence for violating a sex offender residency restriction and failing to register a change of residence.


OVERVIEW: The court rejected defendant's contention that the terms "reside" and "residence" within the sex offender residency restriction and registration statutes were unconstitutionally vague, as well as his contention that his trial counsel was ineffective for failing to challenge the registration statute's requirement that a sex offender register within five days of changing residence within a county. There was sufficient evidence to sustain defendant's conviction for violating the residence restriction because that was a strict liability offense. However, the State failed to prove defendant had the necessary mens rea to violate the registration law. There was insufficient evidence defendant knew or should have known of the duty to register a change in residence. Although Iowa law required the offender to be informed of the duty to register within five days of changing residence, there was no evidence in this record that defendant was so informed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for violating the residency restriction, but reversed his conviction for failing to register.

 

421 of 583 DOCUMENTS


JCO Props. v. Bd. of Review for Scott County


No. 0-429 / 09-1453


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2010 Iowa App. LEXIS 1162



October 6, 2010, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNTIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at JCO Props. v. Bd. of Review, 791 N.W.2d 429, 2010 Iowa App. LEXIS 1750 (Iowa Ct. App., 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Scott County, Gary D. McKenrick, Judge. A taxpayer appeals from a district court ruling establishing the assessed value of lots.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of a judgment from the District Court for Scott County (Iowa), which, in consolidated appeals from decisions from appellee county board of review, established the assessed value of the taxpayer's vacant residential lots in two subdivisions.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer's expert witnesses applied an absorption rate to discount the value of the lots by adjusting the market value to account for the length of time it would take for the lots to be sold. The assessor's expert witness testified as to the market value of the lots without an absorption discount, stating that the market price already accounted for the availability or unavailability of buyers. The district court considered the application of an absorption discount but concluded that the evidence presented by the taxpayer's expert witnesses was highly speculative. The court held that the use of an absorption discount was not appropriate in determining assessed valuation for property tax purposes. Under Iowa Code § 441.21(1)(b) (1993), market value was defined as the fair and reasonable exchange in the year in which the property was listed and valued between a willing buyer and a willing seller. Thus, the presence of a willing buyer and a transaction occurring in the year in question both had to be presumed for assessment purposes. An argument that the district court lacked authority to increase property valuations, asserted for the first time in a reply brief, was waived.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court.

 

422 of 583 DOCUMENTS


In re Brown


No. 0-326 / 09-1651


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2010 Iowa App. LEXIS 870



August 25, 2010, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNTIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at In re Guardianship of Brown, 789 N.W.2d 436, 2010 Iowa App. LEXIS 1482 (Iowa Ct. App., 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Polk County, Ruth B. Klotz, District Associate Probate Judge. Ward's father appeals from district court ruling granting the guardian's motion to dismiss the father's motion to vacate the guardianship and request for other relief.



DISPOSITION: VACATED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of an order of the Iowa District Court for Polk County, granting appellee mother's motion to dismiss the father's motion to vacate the guardianship of their son, the ward. The father had challenged the fact that the mother did not name, in her guardianship petition, the father as a custodian as required by Iowa Code § 633.552 and that she did not provide notice to him in accordance with Iowa Code § 633.554(b)(1).


OVERVIEW: The mother filed her petition for guardianship seven days before the ward's eighteenth birthday. The petition failed to state that the father was a joint custodian. The father learned of the guardianship ten days after the mother was appointed. On appeal, the court decided, contrary to the holding of the district court, that the father was an interested party and his interests were not represented in the guardianship. The father had a strong bond with the ward, had custody of him fifty percent of the time at the time the petition was filed, and provided him financial support. In the mother's petition, she misrepresented to the district court that she alone was the ward's custodian when at that time she only shared custodial responsibilities with the father. Neither did she mention the father at all. Those false and inadequate representations allowed the mother to be named guardian of the ward without notice to the father as required by § 633.554(b)(1). A judgment entered without proper notice was generally considered void and could be attacked at any time. Therefore, the father's application to vacate the guardianship did not have to comply with Iowa R. Civ. P. 1.1013.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order establishing the mother as guardian and remanded to the court to consider the petition for appointment of guardian after notice to the ward, his attorney, the mother, and the father.

 

423 of 583 DOCUMENTS


State v. Breuer


No. 0-423 / 09-1170


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2010 Iowa App. LEXIS 838



August 11, 2010, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNTIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Breuer, 789 N.W.2d 165, 2010 Iowa App. LEXIS 1450 (Iowa Ct. App., 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Jasper County, Darrell Goodhue, Judge. Lee Allen Breuer was granted discretionary review of the denial of his motion to suppress.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Iowa District Court for Jasper County of homicide by vehicle. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred by denying his motion to suppress evidence because the blood was withdrawn without his consent and prior to the arrival of the warrant authorizing the test, thereby violating his state and federal constitutional rights to be free from unreasonable searches and seizure. The court of appeals disagreed. The withdrawal of blood was an intrusion of one's bodily security, and the threat of force was important to an analysis of a consent search. However, defendant did not challenge that probable cause existed for the warrant, which was obtained because his refusal to consent was honored by the officers. Where a search warrant was sought to authorize an intrusion into the human body, the court must determine not only whether officers had probable cause, but must weigh other factors, including the risk to the suspect and the extent of the intrusion on the suspect's interest in personal privacy and bodily integrity. However, once the warrant was issued, a suspect's interest in safety, dignity, and privacy were not furthered by a requirement that officers possess or display the warrant authorizing the search.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

424 of 583 DOCUMENTS


State v. Harris


No. 0-456 / 09-1242


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2010 Iowa App. LEXIS 800



July 28, 2010, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNTIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Emmet County, Don E. Courtney, Judge. Brandon Harris appeals the district court order extending the term of his probation.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty in the Iowa District Court for Emmet County to possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver. Defendant was sentenced to probation, which was later revoked. Defendant was then sentenced to ninety days in jail and his probation was extended. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the district court lacked the authority under Iowa Code § 908.11(4) to extend his probation. The court of appeals agreed. The State argued, inter alia, that defendant failed to comply with the court-ordered restitution plan, and thus the district court had the power to extend his probation pursuant to Iowa Code § 910.4(1)(b). According to the State, at the time of the probation revocation hearing, defendant continued to owe $ 553 in restitution. However, the problem with that argument was that the district court did not find defendant in violation of his restitution obligations. In fact, defendant appeared to have been ahead of the payment schedule, at least in regards to his primary obligation. At the time of the revocation hearing (only nine months into his payment plan), defendant had already paid $ 1522 of his primary restitution obligation and had only $ 403 left. The legislature gave the district court four alternatives for addressing probation violations, at least when the violation involved something other than failure to pay restitution. Therefore, the district court lacked the statutory authority to extend defendant's probation by two years.


OUTCOME: The two year extension of probation was reversed. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

 

425 of 583 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ostrander


No. 0-309 / 09-0976


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2010 Iowa App. LEXIS 760



July 14, 2010, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNTIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Polk County, Scott D. Rosenberg, Judge. Mark Ostrander appeals his conviction for assault causing serious injury.
State v. Ostrander, 788 N.W.2d 397, 2010 Iowa App. LEXIS 1302 (Iowa Ct. App., 2010)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged by trial information with one count of willful injury causing serious injury under Iowa Code § 708.4(1). A jury for the Iowa District Court for Polk County found him guilty of the lesser included offense of assault causing serious injury under Iowa Code §§ 708.1 and 708.2(4) (2007). He was sentenced to be imprisoned for a term not to exceed five years. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The testimony from the witnesses supported the victim's contention that defendant approached his property, threatened him, and then proceeded to punch and kick him. Given the evidence presented, a jury could find sufficient evidence demonstrated that defendant instigated or provoked a fight, or had the ability to retreat at any point during the altercation, but failed to do so. Thus, the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal, as sufficient evidence was presented for the jury to decide that the State proved each element of assault causing serious injury beyond a reasonable doubt including by the same standard, negating defendant's justification defense under Iowa Code §§ 704.3 and 704.6. The undisputed injuries included damage to the victim's left orbital socket, requiring reconstructive surgery, severe bruising on his liver and thigh, and severance of his intestine from his colostomy bag. Thus, under Iowa Code §§ 902.3 and 902.9, the severity of the five-year sentence was not cruel and unusual under the Eighth Amendment as it was not grossly disproportionate to the gravity of the crime committed.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

426 of 583 DOCUMENTS


State v. Glenn


No. 0-416 / 08-1530


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2010 Iowa App. LEXIS 651



June 30, 2010, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNTIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Glenn, 787 N.W.2d 480, 2010 Iowa App. LEXIS 1263 (Iowa Ct. App., 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Polk County, Don C. Nickerson, Judge. The defendant appeals following resentencing for two counts of lascivious acts with a child in violation of Iowa Code section 709.8(1), (2), and (3) (2003).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Iowa District Court for Polk County convicted defendant, upon his guilty plea, of two counts of lascivious acts with a child under Iowa Code § 709.8(1), (2), and (3) (2003). After defendant's sentence had been vacated and remanded to the district court for resentencing, a different judge than the one who originally sentenced defendant imposed a sentence of two five-year terms of imprisonment, to be served consecutively. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted that the imposition of consecutive sentences demonstrated vindictiveness in sentencing. The district court's statements reflected that it carefully weighed the sentencing options and decided to impose consecutive sentences for logical, non-vindictive reasons, including for the protection of the public and to ensure that defendant would continue rehabilitation efforts. Thus, his vindictiveness claim failed. Also, the district court's statements that it was imposing consecutive sentences because it was concerned about protecting the public and that defendant needed more time than he would served pursuant to a concurrent sentence arrangement to continue his rehabilitation met the requirement in Iowa R. Crim. P. 2.23(3)(d) that the district court had to disclose on the record its reasons for selecting a particular sentence. Further, the district court stated generally it had considered the victim impact statements, but there was nothing to demonstrate that the district court specifically relied upon the alleged abuse of the victim's sister and the mother's reference to other offenses in her statement was vague, oblique, and fleeting. Thus, the sentence was proper.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the district court's judgment.

 

427 of 583 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gates


No. 0-351 / 09-1241


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2010 Iowa App. LEXIS 667



June 30, 2010, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNTIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Gates, 787 N.W.2d 480, 2010 Iowa App. LEXIS 1275 (Iowa Ct. App., 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Linn County, Robert E. Sosalla (suppression) and David M. Remley (trial and sentencing), Judges. Connie Jo Gates appeals from her convictions for homicide by vehicle while a controlled substance was present, homicide by vehicle while attempting to elude, operating a motor vehicle without the owner's consent, and possession of a controlled substance.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the Iowa District Court for Linn County found defendant guilty of homicide by vehicle while any amount of a controlled substance was present under Iowa Code § 707.6A(1) (2009); homicide by vehicle while attempting to elude under Iowa Code § 707.6A(2)(b); operating a motor vehicle without the owner's consent under Iowa Code § 714.7; and possession of a controlled substance under Iowa Code § 124.401(5) (2009). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to the Fourth Amendment and Iowa Const. art. I, § 8, the officers had a reasonable basis to conduct protective searches of defendant's clothing and purse because she had been involved in a reckless, high-speed attempt to elude the officers prior to an accident and the officers could have reasonably expected she might continue her attempt to escape the authorities by using weapons on her person or in her purse. Also, during the initial search of her clothing, defendant was not immobilized because she was not yet on a backboard. In addition, the search of the purse was justified because defendant could have used a weapon therein against the unarmed paramedics. Thus, the district court did not err in denying her motion to suppress the evidence seized incident to the search of her clothing and purse. Defendant's statements to the paramedic were not privileged under Iowa Code § 622.10(1). Trial counsel was not ineffective under the Sixth Amendment in failing to object to the admission of the results of the urine test based on implied consent under Iowa Code § 321J.6. Defendant's motion for directed verdict of acquittal on the first homicide by vehicle count was properly denied.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

428 of 583 DOCUMENTS


State v. Armstrong


No. 0-307 / 09-0972


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


787 N.W.2d 472; 2010 Iowa App. LEXIS 668



June 30, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 3, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Plymouth County, Robert J. Dull, Judge. Brett Armstrong appeals the judgment and sentence entered upon his conviction of identity theft.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a bench trial, the Iowa District Court for Plymouth County found defendant guilty of identity theft in violation of Iowa Code § 715A.8 (2007). On appeal, defendant argued that: 1) the State did not present sufficient evidence to prove that he was guilty of identity theft; and 2) his counsel was ineffective for failing to argue that § 715A.8 was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad.


OVERVIEW: The police responded to complaints of noise and possible underage drinking and began checking identifications. Defendant identified himself as his brother to avoid arrest on an outstanding warrant. On appeal, the court disagreed with defendant's argument that § 715A.8(2) only applied when someone fraudulently used another's identification information to obtain a financial benefit. Looking to the word "benefit" in the statute, it was clear that a benefit was any form of advantage. Defendant attempted to gain the advantage of not being arrested under the outstanding warrant in his own name. The court concluded that the State presented substantial evidence to support the district court's verdict that defendant was guilty of identity theft. However, due to an absence in the statute of a means to determine the level of offense, the district court's designation of the crime as an aggravated misdemeanor was not supported by substantial evidence. Defendant's overbreadth argument was waived because he failed to explain what First Amendment right was violated, and his counsel had no duty to raise a vagueness challenge to the statute because it was not vague as applied to defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of identity theft, it reversed the designation of the crime as an aggravated misdemeanor, and it remanded the case to the district court for a finding of the level of the offense and, if necessary, resentencing.

 

429 of 583 DOCUMENTS


Ely v. City Council


No. 0-317/09-1424


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2010 Iowa App. LEXIS 673



June 30, 2010, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNTIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Ely v. City Council of Ames, 787 N.W.2d 479, 2010 Iowa App. LEXIS 1253 (Iowa Ct. App., 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Story County, Dale E. Ruigh, Judge. Plaintiffs appeal the district court ruling rejecting plaintiffs' constitutional challenges to the Ames municipal code and its determination that the city council did not engage in illegal spot zoning.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED, WRIT ANNULLED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners filed a petition for certiorari, alleging defendant city violated their rights to due process and equal protection by designating property adjacent to their property as a historic landmark. Following a bench trial, the Story County District Court, Iowa, concluded that the designation did not violate the due process or equal protection clauses and was not illegal spot zoning. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: In 1920, a family built a house. From approximately 1920 to the late 1940s, this family provided room and board to African-American students attending Iowa State University when the students were denied housing elsewhere. The street on which the house was built was designated as a commercial zoning district. The home, which was rental residential property, was permitted as a nonconforming use. The court concluded that plaintiffs failed to prove they were denied due process when the city designated the house as a historical landmark. Plaintiffs' protected public interests were not immediately implicated in the designation of a neighboring property as a historical landmark. The city's procedure was adequate to protect plaintiffs' interest in maintaining property values and neighborhood aesthetics. There was no equal protection violation by the designation. The two properties were not treated differently as a result of the designation. The city's rezoning of the house did not constitute illegal spot zoning. The property was a permissible nonconforming use and the objective sought by the rezoning, historic preservation, was within the city's police power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of plaintiffs' action and annulled the writ.

Jensen v. City Council of Cambridge


No. 0-087 / 09-0697


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2010 Iowa App. LEXIS 573



June 16, 2010, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNTIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Jensen v. City Council, 786 N.W.2d 873, 2010 Iowa App. LEXIS 1199 (Iowa Ct. App., 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Story County, Michael J. Moon, Judge. A plaintiff challenges the constitutionality of a city's mowing ordinance and asserts that he was inappropriately denied an exemption from that ordinance.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner challenged a decision from the Iowa District Court for Story County, which denied his request for a permanent injunction in a case involving Cambridge, Iowa, Ordinance 07-A, § 3-1.0305(2).


OVERVIEW: The owner was served with a notice that he was in violation of Cambridge, Iowa, Ordinance 07-A, § 3-1.0305(2), and he unsuccessfully sought an exemption as a conservation area. Appellee city council conducted a hearing, but there was no record of the hearing and no written decision on the notice of violation or the request for an exemption. The owner then sought injunctive relief. The request for a permanent injunction was denied, and this appeal followed. In affirming, the appellate court determined that the ordinance at issue was not unconstitutionally vague based on the word "environment" in the definition of a "conservation area." The owner did not negate every reasonable basis upon which the ordinance could have been sustained. A mayor chose and applied one of several reasonable definitions of "environment." A statute was not unconstitutionally vague because a key word was not specifically defined. A challenge to the city council's action was not reviewed due to a lack of a record. Finally, a claim of procedural irregularity in the adoption of the ordinance was not properly submitted to the trial court; therefore, no error was preserved on this issue.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

Lampman v. State


No. 0-056 / 09-0310


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2010 Iowa App. LEXIS 293



April 21, 2010, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNTIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Lampman v. State, 784 N.W.2d 202, 2010 Iowa App. LEXIS 986 (Iowa Ct. App., 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Hardin County, Michael J. Moon, Judge. Applicant appeals following the district court's denial of his application for postconviction relief.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Iowa District Court for Hardin County, which convicted him of one count of sexual abuse in the third degree against a child who was 13 years old and one count of sexual abuse in the second degree against a child who was 11 years old. He received consecutive prison sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of sexual abuse of two children. The trial court imposed two consecutive sentences totaling 35 years in prison. The trial court denied his application for postconviction relief. On appeal, the court found that the admission of one victim's recantation testimony would not likely change the result if defendant was granted a new trial. There were sufficient discrepancies, unusual departures, and changes of testimony in the story the victim told at the postconviction hearing from which the trial court could have concluded that her testimony at the time of trial, and not at the hearing, was the true statement of the events that transpired. Further, counsel was not ineffective for not objecting to the marshalling instructions for second- and third-degree sexual abuse. It was quite unlikely that a jury would have found that defendant performed the sex acts but did not act knowingly and intentionally in so doing. Finally, the consecutive sentencing statute, Iowa Code § 901.8, was not unconstitutional. The trial judge had discretion in determining whether the sentences were to be served consecutively or concurrently.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Bennett v. State


No. 0-200 / 08-1157


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2010 Iowa App. LEXIS 265



April 8, 2010, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNTIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Bennett v. State, 784 N.W.2d 202, 2010 Iowa App. LEXIS 983 (Iowa Ct. App., 2010)
Post-conviction relief granted at, Remanded by State v. Bennett, 2012 Iowa App. LEXIS 542 (Iowa Ct. App., July 11, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Polk County, Karen A. Romano, Judge. Thomas Bennett appeals from the denial of his second application for postconviction relief.
State v. Bennett, 2000 Iowa App. LEXIS 45 (Iowa Ct. App., Nov. 8, 2000)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the order of the Iowa District Court for Polk County, denying his second application for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted appellant of first-degree murder in 1999, and the court sentenced him to life in prison. In 2007, appellant filed his second application for postconviction relief alleging his conviction and sentence was unconstitutional. The district court denied relief, because the application was filed three and a half years after the limitations period expired under Iowa Code § 822.3. The exception to the statute of limitations for newly discovered evidence did not apply, because an affidavit by codefendant recanting his statements implicating defendant in the murder did not meet the test for newly discovered evidence. The legal and factual underpinnings of appellant's claims were in existence during the three-year period and could have been addressed on direct appeal. Because appellant did not raise his separation of powers and equal protection claims before the district court, they were not preserved for review.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

433 of 583 DOCUMENTS


Allamakee County v. Thomas J. Schaumberg Living Trust


No. 9-650 / 09-0082


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2010 Iowa App. LEXIS 163



February 24, 2010, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNTIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Allamakee County v. Thomas J. Schaumberg Living Trust, 781 N.W.2d 101, 2010 Iowa App. LEXIS 597 (Iowa Ct. App., 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Allamakee County, Margaret L. Lingreen, Judge. Thomas J. Schaumberg appeals from the district court's grant of summary judgment in favor of Allamakee County.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owner challenged a decision from the Iowa District Court for Allamakee County, which granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, a county and a board of adjustment, in a zoning dispute.


OVERVIEW: The owner was ordered to stop construction because he did not comply with a zoning ordinance relating to setbacks. The owner contended that the ordinance did not apply to his property located in a private subdivision. He also argued that his property was not a corner lot required to have a side-yard setback. He also challenged the constitutionality of the zoning ordinance. In affirming, the appellate court determined that the Allamakee County, Iowa, Zoning Ordinance explicitly applied to private roads. Nothing in Iowa Code ch. 335 limited the application of a zoning ordinance to public streets. Therefore, it did not matter whether the bordering roads were public or private. Next, the owner's argument that his property was not a corner lot was rejected. Under the ordinance, in order for a thoroughfare to qualify as a street, it had to afford the principal means of access to an abutting property. Therefore, both lanes at issue in this case were streets, even though they were also cul de sacs. Finally, the ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague. When examined in the context of common understanding or practice, the definition of a street included a cul de sac.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

435 of 583 DOCUMENTS


Quaker Oats Co. v. Main


No. 9-896 / 08-1507


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2010 Iowa App. LEXIS 22



January 22, 2010, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNTIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Quaker Oats Co. v. Main, 779 N.W.2d 494, 2010 Iowa App. LEXIS 329 (Iowa Ct. App., 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Polk County, Joel D. Novak, Judge. An employee appeals from a district court judicial review ruling reversing in part the appeal decision of the workers' compensation commissioner.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Iowa District Court for Polk County reversed in part the appeal decision of the workers' compensation commissioner in favor of appellant employee. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee argued the district court erred in determining that his constitutional challenge to Iowa Code § 85.34(7) (2005) under the single-subject requirement of Iowa Const. art. III, § 29 was untimely and reversing the commissioner's determination that § 85.34(7) was inapplicable to his workers' compensation claim because his prior work injuries occurred before the statute's effective date. The appellate court agreed with the district court that the employee's constitutional challenge was not timely. Codification of legislature cured any defect in the subject matter or title. The amendments to Iowa Code § 85.34(7) were enacted and made effective on September 7, 2004. The employee did not file his workers' compensation petition until January 2006. His single-subject challenge was thus untimely. The employee did not have a right to institute and maintain a claim for benefits from two successive work-related injuries until his right shoulder injury occurred, despite the existence of his prior injuries.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

436 of 583 DOCUMENTS


Nicholson v. Frank


No. 9-832 / 08-1418


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 1631



December 17, 2009, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNTIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Nicholson v. HF05, 778 N.W.2d 218, 2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 1994 (Iowa Ct. App., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Floyd County, Colleen D. Weiland, Judge. A one-time property owner appeals the district court's decision to grant a tax deed holder's motion for summary judgment, contending that the statute prescribing the method of notice to a property owner of his or her right to redeem the property is unconstitutional.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant homeowner sought review of a decision of the Iowa District Court for Floyd County granting appellee tax deed holder's motion for summary judgment and dismissed the homeowner's petition against the holder and appellee county treasurer. The homeowner's petition had alleged that she had not received actual notice of a tax sale or of her right to redemption.


OVERVIEW: Iowa Code § 447.9 authorized the holder to serve the homeowner with a notice of redemption by both regular mail and certified mail to her last known address. The homeowner maintained this provision violated her due process rights under the Fourteenth Amendment and Iowa Const. art. I, §§ 1 and 9, because it did not require actual delivery of notice and was therefore unconstitutional. The summary judgment record in this case did not reveal a failure of notice. The holder simultaneously sent its notices by certified mail and by regular mail and there was no indication that the regularly mailed notice came back as undeliverable. Because the holder used two notification methods calculated to apprise the homeowner of her redemption rights and learned that only one of them failed, due process did not require it to take additional steps to notify the homeowner. Although Iowa Code § 447.9 also deemed notice effective upon mailing, the fact that two notices were required and were sent in this case, and the fact that the homeowner's property rights would not immediately have been affected, rendered this statutory scheme as applied to the facts of this case constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

437 of 583 DOCUMENTS


Nicholson v. HF05


No. 9-832 / 08-1418


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


778 N.W.2d 218; 2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 1994



December 17, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO IOWA RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Floyd County, Colleen D. Weiland, Judge. A one-time property owner appeals the district court's decision to grant a tax deed holder's motion for summary judgment, contending that the statute prescribing the method of notice to a property owner of his or her right to redeem the property is unconstitutional.
Nicholson v. Frank, 2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 1631 (Iowa Ct. App., Dec. 17, 2009)

 

438 of 583 DOCUMENTS


In the Interest of J.L.


No. 9-613 / 09-0945


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


779 N.W.2d 481; 2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 1571



November 25, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 11, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Woodbury County, Mary Jane Sokolovske, Judge. J.L., L.R., and S.G. appeal from the district court's ruling transferring jurisdiction to a tribal court.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a parental rights termination case, appellant minor children sought review of an order of the Iowa District Court for Woodbury County, which held that the children could not object to the transfer of jurisdiction to a tribal court pursuant to Iowa Code § 232B.5 (2009), a provision of the Iowa Indian Child Welfare Act (ICWA), Iowa Code § 232B.1 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The children argued that the transfer was not in their best interest and that the Iowa ICWA was unconstitutional. The trial court did not consider the merits of their objection and denied the children's motion to amend or enlarge, refusing to address their constitutional arguments. However, the children were parties to, and had a vital interest in, the transfer proceedings. Therefore, the children were entitled to a voice at every stage of the proceedings, but were denied an opportunity to be heard. By not including the children as parties able to make an objection, the Iowa ICWA violated their procedural due process rights. Therefore, § 232B.5(10), (13) was unconstitutional on procedural due process grounds. Further, a fundamental interest was implicated and § 232B.5 completely prohibited the children from asserting their rights, such as their preference to remain with siblings or their physical or psychological safety. The narrow definition of good cause prohibited the children from objecting to the motion based upon their best interests. Thus, § 232B.5(13) violated U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Iowa Const. art. I, § 9, on substantive due process grounds.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the matter for a hearing on the transfer motion, during which the children shall be allowed to object and the children shall be allowed to introduce evidence of their best interests.

City of Council Bluffs v. Harder


No. 9-680 / 08-1315


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 1455



November 12, 2009, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNTIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at City of Council Bluffs v. Harder, 777 N.W.2d 128, 2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 1914 (Iowa Ct. App., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Pottawattamie County, James M. Richardson, Judge. A property owner appeals the district court decision awarding title of her property to the City of Council Bluffs, contending the court erred in concluding she had abandoned her property.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee City of Council Bluffs filed a petition requesting a transfer of title to property owned by appellant homeowner to the City, alleging the property had been abandoned within the meaning of Iowa Code § 657A.10A (2007), and was a public nuisance. The Iowa District Court for Pottawattamie County awarded title of the property to the City, and the homeowner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The homeowner's house was rendered uninhabitable by fire. The homeowner claimed that she had been paying the property taxes and mortgage and that her failure to correct the situation was due to an ongoing dispute with her insurance company. The homeowner abandoned the property within the meaning of Iowa Code § 657A.10A (2007). The property was unoccupied for more than six months and, after the fire, the property did not meet housing code requirements for human habitation, Iowa Code § 657A.1(1) and Iowa Code § 657A.10A(3)(c), (d), and the utilities had been shut off shortly after the fire, § 657A.10A(3)(b). The condition of the house had deteriorated over the more than three years it remained unoccupied, § 657A.10A(3)(e), and was boarded up, § 657A.10A(3)(f), and no efforts had been made to rehabilitate it, § 657A.10(3)(g). The house sustained several break-ins, indicating that it posed a safety hazard to the neighborhood, § 657A.10A(3)(k). The same unsafe condition was present whether abandonment was the fault of the homeowner or her insurer, and other remedies existed under the law, including the tort of bad faith, for insurers that did not honor their claims-paying obligations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

440 of 583 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sanders


No. 9-597 / 08-1981


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 1396



October 7, 2009, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNTIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by Sanders v. State, 2014 Iowa App. LEXIS 62 (Iowa Ct. App., Jan. 9, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Webster County, Kurt L. Wilke, Judge. Ronnie Sanders appeals from his conviction and sentence for second-degree sexual abuse.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court for Webster County, Iowa, that convicted him of second-degree sexual abuse under Iowa Code § 709.3 (2007), arguing that the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction because the State did not prove he used or threatened to use force creating a substantial risk of death or serious injury to the victim.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court held that the evidence was sufficient to establish that defendant used force creating a substantial risk of death or serious injury to the victim and supported his conviction of second-degree sexual abuse where defendant choked his victim until she lost consciousness and raped her. The emergency room physician who treated the victim testified that, as a result of being choked, the victim had bruising on her neck and around her eyes, that the choking was severe enough to cause the blood vessels around her eyes to rupture and bleed underneath the skin, and that, in order to cause the injuries from choking, defendant had to have used a severe amount of force, which could have been life threatening. This evidence was sufficient to establish that the victim's injuries were caused by asphyxiation, or a lack of oxygen caused by the strangulation, and the evidence demonstrated that, when defendant strangled the victim so that she lost consciousness, he used force that created a substantial risk of serious injury or death.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

State v. Gear


No. 9-345 / 08-1620


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 1473



September 17, 2009, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNTIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Gear, 776 N.W.2d 301, 2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 1765 (Iowa Ct. App., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Poweshiek County, Michael R. Stewart, District Associate Judge. Appeal from the denial of a motion to dismiss, claiming the Iowa Code section 123.46(2) is unconstitutional.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's motion to dismiss the charge of public intoxication, on defendant's claim that the underlying statute, Iowa Code § 123.46(2) (2007), was unconstitutional, was denied by the Iowa District Court for Poweshiek County. The Iowa Supreme Court denied defendant's application for discretionary review. Following a trial to the district court on the minutes, defendant was convicted of public intoxication, second offense, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: A police officer observed defendant in a convenience store. Defendant admitted he was intoxicated and knew it was illegal, but refused to submit to sobriety testing, and the officer arrested him. Defendant alleged the statute, Iowa Code § 123.46(2), was unconstitutional. Even if one of the alternative means of violating § 123.46(2), simulating intoxication, could have been interpreted as restricting free speech as shown by actions, application of overbreadth principles would result only in partial invalidity of the statute. Defendant was convicted of actual intoxication in public. This fell within the statute's plainly legitimate sweep, and defendant's overbreadth argument was rejected. The statute provided sufficient guidance to law enforcement personnel so that they could understand what conduct was prohibited and it did not encourage arbitrary and discriminatory enforcement; therefore, the statute was not vague. Defendant summarily claimed his sentence was disproportionate to his crime; he failed to meet the threshold of gross disproportionality, particularly because he was not sentenced to any jail time and his fine was one-sixth of the maximum fine, plus surcharges and costs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

443 of 583 DOCUMENTS


Martin v. Crook


No. 9-491 / 08-1711


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 784



August 6, 2009, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNTIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Martin v. Crook, 776 N.W.2d 110, 2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 1741 (Iowa Ct. App., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Polk County, Donna L. Paulsen, Judge. Plaintiffs-appellants appeal from a jury verdict in favor of the defendants-appellees in a case involving a collision by the side of a highway.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, two parents and their three children, sought review of a decision of the Iowa District Court for Polk County, which, based on a jury verdict, entered judgment for appellees, a driver and a rental car company, in a suit alleging negligence for personal injuries sustained by the father when the rental car skidded on an icy highway and struck him, and for negligent infliction of emotional distress as to the rest of the family.


OVERVIEW: Icy patches intermittently covered the road on the day in question. Appellants had pulled off the road to help a stranded car. The other driver averred that he had adjusted his speed for the ice; that as he neared the stranded car, the cars ahead of him began sliding and zig-zagging; and that to avoid hitting them, he tapped his breaks and lost control of his car, which slid directly into the stranded car and the individuals standing nearby. In ordering a new trial, the court found that since the district court had eliminated the legal excuse defense from the case, there was no basis for the jury to have exonerated the driver from a finding of negligence. The district court also erred in not granting jury instructions on legal excuse and sudden emergency since it was for the jury to decide whether the driver's violation of the rules of the road was excused by the unforeseen circumstances of the ice and the vehicles in front of him. While only the mother's emotional distress claim should have been submitted to the jury, the court also found that the rental company should have been dismissed because the Graves Amendment, 49 U.S.C.S. § 30106, preempted state law in this matter.


OUTCOME: The court held that the rental company should have been dismissed from the case and reversed and remanded the case for a new trial on appellants' negligence claims against the driver.

State v. Russell


No. 9-440 / 08-1449


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 712



July 22, 2009, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNTIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Russell, 772 N.W.2d 270, 2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 1321 (Iowa Ct. App., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Lee (South) County, William L. Dowell, Judge. Charles Russell appeals from the special sentence imposed upon his convictions of third-degree sexual abuse and kidnapping.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty in the Iowa District Court for Lee (South) County to sexual abuse in the third degree, in violation of Iowa Code §§ 709.1(3) and 709.4(2)(b), and kidnapping in the third degree, in violation of Iowa Code §§ 710.1(3) and 710.4. The district court imposed consecutive sentences and imposed a special sentence pursuant to Iowa Code § 903B.1 (2007), requiring lifetime supervision. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that his trial counsel was ineffective in failing to assert that § 903B.1 violated the federal and state constitutional provisions regarding substantive due process, U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Iowa Const. art. I, § 9. He argued that the imposition of extended parole following incarceration under § 903B.1 infringed upon his fundamental rights to liberty, privacy, and freedom from governmental restraint. The court held that as a parolee, defendant had no fundamental liberty interest in freedom from extended supervision, and he had a limited expectation of privacy. Therefore, the court applied the rational basis test to determine whether § 903B.1 violated defendant's due process rights. Because there was a reasonable fit between the State's interest in protecting its citizens from sex crimes and the special sentence imposed by § 903B.1, that section was not unconstitutional. Defendant's counsel's assistance was not ineffective for failing to raise a meritless claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentence.

 

445 of 583 DOCUMENTS


State v. Harkins


No. 9-138 / 07-1561


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


786 N.W.2d 498; 2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 672



July 22, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Harkins, 772 N.W.2d 269, 2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 1258 (Iowa Ct. App., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Cedar County, J. Hobart Darbyshire, Judge. Harkins appeals his sentence for third-degree sexual abuse.
State v. Harkins, 734 N.W.2d 487, 2007 Iowa App. LEXIS 1641 (Iowa Ct. App., 2007)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Iowa District Court for Cedar County of third-degree sexual abuse in violation of Iowa Code § 709.4 (2005) and sentenced to ten years in prison and a special life sentence pursuant to Iowa Code § 903B.1 (Supp. 2005). He appealed, contending that § 903B.1 was unconstitutional and asserting an ineffective assistance of counsel claim.


OVERVIEW: Iowa Code § 903B.1 required that certain sex offenders be committed into the custody of the Iowa Department of Corrections for life. Defendant argued that § 903B.1 violates the separation of powers doctrine, the due process clause, and the equal protection clause. He also argued that the sentence constituted cruel and unusual punishment. The court held that a case decided after defendant's appeal controlled as to the equal protection and separation of powers claims, and thus, those claims failed. Defendant's procedural due process claim did not stem from the imposition of the § 903B.1 sentence. Rather, defendant claimed that if he violated the rules of parole and his release was revoked, the statute contemplated additional proceedings that were not specified. Because defendant had not violated any terms of his extended parole, this issue was not ripe for review. His substantive due process claim was rejected because the State had a rational interest in protecting its citizens from sex offenders. Section 903B.1 was not grossly disproportionate to the gravity of the offenses to which it applied, and its imposition did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

Doss v. State


No. 9-482 / 08-1512


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 681



July 22, 2009, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNTIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Doss v. State, 772 N.W.2d 270, 2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 1302 (Iowa Ct. App., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Warren County, Paul R. Huscher, Judge. Appeal from the district court's denial of postconviction relief.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Iowa District Court for Warren County denied defendant's application for postconviction relief. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended postconviction counsel was ineffective by not asserting that trial counsel was ineffective for failing to challenge the constitutionality of Iowa Code § 903B.1 (Supp. 2005). The appellate court concluded any issues raised in defendant's pro se brief were not preserved for appellate review, were waived for failure to cite authority, or were otherwise not properly before the appellate court. Under Iowa Code § 903B.1, defendant was not being punished for "crimes not committed" but rather for third-degree sexual abuse. His sentence had not been served; the special sentence was part of his sentence that he was currently serving. A challenge to the statute based on future parole violations was not ripe. Iowa Code § 903B.1 was not grossly disproportionate to the gravity of the offenses to which it applied and its imposition did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment. The registration requirement pursuant to Iowa Code § 692A.2(1) was not punishment. Because it was not punitive, its imposition together with the special sentence did not add to the punishment imposed. Trial counsel had no duty to raise constitutional challenges and defendant was not prejudiced.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

No. 9-339 / 08-1369


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 678



July 22, 2009, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNTIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at In re Young, 772 N.W.2d 269, 2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 1268 (Iowa Ct. App., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Black Hawk County, Jon Fister and Nathan Callahan, Judges. Young appeals the State's in rem forfeiture of his handgun.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State filed an in rem forfeiture complaint seeking forfeiture of a handgun. Appellant owner responded by filing a motion to dismiss. The Iowa District Court for Black Hawk County, denied the motion to dismiss and entered a forfeiture order in favor of the State. The owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The owner was arrested for weapons possession and operating while intoxicated, and his handgun was confiscated for evidence. The owner was convicted on both charges. The State filed an in rem forfeiture complaint seeking forfeiture of the handgun. The State did not utilize the notice of pending forfeiture administrative process, and the owner responded by filing a motion to dismiss. The trial court denied the owner's motion to dismiss, and gave the owner thirty days to file a claim for the property and answer to the State's complaint. After the owner failed to file either an answer or a claim as authorized by the trial court, the State applied for a forfeiture order, which was entered. The appellate court ruled that the owner's failure to move to set aside the default judgment did not constitute an appellate waiver. The default judgment was a final judgment, and all final judgments could be appealed. Also, the trial court's default judgment was proper. The owner had the benefit of the trial court's specific order allowing him thirty days to answer the State's in rem complaint, and he elected not to file an answer.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.
