State v. Jorgensen


No. 9-379 / 08-0916


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


785 N.W.2d 708; 2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 679



July 22, 2009, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNTIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Jorgensen, 772 N.W.2d 269, 2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 1273 (Iowa Ct. App., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Cerro Gordo County, Carlynn D. Grupp, District Associate Judge. The defendant appeals from the special sentence imposed pursuant to Iowa Code section 903B.2 (Supp. 2005) following his conviction for indecent exposure.
State v. Jorgensen, 758 N.W.2d 830, 2008 Iowa Sup. LEXIS 164 (Iowa, 2008)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Iowa District Court for Cerro Gordo County, which resentenced him to include a special 10-year sentence pursuant to Iowa Code § 903B.2 (Supp. 2005) after his probation for indecent exposure was revoked.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of indecent exposure. He received a one-year suspended sentence and was placed on probation for one year. His probation was later revoked and the original sentence was imposed. The trial court resentenced him to include a special 10-year sentence pursuant to § 903B.2. On appeal, the court found no violation of the prohibition against cruel and unusual punishment under either U.S. Const. amend. VIII or Iowa Const. art. I, § 17. Section 903B.2 was not grossly disproportionate to the acts of committing the crime of indecent exposure and subsequently violating parole terms. Further, given that there was a rational basis for the legislature's inclusion of indecent exposure within § 903B.2, the court was not at liberty to declare the classification unconstitutional. Section 903B.2 rationally advanced the State's objective in protecting its citizens from sex crimes. Thus, trial counsel was not ineffective in failing to raise the meritless claim that the statute violated defendant's right to equal protection of the law. Finally, § 903B.2 did not violate defendant's right to substantive due process under U.S. Const. amend. XIV or Iowa Const. art. I, § 9.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Jenkins


No. 9-415 / 08-0537


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 649



July 2, 2009, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNTIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Jenkins, 772 N.W.2d 268, 2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 1236 (Iowa Ct. App., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Webster County, Gary L. McMinimee, Judge. Jeremy Frank Jenkins appeals from the special sentence imposed upon his conviction of assault with intent to commit sexual abuse.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Iowa District Court for Webster County, which imposed a special sentence upon him pursuant to Iowa Code § 903B.2 (Supp. 2005) after he was convicted of assault with intent to commit sexual abuse.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his counsel was ineffective for failing to argue that imposition of the special sentences violated his constitutional rights of substantive due process under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Iowa Const. art I, § 9. On appeal, the court determined that the limited privacy and liberty interests as issue were entitled to only rational basis review. In addition, the court found that because there was a rational basis for a special sentence imposed pursuant to Iowa Code § 903B.2 (Supp. 2005), including that the State had a strong interest in protecting its citizens from sex crimes and the frightening and high risk of recidivism posed by sex offenders, there was no merit to defendant's claim that the provisions violated his substantive due process rights. There was a reasonable fit between the State's interest in protecting its citizens from sex crimes and the extended supervision required under § 903B.2. As a result, there was no merit to defendant's claim that his trial counsel was not ineffective in failing to raise such issue at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

452 of 583 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kingery


No. 9-429 / 08-1184


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


774 N.W.2d 309; 2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 654



July 2, 2009, Filed


NOTICE: Released for Publication September 25, 2009.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Kingery, 772 N.W.2d 269, 2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 1261 (Iowa Ct. App., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Linn County, Patrick R. Grady, Judge. Douglas Kingery appeals from the imposition of special sentences pursuant to Iowa Code sections 903B.1 and .2 (2007).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Iowa District Court for Linn County, which imposed special sentences upon defendant pursuant to Iowa Code §§ 903B.1 and 903B.2 (2007).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his counsel was ineffective for failing to argue that imposition of the special sentences violated his constitutional rights of equal protection and substantive due process. On appeal, the court found that as long as the classificatory scheme chosen by the Iowa Legislature rationally advanced a reasonable and identifiable governmental objective, it had to disregard the existence of other methods that the court perhaps would have preferred. The classification found in Iowa Code §§ 903B.1 and 903B.2 (2007) rationally advanced the State's objective in protecting its citizens from sex crimes. Accordingly there was no equal protection violation. Furthermore, because there was a rational basis for a special sentence imposed pursuant to §§ 903B.1 and 903B.2, including that the State had a strong interest in protecting its citizens from sex crimes and the frightening and high risk of recidivism posed by sex offenders, there was no merit to defendant's claim that the provisions violated his substantive due process rights. Accordingly, defendant's trial counsel was not ineffective in failing to raise such issues at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Laforge


No. 9-298 / 08-1660


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 594



June 17, 2009, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNTIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Laforge, 772 N.W.2d 15, 2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 1201 (Iowa Ct. App., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Polk County, Don C. Nickerson, Judge. The State appeals and the defendant cross-appeals from a district court ruling denying the defendant's motion to suppress evidence but granting her motion to dismiss the criminal charge against her.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Iowa District Court for Polk County granted defendant's motion to suppress evidence but granted her motion to dismiss the charge of homicide by vehicle under Iowa Code, § 707.6A(1) (2007). The State appealed, and defendant cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court held that blood test results obtained from a warrantless withdrawal of defendant's blood should have been suppressed because defendant was not under arrest at the time of the withdrawal, as required by Iowa Code § 321J.10A(1), even if there was probable cause. The record also did not support a warrantless search under the emergency provision of Iowa Code § 321J.10A(1)(c). The court also held that the destruction of the blood sample did not warrant dismissal. There was no Brady violation because the State's failure to inform the lab of defendant's request that the evidence be preserved appeared to be an oversight rather than intentional; the sample was then destroyed pursuant to the lab's usual procedure; and there was no evidence that the blood sample was exculpatory in any way. Further, given the State's lack of bad faith in destroying the blood sample, the district court erred in dismissing the criminal charges against defendant based on its conclusion that the destruction of the blood sample deprived defendant of a meaningful opportunity to present a complete defense.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the denial of defendant's motion to suppress the blood test results obtained from the warrantless withdrawal of her blood, affirmed the holding that defendant did not establish bad faith in the failure to preserve the blood sample, reversed the finding that the right to a fair trial was violated by the destruction of the blood sample, and reversed the dismissal of the criminal charge. The court remanded for further proceedings.

In re Cloyd


No. 9-305 / 08-1806


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 608



June 17, 2009, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNTIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at In re Marriage of Cloyd, 772 N.W.2d 16, 2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 1170 (Iowa Ct. App., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Story County, Timothy J. Finn, Judge. Jeffrey M. Cloyd appeals from the decree dissolving his marriage to Brenda M. Cloyd.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS MODIFIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The parties were divorced and the Iowa District Court for Story County awarded them joint legal custody of their children, with appellee mother having primary physical care, and divided the marital property. Appellant father was given visitation every other weekend, ordered him to pay child and medical support for the children, and denied him an alimony award. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the father contended the district court should have awarded the parties shared care of their two children; the district court did not use the proper incomes in computing child support; the medical support provision needed modification; the property division was not equitable; and he should have been awarded alimony. The appellate court agreed that the medical support provision needed supervision to comply with Iowa Ct. R. 9.12. However, the appellate court disagreed with the father on all remaining issues. The court's district's primary reason for its custody decision was that the parties had different attitudes towards discipline, and the mother more closely monitored the children's rules and enforced them. The appellate court found no basis to rely only on average past years' income to determine income for child support purposes because, in the current economy, the mother's past income would not continue in the future, and her ability to continue at past income levels was not likely. Thus, there was no basis to decrease the father's child support. Similarly, denial of alimony was proper as it was most likely that the mother's income would continue to decrease.


OUTCOME: The mother's medical support obligation was increased; as modified, the judgment was affirmed.

Hartsfield v. Iowa Dist. Court for Jones County


No. 9-220 / 08-0562


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 626



June 17, 2009, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNTIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Hartsfield v. Iowa Dist. Court for Jones County, 772 N.W.2d 15, 2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 1214 (Iowa Ct. App., 2009)
Related proceeding at State v. Hartsfield, 2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 1520 (Iowa Ct. App., Oct. 21, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Jones County, Nancy A. Baumgartner, Judge. A prisoner challenges an order finding him in contempt of court for refusing to submit to DNA sampling.



DISPOSITION: WRIT ANNULLED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate was convicted and sentenced for possession with intent to deliver, drug tax stamp, delivery of controlled substance, and conspiracy to commit a felony. When he refused to give a DNA sample for DNA profiling, defendant State filed a contempt action. Defendant Iowa District Court for Jones County found the inmate in contempt and ordered him imprisoned until he provided a DNA sample. The inmate petitioned for a writ of certiorari.


OVERVIEW: On review, the inmate contended Iowa Code ch. 81 did not apply to individuals like him who were convicted and sentenced before ch. 81 was enacted, and that even if ch. 81 did apply retroactively, the district court's order that he "shall be imprisoned until he provides a sample of his DNA" violated ex post facto laws. The inmate also argued that he should have been granted a jury trial. The appellate court disagreed, finding first that, by its terms, Iowa Code § 81.1 applied to any person against whom a judgment or conviction for a felony had been entered. The inmate was such a person. While the inmate's refusal to submit a DNA sample led to additional incarceration, it was the violation of the DNA profiling law which carried its own penalty that triggered that result. The effects of ch. 81 were not punitive to any significant extent. The initial burden, that of providing an oral swab, was de minimis; and the burden imposed on those who refused to meet that burden was the well-recognized sanction of contempt. Thus, ch. 81, as applied to the inmate, did not violate ex post facto laws. Finally, no jury trial was required as the contempt proceeding was civil in nature.


OUTCOME: The district court's order was upheld and the writ of certiorari was annulled.

2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 239

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNTIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Anderson v. City Dev. Bd. of State, 767 N.W.2d 420, 2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 860 (Iowa Ct. App., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Polk County, Michael D. Huppert (judicial review) and D.J. Stovall (motion to dismiss), Judges. John Anderson appeals from the ruling of the district court affirming a decision by the City Development Board approving an involuntary annexation and from the dismissal of his request for declaratory relief, which he had joined with his petition for judicial review.
Anderson v. City Dev. Bd., 2006 Iowa App. LEXIS 625 (Iowa Ct. App., June 28, 2006)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of an order from the Iowa District Court for Polk County, which awarded judgment to respondents, a city and a city development board (CDB), in an action challenging the involuntary annexation of land.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner brought an action against respondents, challenging the city's involuntary annexation of land. The trial court found that the petition for involuntary annexation was properly approved by the CDB. On appeal, the court found that the trial court's ruling was well reasoned and fully supported by the record. The city development committee did not err in concluding there was not a "substantial" amendment to the annexation that would trigger a continuance under Iowa Code § 368.18 (1997). The original petition filed in June 1998 involved the annexation of approximately 8,890 acres. The amended petition removed acres that had been voluntarily annexed between the original petition in 1998 and the 2005 hearing: the parties affected by the voluntary annexations were aware of those proceedings. No territory was added. The trial court did not err in dismissing petitioner's request for declaratory relief because the allegations of procedural irregularity in the special election approving the annexation proposal should have been made in a separate election contest under Iowa Code ch. 57 and 62.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff realtor sought review of an order from the Iowa District Court for Floyd County, which awarded partial summary judgment and judgment to defendant seller in an action to recover a commission.


OVERVIEW: The realtor brought an action against the seller of a sports bar to recover a real estate commission based on an alleged oral brokerage agreement. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 186



March 11, 2009, Filed

AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Schwebke v. State, 766 N.W.2d 648, 2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 821 (Iowa Ct. App., 2009)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Schwebke v. Fayram, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 46202 (N.D. Iowa, June 2, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Hardin County, Carl D. Baker, Judge. Kendon H. Schwebke appeals the district court's denial of his application for postconviction relief following his conviction for murder in the second degree.
State v. Schwebke, 690 N.W.2d 700, 2004 Iowa App. LEXIS 1680 (Iowa Ct. App., 2004)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Iowa District Court for Hardin County denied defendant's application for postconviction relief following his conviction for murder in the second degree under Iowa Code § 707.3 (2001). Defendant sought review.


OVERVIEW: The court held that trial counsel was not rendered ineffective by failing to object to the jury instructions for murder in the second degree, in part because there was sufficient evidence to support submission of the theory that defendant was the principal. The evidence included that defendant harbored a strong dislike for the victim, had threatened to shoot him, owned a.22 caliber semi-automatic rifle, which he took to the victim's residence, and entered the residence with another individual. The victim was killed by a.22 caliber bullet to the head. The court also held that the prosecutor did not commit prejudicial misconduct by characterizing defendant's conduct as callous, stating that defendant had the ability to stop the murder and did not, stating that defendant was deceitful and had lied, or using argument to personally vouch for State witnesses and express a personal opinion as to evidence and guilt. Therefore, counsel did not breach an essential duty by not objecting. Finally, appellate counsel was not rendered ineffective by failing to challenge on direct appeal the trial court's overruling of hearsay objections to admissible evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision denying defendant's postconviction application.

2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 167



March 11, 2009, Filed

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNTIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at S.O. v. Carlisle Sch. Dist., 766 N.W.2d 648, 2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 824 (Iowa Ct. App., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Warren County, Peter A. Keller, Judge. Plaintiffs appeal the district court's ruling granting defendants' motion for summary judgment on the ground that plaintiffs' action was barred by the statute of limitations.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents brought various tort claims against appellees, a school district, a teacher, and the school principal when it was discovered that one of their minor children had been sexually abused in school and that the alleged abuse had not been reported. Finding that the parents' action was barred by the statute of limitations, the Iowa District Court for Warren County granted the school's motion for summary judgment. The parents appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the parents raised several issues contending the district court erred in granting the school's motion for summary judgment. The appellate court found that the district court did not err in holding that the parents' claims premised upon the civil liability provisions of Iowa Code § 232.75(2) (2005) were subject to the provisions of Iowa Code ch. 670 as the teacher and the principal were acting within the scope of their employment when they allegedly failed to report the alleged abuse. Further, and the continuing tort doctrine did not apply to the teacher's and the principal's alleged failure to report because, even if the parents' injury was continuing in nature, there was only a single act of omission. However, the appellate court agreed with the parents that where no notice was given, Iowa Code § 670.5 (2005) violated the Iowa and United States equal protection clauses when read to omit the minor tolling provision of Iowa Code § 614.8(2); there was no rational basis justifying the classification resulting from claims filed by minors against a municipality and claims filed by minors against private tortfeasors. As such, the summary judgment should not have been granted.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Lee v. State


No. 8-821 / 07-1879


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 119



February 19, 2009, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNTIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Polk County, James Richardson, Judge. The State of Iowa appeals a judgment in favor of a terminated employee, maintaining that her lawsuit under the Family and Medical Leave Act was barred by the doctrine of sovereign immunity.
Lee v. State, 765 N.W.2d 607, 2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 735 (Iowa Ct. App., 2009)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the State of Iowa, appealed a judgment from the District Court for Polk County (Iowa), which, in a jury trial, ruled that sovereign immunity did not bar plaintiff employee's claims against the State under the Family and Medical Leave Act (FMLA) and made an award to the employee that included damages and interest.


OVERVIEW: The employee was terminated after notifying a public employer that she was receiving medical treatment. The district court found that Eleventh Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. XI, immunity did not bar the suit. The court stated that Congress unequivocally intended to abrogate Eleventh Amendment immunity as to the FMLA when it explicitly provided in 29 U.S.C.S. § 2617(a)(2) that employee lawsuits for money damages could be maintained against any employer, including a public agency. The court concluded that the FMLA's self-care provision, 29 U.S.C.S. § 2612(a)(1)(D), was a valid exercise of the constitutional power authorized by U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 5, and that immunity was therefore properly abrogated as to the self-care provision. The court noted that the legislative history indicated that Congress was attempting to alleviate the disparate impact of serious illness on women wage earners. Because the self-care provision was enacted to alleviate gender discrimination, a heightened standard of review applied. The State's actions in providing FMLA leave pursuant to Iowa Admin. Code r. 11-63.4 and informing employees of their FMLA rights amounted to a waiver of sovereign immunity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's judgment.

No. 8-884 / 08-0554


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 77



February 4, 2009, Filed

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Rojas v. Pine Ridge Farms, L.L.C., 764 N.W.2d 783, 2009 Iowa App. LEXIS 520 (Iowa Ct. App., 2009)

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Polk County, Douglas F. Staskal, Judge. Dependents of deceased employee separately appeal from a district court judicial review ruling affirming the appeal decision of the workers' compensation deputy commissioner.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED ON BOTH APPEALS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, surviving spouse and child and claimant and children, challenged the judgment of the Iowa District Court for Polk County, affirming the appeal decision of the workers' compensation deputy commissioner allocating workers' compensation survivors' benefits between the parties, in the action with appellees, employer and insurer.


OVERVIEW: The employee was born and raised in Mexico. The employee was married to the claimant and had five children. The employee travelled to the United States for work, and regularly sent the claimant money. While living and working in Iowa, the employee married the spouse, and had one child. The employee was killed in a accident while working, and the spouse and claimant each applied for survivors' benefits. The deputy commissioner allocated 50-percent of the death benefits to the spouse and twenty percent to her child. The remaining 30-percent was assigned equally to the claimant and her children, resulting in them actually receiving 15-percent due to the effect of Iowa Code § 85.31(5) (2005). The appellate court ruled that the deputy did not err in its equitable apportionment of survivors' benefits. The record showed that the employee contributed approximately 15-percent of his annual earnings to support the claimant and her children, which was the percentage of benefits her family would ultimately receive under the agency's allocation. Also, as nonresident aliens, the claimant and her children did not have standing to assert their constitutional challenges to Iowa Code § 85.31(5).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Meduna v. City of Crescent


No. 8-573 / 07-1919


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


761 N.W.2d 77; 2008 Iowa App. LEXIS 1265



December 17, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 2, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Pottawattamie County, James S. Heckerman, Judge. Plaintiffs appeal from the district court ruling finding the use of their home as a bed and breakfast was prohibited under a city zoning ordinance and ordering them to cease and desist operation of the business.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, claimants, challenged the judgment of the Iowa District Court for Pottawattamie County, finding that the use of their home as a bed and breakfast was prohibited under a zoning ordinance, and ordering them to cease and desist operation of the business, in the action with defendant city.


OVERVIEW: The claimants established a one-bedroom bed and breakfast in their single family residence believing under the city's zoning ordinances it was a small home occupation, a permitted use in a R-1 residential zone. The city disagreed and charged the claimants with violation of its zoning ordinance. The claimants sued seeking a declaratory judgment declaring their bed and breakfast a permitted use, and asked that a writ of mandamus issue compelling the city to cease interfering with the lawful use of their property. The claimants were found guilty of a municipal infraction and their request for relief was denied. The appellate court ruled that the claimants' one bedroom bed and breakfast was a permitted use under the R-1 zoning ordinance. It was the size of the occupation that defined what was permitted in R-1 districts. There was nothing in the ordinances to support a finding that a small home occupation was precluded from being classified as a small business because it was permitted in another zone. A one bedroom bed and breakfast was clearly the smallest of small, and the only conclusion the appellate court could reach was that it was a permitted use under the R-1 ordinance.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

In the Interst of A.P.


No. 8-629 / 08-0439


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2008 Iowa App. LEXIS 1266



December 17, 2008, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at In the Interst of A.P., 760 N.W.2d 210, 2008 Iowa App. LEXIS 1712 (Iowa Ct. App., 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Linn County, Susan Flaherty, Associate Juvenile Judge. A Native American tribe appeals from the juvenile court's denial of its motion to intervene in children in need of assistance proceedings.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Indian Tribe challenged the judgment of the Iowa District Court for Linn County, denying its motion to intervene in the children in need of assistance proceedings (CINA).


OVERVIEW: The mother was an enrolled member of the Tribe. It was undisputed that neither child was a member of the Tribe, nor were their fathers members of the Tribe. The State filed CINA proceedings as to the two children. The juvenile court denied the Tribe's motion to intervene in the CINA proceedings. The Tribe alleged that the children were Indian children within the meaning of Iowa's Indian Child Welfare Act (Iowa ICWA), Iowa Code chapter 232B (2007). The Tribe argued that Iowa Code § 232B.3(6) had not been declared unconstitutional on its face. The appellate court disagreed with Tribe's assertion. The appellate court ruled that it was proper form the juvenile court to deny the Tribe's motion to intervene. The Iowa ICWA's definition of "Indian child" found in Iowa Code § 232B.3(6) was unconstitutional because it included ethnic Indians who were not eligible for tribal membership. Consequently, the appellate court must apply the Federal definition of "Indian child" to determine whether the Federal or Iowa ICWA applied to the case. The children were not members of the Tribe. The children were not eligible for membership in the Tribe.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Hansen

COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2008 Iowa App. LEXIS 1251



December 17, 2008, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Scott County, Mark J. Smith (motion to suppress), Mary E. Howes (trial), Judges. Defendant appeals his conviction for failure to affix a drug tax stamp.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Iowa District Court for Scott County, convicting him of failure to affix a drug tax stamp.


OVERVIEW: The officers noticed cars were slowing down or stopping in front of them, and observed defendant standing in the middle of the four-lane road. Defendant was talking to a man on the sidewalk, and did not appear to be paying attention to the traffic problems he was creating. The officers believed defendant had committed disorderly conduct, in violation of Iowa Code § 723.4(7) (2007). The officers stopped defendant, who by then had reached the sidewalk, and arrested him. The officers performed a search incident to arrest, and found 79.2 grams of marijuana in defendant's pants pocket. There was no drug tax stamp on the marijuana. The appellate court ruled that there was probable cause to arrest defendant for violating Iowa Code § 723.4(7). The traffic was honking and stopping due to defendant in the middle of the road. Defendant was impeding the flow of traffic and the officers considered it to be a dangerous situation. The officers properly arrested defendant for disorderly conduct based on his actions in their presence, and the officers properly conducted a search incident to arrest.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Wiebbecke v. Benton County Bd. of Supervisors

COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2008 Iowa App. LEXIS 499



July 16, 2008, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Wiebbecke v. Benton County Bd. of Supervisors, 2008 Iowa App. LEXIS 1342 (Iowa Ct. App., July 16, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Benton County, Kristin L. Hibbs, Judge. The petitioner appeals from the district court's review upholding the Benton County Board of Adjustment's zoning decision.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner property owner sought review of an order from the Iowa District Court for Benton County, which dismissed his petition for a writ of certiorari and upheld the denial of a zoning variance by respondent county board of adjustment.


OVERVIEW: Prior to purchasing his agricultural land, the owner did not consult an attorney, review the abstract, or obtain a title opinion to determine if any use restrictions were applicable. The owner intended to build a large metal pole building, in which he would reside, store his personal belongings, and work on old cars. He later discovered that the land he purchased was within the county's agricultural land use district. The county board of adjustment denied the owner's application for a variance. The trial court dismissed the owner's petition for a writ of certiorari and upheld the denial of a variance. On appeal, the court found that the board made sufficient factual findings. Although written findings were not made, the board's reasoning and conclusions were included in the reported and transcribed hearing, thus facilitating review of the board's action. The county agricultural land preservation ordinance was in effect at the time the owner purchased the land. He did not acquire a use contrary to the existing agricultural classification. Accordingly, the court found no merit to the owner's claim that the ordinance was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Harrod v. City of Council Bluffs


No. 8-156 / 07-0864


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2008 Iowa App. LEXIS 328



May 29, 2008, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Harrod v. City of Council Bluffs, 753 N.W.2d 18, 2008 Iowa App. LEXIS 621 (Iowa Ct. App., May 29, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Pottawattamie County, James S. Heckerman, Judge. Appeal from the district court's grant of summary judgment in favor of defendant based on immunity.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff carjacking victim brought an action against defendant city in the Iowa District Court for Pottawattamie County, contending he was injured as a result of city police officers' negligence. The district court granted the city's motion for summary judgment after making a finding the officers were making an emergency response and entitled to immunity under Iowa Code § 670.4(11) (2005). The victim appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victim, his girlfriend, and a friend were carjacked by a man with a gun. The victim drove to his girlfriend's parents' house to get money for the carjacker. Once in the house, the girlfriend called 911 and stated that the carjacker had a gun and that her boyfriend was in the car. Police arrived. The victim got the gun away from the carjacker and shot him in the head. The officers commanded him to put hands up and drop it. The officers then fired their guns nearly 20 times. The victim, still in the car, was seriously injured by the shots. The court held that Iowa Code § 670.04(11) (2005) was unambiguous, providing no basis to explore its legislative history. Because the victim's claim was based upon an act or omission in connection with an emergency response by officers carrying out their official duties, the officers were entitled to immunity under the statute. There was no evidence that the officers intended to harm the victim, and there was no opportunity for deliberation. Therefore, the officers' conduct did not shock the conscience sufficiently to support a claim under U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to the city.

In re Det. of Meyers

COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2008 Iowa App. LEXIS 268



Filed May 14, 2008, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at In re Detention of Meyers, 752 N.W.2d 453, 2008 Iowa App. LEXIS 804 (Iowa Ct. App., May 14, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Winnebago County, Bryan H. McKinley, Judge. The respondent appeals from the district court's order committing him as a sexually violent predator.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient was diagnosed with antisocial personality disorder and had a long history of sexual assault. Near his release date, appellee State filed a petition under Iowa Code ch. 229A to have him committed as a sexually violent predator. The Iowa District Court for Winnebago County declared the patient to be a sexually violent predator and committed him to the care of the Iowa Department of Human Services. The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the patient contended, inter alia, that the State failed to prove whether he was both dangerous and possessed a mental abnormality that made him likely to engage in sexually violent predatory acts at the time of commitment and that the trial court erred in admitting irrelevant and unfairly prejudicial evidence by way of expert testimony and actuarial risk assessment as to his projected risk to reoffend 5, 10, and 15 years into the future. The appellate court disagreed, holding first that the district court did not err in overruling the patient's request for a directed verdict as there was no temporal element required under Iowa Code ch. 229A. Further, the risk assessments in question were relevant to the essential question of whether the patient was more likely than not to commit a sexually violent offense if he was not confined in a secured facility. The appellate court found that the actuarial instruments, while measuring future reconviction rates, assisted in understanding this essential question. These assessments were part of a larger clinical analysis that took into account a variety of other factors. Thus, admission of this evidence was proper.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Pierce


No. 8-105 / 07-0496


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2008 Iowa App. LEXIS 272



May 14, 2008, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Pierce, 752 N.W.2d 452, 2008 Iowa App. LEXIS 777 (Iowa Ct. App., May 14, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Dallas County, Gregory A. Hulse, Judge. A defendant appeals from the district court's denial of his application to discharge probation.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant served his sentences for third-degree burglary, assault with intent to commit sexual abuse, false imprisonment, and fourth-degree criminal mischief, he sought to discharge his probation or modify the conditions. The Iowa District Court for Dallas County denied defendant's request, finding that the purposes of probation had not yet been fulfilled. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant raised several issues challenging the district court's denial of his application to discharge or modify the conditions of his probation, including the requirement that he participate in a sexual offender treatment program. The appellate court found that although the district court discussed much of the information defendant presented in his application, nothing in its ruling changed the burden of proof, as he contended. As the current burglary conviction for which he was on probation arose from the same incident in which he was convicted for assault with intent to commit sexual abuse, there was a reasonable relationship between defendant's required participation in the sex offender treatment program and the statutory purposes of probation for his burglary conviction. Although he had previously successfully completed a relatively short probationary period, he subsequently committed more criminal offenses, including with the same type of assaultive conduct, which resulted in his incarceration and current probation. Thus, not enough time had passed to determine whether rehabilitation efforts had been successful.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Johnson County, Stephen C. Gerard, II (motion to suppress) and Mitchell E. Turner (trial), Judges. Defendant appeals from his conviction of operating while intoxicated.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Iowa District Court for Johnson County (Iowa) denying his motion to dismiss the results of a breath test and convicting him for operating while intoxicated, second offense, in violation of Iowa Code Ann. § 321J.2 (2003 Supp.).


OVERVIEW: An officer stopped defendant's vehicle after he drove through a red light. Results of field sobriety tests and two preliminary breath tests indicated that defendant was intoxicated. After his arrest, defendant supplied a breath sample to be analyzed by a DataMaster cdm testing device. On appeal, defendant argued that the district court erred in admitting the breath test results taken with the DataMaster device because the State failed to lay an adequate foundation. Defendant also argued that the district court erred in permitting expert testimony of a criminalist concerning the formulas used in obtaining a breath test result. Defendant was not prejudiced by the expert testimony, which was admissible under Iowa R. Evid. 5.702, 5.703, 5.704. The jury instructions, viewed as a whole, were not prejudicial and did not unduly emphasize the need to reach a verdict unanimously.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court.

 

473 of 583 DOCUMENTS


Taylor v. State


No. 8-017 / 07-0626


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


752 N.W.2d 24; 2008 Iowa App. LEXIS 102



February 13, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Polk County, Glenn E. Pille, Judge. Applicant appeals contending the department of corrections retrospectively applied changes in parole procedures that violate the ex post facto clauses of the federal and state constitutions.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was given 25-year and 5-year sentences for second-degree sexual abuse and engaging in lascivious acts with a child, to run consecutively. He sought postconviction relief on grounds that a statutory amendment regarding parole board procedures constituted ex post facto violations. The Iowa District Court for Polk County denied the application, and appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: On review, appellant challenged the dismissal of his petition, arguing that the department of corrections retroactively applied changes in parole review procedures contained in Iowa Code § 906.5 (1995) constituted ex post facto violations. The appellate court disagreed, finding first that the amendment to the statute did not extend the length of incarceration on its face. Further, appellant failed to prove that the change in law from conducting yearly personal interviews to only reviewing an inmate's case file each year produced a serious risk of increasing the measure of punishment attached to an inmate's crime. This lack of proof, coupled with the parole board's discretion to grant interviews in any given case, made appellant's ex post facto claim speculative. As such, the appellate court found no violation of the federal or state constitutional ex post facto prohibitions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Cowles


No. 7-827 / 06-1461


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2008 Iowa App. LEXIS 13



January 16, 2008, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Cowles, 746 N.W.2d 278, 2008 Iowa App. LEXIS 1734 (Iowa Ct. App., 2008)
Vacated by, Remanded by State v. Cowles, 757 N.W.2d 614, 2008 Iowa Sup. LEXIS 130 (Iowa, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Davis County, Daniel P. Wilson, Judge. The State seeks discretionary review of the district court's correction of an illegal sentence.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to second-degree sexual abuse for acts committed with his preteen daughter between April 9, 1996, and February 2, 1997. The Iowa District Court for Davis County sentenced defendant, citing Iowa Code § 902.12 (2003). Defendant applied for correction of illegal sentence. The district court corrected its prior sentencing order to delete the reference to § 902.12. The State sought and obtained discretionary review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted that Iowa Code § 902.12 (2003) as applied to him violated the Ex Post Facto Clauses of the federal and state constitutions, under U.S. Const. art I, § 10 and Iowa Const. art. I, § 21. The State argued that defendant failed to preserve error on his challenge to the sentence. The court disagreed because defendant unequivocally asserted that the sentence imposed on him was not authorized by the statutes in effect at the time the abuse began. The sex acts to which defendant pled guilty began before July 1, 1996. Therefore, there was a period of time from April 9, 1996, to June 30, 1996, before which Iowa Code § 902.12 (2003) became effective. The district court concluded that, under the circumstances, it had to presume that the entry of judgment may have been based on pre-July 1, 1996, acts. Since § 902.12 did not take effect until July 1, 1996, application of the statute to defendant was unconstitutional, and therefore, illegal. The court discerned no error in the district court's reasoning.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

2008 Iowa App. LEXIS 23

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Feregrino, 746 N.W.2d 278, 2008 Iowa App. LEXIS 1744 (Iowa Ct. App., 2008)
Vacated by State v. Feregrino, 756 N.W.2d 700, 2008 Iowa Sup. LEXIS 137 (Iowa, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Pottawattamie County, Gary K. Anderson, Judge. John Feregrino, Jr. appeals his conviction, following a trial to the court, for operating while intoxicated (OWI), first offense.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted, before the Iowa District Court for Pottawattamie County, of operating while intoxicated (OWI), first offense. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A police officer was on duty and heard loud music coming from a vehicle. The music could be heard from one hundred feet or more away. The officer stopped the vehicle for being in violation of a city ordinance. After stopping the vehicle, an officer detected a strong odor of alcoholic beverage on defendant's breath. When asked if he had been drinking, defendant responded, "not a whole lot." Defendant failed field sobriety tests. On appeal, defendant contended the district court erred in denying his motion to suppress and that his trial counsel was ineffective for failing to assure his waiver of jury trial was knowing, voluntary, and intelligent. Defendant maintained that the city ordinance with respect to noise was void for vagueness; however, a plain reading of the ordinance defined the offense with sufficient definiteness such that an ordinary person could easily understand what conduct was prohibited. As to whether trial counsel was effective, counsel failed to ensure substantial compliance with the requirements of Idaho R. Crim. P. 2.17(1) because counsel failed to ensure that defendant's waive of a jury trial was voluntary and intelligent. Prejudice was presumed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed as to the denial of the motion to suppress, but the conviction was reversed, and the matter was remanded for a trial to a jury, unless defendant voluntarily and intelligently waived his right to a trial by jury.

State v. Tovar


No. 7-903 / 07-0258


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2007 Iowa App. LEXIS 1337



December 28, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Tovar, 745 N.W.2d 96, 2007 Iowa App. LEXIS 1976 (Iowa Ct. App., Dec. 28, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Black Hawk County, James C. Bauch, Judge. Mark Randall Tovar appeals the lifetime parole provision of his sentence for sexual abuse in the third degree.



DISPOSITION: RESENTENCE VACATED AND REMANDED FOR REINSTATEMENT OF ORIGINAL SENTENCE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of sexual abuse in the third degree, and sentenced to a period not to exceed ten years. The State filed a motion for resentencing. The Iowa District Court for Black Hawk County resentenced defendant to add a lifetime parole provision in accordance with Iowa Code § 903B.1 (Supp. 2005). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: In August 2006, defendant pled guilty to one count of third-degree sexual abuse and one count of lascivious acts with a child. The amended trial information alleged that the acts occurred between June 1, 2005, and August 27, 2005. The charges were brought after defendant's girlfriend reported to the police that she believed defendant had sexually assaulted her seven-year-old daughter. Defendant argued that resentencing him to lifetime parole under Iowa Code § 903B.1 (Supp. 2005) was an illegal sentence. The appellate court ruled that the mandatory sentencing enhancement required by Iowa Code § 903B.1 could not legally be imposed upon defendant. The imposition of mandatory lifetime parole was not effective until July 1, 2005, and it could not be used as a sentence for criminal acts committed before July 1, 2005. It was neither proven that defendant committed the act after July 1, 2005, nor did he specifically plead guilty to committing the act after July 1, 2005. For acts committed before July 1, 2005, imposition of lifetime parole was discretionary under Iowa Code § 903B.1(3) (2005).


OUTCOME: The resentence was vacated and remanded for reinstatement of the original sentence.

In the Interest of C.J.D.


No. 7-717 / 07-0766


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2007 Iowa App. LEXIS 1309



December 12, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at In the Interest of C.J.D., 743 N.W.2d 872, 2007 Iowa App. LEXIS 2028 (Iowa Ct. App., Dec. 12, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Pottawattamie County, Gary Anderson, District Associate Judge. A father appeals the termination of his parental rights to his children.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father appealed from the District Court for Pottawattamie County (Iowa) the termination of his parental rights, claiming that the trial court erred in finding clear and convincing evidence that he failed to support his children without good cause according to Iowa Code § 600A.8(4) (2005) and in finding that termination was in the best interests of the children. He made additional constitutional claims.


OVERVIEW: After going to prison for using a minor to engage in sexually explicit conduct, the father failed to pay child support; however, his actions did not manifest indifference to his children. He attempted to maintain a relationship with his daughters by calling them twice every month and sending letters and small gifts to them on a weekly basis. He only earned $ 17 per month in prison, $ 14 of which he used to pay for phone calls and letters to the children. Good cause existed for his failure to contribute to the children's support. Therefore, the evidence was inadequate to terminate his parental rights under § 600A.8(4). Although it was specific to the case as it was passed due to the lobbying efforts of the maternal grandmother, § 600A.8(10) was inapplicable to the father as there was no express language that it was to be applied retroactively. Although it may have been in the best interests of the children for their father's parental rights to have been terminated, any such analysis was not reached because no grounds for termination were established by clear and convincing evidence. The children would be adequately protected under the divorce court's orders.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Jordan, 743 N.W.2d 872, 2007 Iowa App. LEXIS 2030 (Iowa Ct. App., Dec. 12, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Jasper County, Paul R. Huscher, Judge. Tyron Jordan appeals from his conviction for neglect of a dependent person.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Iowa District Court for Jasper County in which he was convicted of neglect of a dependent person in violation of Iowa Code § 726.3 (2005).


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that there was insufficient evidence to support his conviction and that his trial counsel was ineffective for failing to request and object to certain jury instructions and failing to challenge § 726.3 as unconstitutional. The evidence showed that defendant's 18-month-old son suffered severe burns while in defendant's care. Defendant initially claimed that while he was running a bath for his son, the water temperature suddenly surged, causing the burns. He subsequently claimed that he had instructed his four-year-old stepdaughter to run a bath for his son and that she ran the water too hot. Witnesses for the State testified that it was unlikely that the son's injuries could have occurred from the situations described by defendant. Affirming, the court held that the jury was entitled to credit the State's witnesses over defendant's testimony and that even if the jury had believed defendant, it could have found him reckless in asking a four-year-old child to run a bath for his son. The court preserved for postconviction review the claim of ineffectiveness with regard to the jury instructions and overruled the claim with regard to the constitutionality of § 726.3.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment but preserved the ineffectiveness claim with regard to jury instructions for postconviction review.

Faught v. Clear Lake Sanitary Dist.


No. 7-590 / 06-1389


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2007 Iowa App. LEXIS 1253



November 29, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Cerro Gordo County, Paul W. Riffel, Judge. Property owners appeal from a district court summary judgment ruling dismissing their appeal from resolutions passed by the board of trustees of a sanitary district annexing their property into the sanitary district and ordering them to connect to the district's sewer system.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners appealed a summary judgment ruling of the Iowa District Court for Cerro Gordo County dismissing their appeal from resolutions passed by the board of trustees of defendant sanitary district annexing a portion of their real estate into the sanitary district pursuant to Iowa Code § 358.16 and ordering the owners to connect to the district's sewer system.


OVERVIEW: The owners argued that § 358.16 violated the due process clauses of the United States and Iowa Constitutions because it allowed annexation of property without notice. The court concluded that the statute did not require the district to provide notice to property owners affected by the annexation prior to annexation. The annexation procedure set forth in § 358.16 did not violate the owners' due process rights. The district, as owner of 25 percent of the property to be benefitted by the annexation, was allowed by statute to petition for annexation. Section 358.16 made no distinction between public and private owners of land. The statute allowed the district to require the owners to connect to the district's sewer system upon annexation of their property. Although the county board of health issued a permit to the owners for an on-site waste water treatment system, the board specifically stated it had no intent to affect the ability of the district to compel connection to the sewage treatment system. The county board of health was divested of its jurisdiction after the owners' property was annexed by the district.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

In the Interest of K.C.


No. 7-799 / 07-1473


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2007 Iowa App. LEXIS 1179



November 15, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at In the Interest of K.C., 743 N.W.2d 871, 2007 Iowa App. LEXIS 1951 (Iowa Ct. App., Nov. 15, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Linn County, Barbara Liesveld, District Associate Judge. A mother appeals the juvenile court order modifying custody of her children.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought to have children temporarily removed from appellant mother's custody. The Iowa District Court for Linn County granted an ex parte removal order. Following a hearing held within 20 days of the order, the juvenile court modified a prior dispositional order that had authorized placement of the children with the mother. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother contended that: (1) she was denied due process by having her children removed from her custody ex parte without a subsequent removal hearing within 10 days pursuant to Iowa Code § 232.78, and (2) the juvenile court erred in ordering a modification on less than clear and convincing evidence of changed circumstances. The appellate court held that Iowa's statutory scheme for protecting the rights of natural parents in termination proceedings was constitutional, and that it was implicit in the power of the juvenile court in monitoring its prior child-in-need-of assistance (CINA) orders to temporarily, even summarily, remove a child pending a hearing on the modification. In other words, Iowa Code § 232.78 did not provide the only authorization for summary removal when a child was already under the jurisdiction of the juvenile court under a CINA order. Also, there was clear and convincing evidence to support the district court's finding of a change of circumstances warranting modification because the mother admitted to smoking marijuana or consuming alcohol on several recent occasions and she could not explain a number of "misoccurred" alcohol tests.


OUTCOME: The juvenile court's order was affirmed.

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Welded Constr. v. Finnerty, 743 N.W.2d 870, 2007 Iowa App. LEXIS 1907 (Iowa Ct. App., Nov. 15, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Polk County, Glenn E. Pille, Judge. Employer and workers' compensation insurance carrier appeal a district court judicial review decision affirming an award of workers' compensation benefits.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, an employer and its insurer, challenged a judgment of the Iowa District Court for Polk County affirming an award of workers' compensation benefits to appellee employee.


OVERVIEW: The employee, a fuel truck operator, injured his right shoulder when he slipped and fell from an excavator. On appeal, the court affirmed the commissioner's award of benefits under Iowa Code § 85.36 because: (1) the commissioner properly based the employee's compensation rate on a 60-hour work week because the employee testified that he worked 60 hours a week at a minimum and that one week he worked 110 hours; and (2) the court rejected the argument that a layoff of an indefinite length projected to occur at some unknown time in the future required a different calculation than the one based on 13 weeks of preinjury actual earnings. The commissioner did not err by concluding that the employee had reached maximum medical improvement (MMI) under Iowa Code § 85.34(1) on August 28, 2001 because two treating physicians specifically found that he had reached MMI on that date and continued him on indefinite restrictions. Substantial evidence also supported the agency's determination that the employee was not able to return to work in May 2001 due to his restrictions. The agency's award of penalty benefits under Iowa Code § 86.13 was also affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Carlisle v. City of Shannon City


No. 7-571 / 05-2036


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2007 Iowa App. LEXIS 1132



October 24, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Carlisle v. City of Shannon City, 742 N.W.2d 605, 2007 Iowa App. LEXIS 1882 (Iowa Ct. App., Oct. 24, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Ringgold County, Martha Mertz, Judge. David Carlisle appeals from denial of his petition for injunctive relief.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner appealed a judgment of the Iowa District Court for Ringgold County, which denied his petition for an injunction that would have prohibited defendant city from enforcing provisions of municipal ordinances that required mandatory hookup to the city wastewater treatment facilities.


OVERVIEW: The owner argued that he was not subject to the jurisdiction of the city's mandatory connection ordinance, that the franchise and mandatory connection ordinances did not apply to him, and that the ordinances were not authorized by statute. The court found no merit to any of these arguments. With respect to the owner's argument that the ordinances were an unconstitutional exercise of municipal power, the court concluded that the restraints imposed on the owner did not unconstitutionally deprive him of valuable property interests. The owner would receive a new on-site system for little or no initial cost, and the monthly charge to utilize the system was reasonable. The owner would still have the use and enjoyment of his property, limited only by the existing need to comply with applicable laws and regulations. The requirement that the owner allow a rural water district to come onto his property was not a taking within the meaning of the Iowa or United States Constitutions. Mandatory compliance with the city's sewer ordinances was a reasonable means by which to protect the health of the community.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Scott v. State


No. 7-697 / 06-2084


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2007 Iowa App. LEXIS 1157



October 24, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Scott v. State, 742 N.W.2d 606, 2007 Iowa App. LEXIS 2056 (Iowa Ct. App., Oct. 24, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Black Hawk County, Bruce B. Zager, Judge. Defendant appeals from the district court order denying his application for postconviction relief.
Scott v. State, 1998 Iowa App. LEXIS 124 (Iowa Ct. App., Dec. 28, 1998)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant applicant appealed an order of the Iowa District Court for Black Hawk County denying his application for postconviction relief (PCR).


OVERVIEW: In 2006, the Iowa Supreme Court issued its decision in the case of State v. Heemstra. That case significantly altered the existing felony-murder rule. The Iowa Supreme Court made the new felony-murder rule applicable to all prospective cases and all cases pending on direct appeal, but specifically chose not to make the modification retroactive. The applicant filed his pro se PCR application on September 8, 2006. The applicant claimed the PCR court should reverse his first-degree murder conviction because the original trial court's jury instructions were improper in light of the Heemstra decision. The applicant also claimed the Iowa Supreme Court's decision not to make Heemstra retroactive violated his constitutional rights. The instant court concluded that the Iowa Supreme Court's decision not to make the Heemstra rule retroactive fell within the general rule that state courts have the authority to determine the retroactivity of their own decisions. The instant court found no merit to the applicant's claim that his PCR counsel was ineffective because she did not find more issues to challenge beyond those raised in the current PCR petition.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Polk County, Karla J. Fultz, Associate Juvenile Judge. D.L.N. appeals the juvenile court's order requiring him to register with the sex offender registry.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile challenged the order of the Iowa District Court for Polk County requiring him to register with the sex offender registry.


OVERVIEW: In November 2003, appellant was alleged to have committed the delinquent act of sexual abuse in the second degree in violation of Iowa Code §§ 709.1(3) and 709.3(2). Moyer v. State

COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2007 Iowa App. LEXIS 1059



October 12, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Moyer v. State, 2007 Iowa App. LEXIS 1901 (Iowa Ct. App., Oct. 12, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Fremont County, James Heckerman, Judge. Applicant appeals from the district court's dismissal of his postconviction relief claims.
State v. Moyer, 695 N.W.2d 334, 2004 Iowa App. LEXIS 1872 (Iowa Ct. App., 2004)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged a judgment of the Iowa District Court for Fremont County denying his petition for postconviction relief from his convictions of conspiracy to manufacture a controlled substance, possession with intent to deliver five grams or less of methamphetamine, and four counts of possession of methamphetamine precursors.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court held that defense counsel was not ineffective for failing to object to the amendment of the information against the inmate because in a drug trafficking case, a conspiracy charge amendment effectively added a new means of committing the same offense and was permissible. Counsel was not ineffective for failing to challenge the addition of witnesses in the amendment because he received notice of the amendment 11 days before trial, which gave him ample time to adequately prepare a defense in response to the amendment. Counsel testified that he discussed the option of seeking a continuance with the inmate and that he rejected the option. Counsel was not ineffective for failing to challenge the initial seizure of defendant as illegal because the officer had reasonable cause to make an investigatory stop, as viewing a stopped car in the country at two a.m. gave the officer reasonable cause to believe a driver may have needed assistance. Seeing a group of persons using the inmate's property also supported a reasonable suspicion of trespass.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying the inmate postconviction relief was affirmed.

State v. Hall


No. 7-558 / 07-0354


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


740 N.W.2d 200; 2007 Iowa App. LEXIS 939



September 6, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 18, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Polk County, Odell McGhee, Judge. Raymond Hall appeals the portion of his sentence for sexual exploitation of a minor that imposes a no-contact order.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Iowa District Court for Polk County he pled guilty to one count of sexual exploitation of a minor, and the other four sexual exploitation of a minor counts were dismissed. The district court accepted defendant's guilty plea and placed him on probation for two years. As part of its sentencing order, the a no-contact order was entered. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the district court erred in imposing a no-contact order pursuant to Iowa Code § 901.5(7A) as part of his sentence because the order was not authorized by statute. The appellate court found that because defendant claimed the no-contact order was not authorized by statute, his failure to raise the issue of sentencing error at the time of sentencing did not constitute a waiver of his right to raise the issue on appeal. The appellate court agreed with the State that the district court was authorized under Iowa Code § 907.6 to define reasonable probation conditions; however, § 907.6 did not authorize creation of a condition of probation that could result in criminal prosecution under Iowa Code § 664A.2 (Supp. 2005) as § 664A.2 did not list Iowa Code § 728.12(3) as a triggering offense. Therefore, the no-contact order was not authorized pursuant to Iowa Code § 664A.2 or Iowa Code § 907.6. And although the trial court had justification to impose a condition of probation that restricted defendant from engaging in most communication with minors, there was no justification for forbidding him from incidental communication with minors.


OUTCOME: That portion of the sentence containing the imposition of a no-contact order under Iowa Code ch. 664A was reversed, and the case was remanded to the district court for entry of the restrictions on communication and contact with minors as conditions of probation and for clarification of the restriction on communication with minors.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Wayne County, David L. Christensen, Judge. Paul Ray Anderson Jr. appeals the district court's order for reimbursement of the cost of his legal assistance.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The jury found defendant not guilty on October 31, 2005. On November 22, 2005, the Iowa District Court for Wayne County ordered him to reimburse the State for the total costs of his legal assistance pursuant to Iowa Code § 815.9. The district court dismissed a constitutional challenge and ordered a payment plan of $35 per month. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The jury found defendant not guilty on October 31, 2005. On November 22, 2005, the court ordered him to reimburse the State for the total costs of his legal assistance pursuant to Iowa Code § 815.9. Defense counsel filed a motion challenging the constitutionality of § 815.9. Regarding the constitutionality of § 815.9, the Court of Appeals of Iowa held that the instant case was similar case to State v. Dudley. The issues in the instant appeal were fully discussed and decided in Dudley. The court found the reasoning in Dudley persuasive and the authority cited in the case controlling. Therefore, the court of appeals refused to address the same issues in the instant case.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

489 of 583 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dudley


No. 7-129 / 06-0049


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2007 Iowa App. LEXIS 757



Filed June 27, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Dudley, 2007 Iowa App. LEXIS 1530 (Iowa Ct. App., June 27, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Wayne County, David L. Christensen, Judge. Acquitted indigent defendant appeals from a district court order requiring him to reimburse the State of Iowa for the total cost of legal assistance provided to him.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Iowa District Court for Wayne County ordered defendant to reimburse the State for the total cost of his legal assistance pursuant to Iowa Code § 815.9 (2005), after he was acquitted of criminal charges. Defendant challenged the constitutionality of § 815.9 and, in the alternative, requested a payment plan. The district court overruled the constitutional challenges to the statute and entered a payment plan order. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that § 815.9 unconstitutionally violated his constitutional rights to equal protection and due process, and that his counsel in § 815.9 proceedings was ineffective. The statute did not violate equal protection because it did not eliminate any of the exemptions available to civil debtors. The provision for the repayment of costs and fees in reasonable installments if reimbursement was not timely made required the district court to consider defendant's reasonable ability to pay. Furthermore, defendant was not required to reimburse the State for costs that were assessed to a convicted indigent defendant. Thus, § 815.9 provided protections that were not afforded to other judgment debtors or to convicted indigent defendants. Section 815.9 survived defendant's procedural due process attack because defendant was afforded a hearing and he was provided with adequate notice of his responsibility to reimburse the State for his court-appointed attorney fees. Defendant's claims of ineffective assistance of counsel were without merit because, as an acquitted indigent defendant, he was not constitutionally or statutorily entitled to court-appointed counsel in § 815.9 proceedings.


OUTCOME: The district court's judgment was affirmed.

COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2007 Iowa App. LEXIS 601
