SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Richards v. Xenia Rural Water Dist., 2007 Iowa App. LEXIS 1503 (Iowa Ct. App., May 23, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Hamilton County, David R. Danilson, Judge. Plaintiff appeals the district court's grant of summary judgment to defendant in condemnation proceedings.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner appealed a decision of the Iowa District Court for Hamilton County, which granted a motion to dismiss and summary judgment to defendant water district for various claims in the owner's pro se action to void the district's application under Iowa Code §§ 6B.3, 6B.4 for condemnation or to quiet title for an easement claimed by the district to install and maintain a water pipeline across the owner's property.


OVERVIEW: The owner claimed that an easement was not necessary and that the district had not complied with the requirements of Iowa Code § 6B.3(a)(b) by showing the location of the right-of-way sought to be condemned, and failed to provide notice under Iowa Code § 6B.2A(2). On review, the court affirmed the decisions. The district court properly dismissed under Iowa R. Civ. P. 1.421(1)(f) the owner's due process claim because a pre-determination hearing was not required and the owner took substantial steps to alert the district court of his objections and resistance to the condemnation. It was not improper to deny the owner's motion to amend to include a claim that the description of the easement was nonsensical because on its face the claim appeared legally ineffectual. The district was entitled to summary judgment on the issue as to whether the condemnation was necessary under Iowa Code § 6A.1 because it presented evidence to show that the site selected for the pipeline was reasonable, which was all that was required. Because the owner's affidavits and response were untimely under Iowa R. Civ. P. 1.981(3), he presented no evidence to show that the selected site was unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decisions of the district court.

May 9, 2007, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Woodbury County, Edward A. Jacobson, Judge. Jose Gilberto Medina-Hernandez appeals his convictions for forgery and tampering with records, challenging the sufficiency of the evidence.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Iowa District Court for Woodbury County, which convicted him of forgery, in violation of Iowa Code § 715A.2(2)(a)(4) (2003), and tampering with records, in violation of Iowa Code § 715A.5.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of forgery and tampering with records. On appeal, he challenged the sufficiency of the evidence to sustain his convictions. As to the forgery count, the court found that the evidence proved beyond a reasonable doubt that the social security card that defendant presented to a driver's license station was not valid, and he had no legal right to use it for any purpose; he presented the card with the intent to defraud; the card was a document prescribed by statute for entry into or evidence of authorized stay or employment in the United States; and defendant knew the document was forged. The evidence was sufficient for the trial judge to find that defendant did not have authorization from the owner to use the social security card. As to the tampering with records count, the record showed that defendant signed a different name to obtain a driver's license. He was using the other name to hide his true identity and his illegal status.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

OVERVIEW: A store employee observed defendant masturbating among racks of clothing. In re Marriage of Grittman


No. 6-984 / 05-1925


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2007 Iowa App. LEXIS 204



February 28, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNTIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at In re Marriage of Grittman, 730 N.W.2d 209, 2007 Iowa App. LEXIS 637 (Iowa Ct. App., Feb. 28, 2007)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS MODIFIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Iowa District Court for Polk County granted judgment in favor of appellee mother by establishing a postsecondary education subsidy for the parties' child. Appellant father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The father argued that Iowa Code § 598.21(5A) (2003) violated equal protection under both the federal and state constitutions; the district court erred in ordering the subsidy because the child's expected contributions exceeded the cost of attending a public in-state university; and the district court erred in awarding attorney fees. The appellate court found that the statute was not unconstitutional as it did not violate equal protection. The daughter's available contribution was $7300. By subtracting from the in-state tuition of $15,852 and dividing by two, the appellate court came to the father's contribution: $4276. The father was responsible for a postsecondary education subsidy but the amount was modified from $5000 to $4276. The district court did not err in awarding the mother attorney fees since the action related back to the divorce decree. The mother's request for appellate attorney fees was denied.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed as modified.

Baker v. City of Iowa City


No. 6-1008 / 05-1833


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2007 Iowa App. LEXIS 228



February 28, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNTIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Baker v. City of Iowa City, 730 N.W.2d 210, 2007 Iowa App. LEXIS 643 (Iowa Ct. App., 2007)
Vacated by, Remanded by Baker v. City of Iowa City, 750 N.W.2d 93, 2008 Iowa Sup. LEXIS 79 (Iowa, 2008)
Related proceeding at, Decision reached on appeal by Baker v. City of Iowa City, 2015 Iowa Sup. LEXIS 62 (Iowa, May 22, 2015)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landlord challenged the judgment of the Iowa District Court for Johnson County dismissing his action for declaratory judgment, injunctive relief, damages and a writ of certiorari, filed against appellees, Iowa City and the Iowa City Human Rights Commission, finding the action was moot.


OVERVIEW: The landlord advertised for a resident manager to collect rent and perform maintenance. An applicant for the position, who was not hired, filed a complaint with the Commission alleging the landlord engaged in housing and employment discrimination based on the applicant's race and marital status. The claimed violations were premised on the City's Human Rights Ordinance. While the administrative action was pending, the landlord sued the City and the Commission. The landlord reached a settlement of the administrative action and that action was dismissed with prejudice. In light of the settlement, the district court concluded the civil action with the City and Commission was moot. The landlord argued that the district court erred as a matter of law in concluding that the settlement and dismissal of the administrative action rendered his claims moot. The appellate court agreed with the district court that the case was moot. The landlord's entire lawsuit was premised on the discrimination complaint filed with the Commission. With the dismissal of the discrimination complaint, the controversy that precipitated the landlord's lawsuit was eliminated.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

In re Det. of Harless


No. 6-1017 / 06-0033


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2007 Iowa App. LEXIS 66



January 31, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at In re Det. of Harless, 728 N.W.2d 853, 2007 Iowa App. LEXIS 451 (Iowa Ct. App., Jan. 31, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Woodbury County, Duane E. Hoffmeyer, Judge. Martin Dean Harless appeals his civil commitment as a sexually violent predator pursuant to Iowa Code chapter 229A (2005).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Iowa District Court for Woodbury County denied appellant offender's motions for directed verdict in which he argued that the language of Iowa Code ch. 229A required proof of a more immediate risk to reoffend than the actuarial numbers presented by the State and thus the State failed to show he was presently more likely than not to reoffend if not confined. The offender was civilly committed as a sexually violent predator and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: The offender contended that the State failed to prove he was presently more likely than not to engage in a sexually violent offense if not confined in a secure facility as required by Iowa Code § 229A.2. Both parties presented expert testimony to the jury on the offender's likelihood to reoffend and thus whether he met the statutory definition of a sexually violent predator. Some of the evidence showed that his lifetime risk to reoffend was 52%. There were several factors that suggested the 52% was low including the fact that since his first conviction for a sexual offense there had not been a period of time of more than a few months where he had been free and had not reoffended, as well as his failure to complete a structured sexual offender program. Perhaps the most compelling evidence presented that the 52% likelihood to reoffend was low was that the actuarial instruments used actually measured recidivism by using rates of reconviction for sexual offenses rather than using rates of reoffending. The jury could have found beyond a reasonable doubt that the offender was presently more likely than not to reoffend if not confined to a secure facility as required by § 229A.2.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Brunk


No. 6-677 / 05-1468


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2006 Iowa App. LEXIS 1082



September 21, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Wapello County, Kirk A. Daily, Judge. Jody Paul Brunk appeals his conviction, following a trial to the court on the minutes of evidence, for operating while intoxicated, second offense.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Iowa District Court for Wapello County, which convicted him of operating while intoxicated (OWI), second offense. Specifically, defendant challenged the denial of his motion to suppress evidence.


OVERVIEW: Police received an anonymous call that a man in a red pickup truck was in a parking lot did not look conscious. An officer was dispatched to the area, and he observed defendant leaving the parking lot in the vehicle. Although he did not observe defendant violating any traffic laws, he stopped the vehicle. Defendant was subsequently arrested for OWI, and he filed a motion to suppress based on the legality of the stop. The district court denied his motion, and defendant sought review. In affirming, the appellate court determined that defendant's rights under the Fourth Amendment and Iowa Const. art. I, § 8 were not violated since the community caretaking exception applied. There was a three-prong test to determine if this exception applied. First, there was a seizure when the stop was made. Second, the police officer was conducting a bona fide community caretaker activity because defendant could have had a medical problem that the officer was unable to ascertain just by following him for a few minutes. Finally, the public need and interest required the officer to determine defendant's condition. This need and interest outweighed the minimal intrusion on defendant's rights.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

Perkins v. Dallas Center-Grimes Cmty. Sch. Dist.


No. 6-241 / 05-1075


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2006 Iowa App. LEXIS 467



May 24, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Perkins v. Dallas Center-Grimes Cmty. Sch. Dist., 2006 Iowa App. LEXIS 1414 (Iowa Ct. App., May 24, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Polk County, Robert J. Blink, Judge. Plaintiff appeals from the district court's ruling granting summary judgment in favor of defendant.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff student, by her parent and next friend, appealed a decision of the District Court for Polk County (Iowa), which granted summary judgment to defendant school district, a municipality under Iowa Code § 670.1(2) (2003). The student sued the district for judgment for injuries that she suffered when she put her hand and wrist through a glass door at a high school. The district claimed that her suit was barred under Iowa Code § 670.5.


OVERVIEW: The Iowa Supreme Court had held that Iowa Code § 614.8, which extended the statute of limitations in Iowa Code ch. 614, did not apply to toll statutes of limitation outside of Chapter 614. The supreme court had also held that provisions of Iowa Code § 670.5 could be severed to "save" the provision permitting the filing of an action within two years after timely notice of a claim had been given, while other parts of the statute were unconstitutional. Because § 670.5 remained a valid statute of limitations, Iowa Code § 614.8 did not apply to toll the two-year statute of limitations in Iowa Code § 670.5. The student failed to file suit within two years of the notice of claim. Thus, her suit was untimely and summary judgment was properly granted in favor of the district.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the district court's ruling granting summary judgment in favor of the school district and dismissing the case.

State v. Doss


No. 6-281 / 05-1192


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2006 Iowa App. LEXIS 485



May 24, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Doss, 2006 Iowa App. LEXIS 1431 (Iowa Ct. App., May 24, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Black Hawk County, K.D. Briner and Bruce Zager, Judges. Michael Doss appeals from the sentence entered upon his conviction for willful injury.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to willful injury, a class "D" felony in violation of Iowa Code § 708.4(2) (2003). The Iowa District Court for Black Hawk County sentenced defendant to a five-year indeterminate term of incarceration and ordered defendant to submit a DNA sample for profiling. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the district court abused its discretion by imposing DNA profiling as a part of sentencing. Defendant alternatively claimed that trial counsel provided ineffective assistance by failing to argue that mandatory DNA profiling violated (1) the constitutional proscription against unreasonable searches and seizures under the Fourth Amendment and Iowa Const. art. I, § 8, and (2) his right to equal protection of the laws. The appellate court rejected defendant's arguments. Iowa Code ch. 81 (Supp. 2005) required the district court to order DNA profiling because defendant, a felon, was sentenced after June 14, 2005. Counsel breached no duty in failing to assert an equal protection challenge, because all felons were subject to DNA profiling and the statutory provisions authorizing DNA profiling for convicted felons were rationally related to legitimate government purposes such as identifying perpetrators of future crimes and exonerating the innocent. Counsel was not ineffective in failing to raise the search and seizure issue, because the DNA profiling statute did not authorize unreasonable searches in violation of the Fourth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed.

 

499 of 583 DOCUMENTS


Latiker v. City of Council Bluffs


No. 6-069 / 05-0304


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2006 Iowa App. LEXIS 440



April 26, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Latiker v. City of Council Bluffs, 2006 Iowa App. LEXIS 1358 (Iowa Ct. App., Apr. 26, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Pottawattamie County, Timothy O'Grady Judge. Leroy Latiker appeals from the district court order affirming the order of the Board of Public Health for the City of Council Bluffs and dismissing his action for damages against the City.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individual sued appellee city, contending that certain ordinances governing the forfeiture of his dog were unconstitutionally vague, violated his procedural and substantive due process rights, and were preempted by state law. The Iowa District Court for Pottawattamie County affirmed the city's order of forfeiture and dismissed the action for damages. The individual appealed.


OVERVIEW: City of Council Bluffs, Iowa, Ordinance § 4.20.030 was not unconstitutionally vague as it could be interpreted to allow the director to take the actions provided in other ordinance sections in the same chapter. The impoundment of animals did not violate procedural due process as the individual had received oral notice of the impoundment of his dog and written notice of the city's intention to forfeit the dog through adoption. He also had a hearing before the city's board of health. The individual was not entitled to notice of the right to redeem his dog as the dog had been impounded under City of Council Bluffs, Iowa, Ordinance § 4.20.030. The impoundment did not violate substantive due process given the director's authority to take actions as he deemed appropriate. Section 4.20.030 was not preempted by state law because Iowa Code § 364.3(3) allowed a city to set more stringent standards and requirements unless otherwise provided by state law and there was no state law prohibiting a city from allowing for forfeiture in a simple misdemeanor case. Finally no double jeopardy occurred because the purpose of the forfeiture under the ordinance was indisputably remedial in nature.


OUTCOME: The order affirming the order of forfeiture and dismissing the individual's claims for damages was affirmed.

State v. King


No. 6-137 / 05-1034


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2006 Iowa App. LEXIS 261



March 29, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. King, 715 N.W.2d 770, 2006 Iowa App. LEXIS 897 (Iowa Ct. App., Mar. 29, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Buchanan County, K. D. Briner, Judge. A defendant appeals from the sentence imposed following his guilty plea to one count of lascivious acts with a child.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant entered a guilty plea to one count of lascivious acts with a child, the Iowa District Court for Buchanan County sentenced him to an indeterminate five-year term of confinement, to be followed by two years of special release. The court also imposed a $ 750 fine and a 30-percent surcharge. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended two-year additional term constituted an illegal sentence because it exceeded the maximum sentence allowed under Iowa Code § 902.9(5), the general indeterminate sentencing statute, and conflicted with the definitions of "parole" and "work release" found in Iowa Code §§ 904.901, 906.1. The appellate court disagreed, finding that defendant's sentence was clearly authorized under Iowa Code § 709.8 (2003). Moreover, there was no basis for defendant's claim that the trial court imposed a sentence above and beyond the statutorily authorized maximum. Even if the two statutes were irreconcilable, the specific provisions of § 709.8 prevailed over the more general provisions of Iowa Code § 902.9. In either event, the trial court did not impose an illegal sentence. Even if the conflict between the statutes was sufficient to create a latent ambiguity, that ambiguity alone was not a basis for invalidating the statutory sentencing scheme. As the disputed portion of Iowa Code § 709.8 (2003) was more specific than the general parole and work release provisions, and was enacted subsequent to those provisions, it prevailed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Carter


No. 5-980 / 04-1271


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2006 Iowa App. LEXIS 164



March 1, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Carter, 2006 Iowa App. LEXIS 835 (Iowa Ct. App., Mar. 1, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Webster County, Fredrick E. Breen, District Associate Judge. Kenneth Carter appeals from the judgment and sentence entered upon his conviction for possession of marijuana.
State v. Carter, 604 N.W.2d 64, 1999 Iowa Sup. LEXIS 338 (Iowa, 1999)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Iowa District Court for Webster County, which denied his motion to suppress evidence and convicted him of possession of marijuana.


OVERVIEW: As a result of a search of his home, defendant was charged with drug-related crimes. The case was referred to the Iowa Department of Revenue and Finance to collect taxes due on the drugs. The charges against defendant were dismissed. Nearly six months later, the Department obtained an administrative warrant to search defendant's residence and seize any item to satisfy the tax. As officers were executing the administrative warrant, they noticed the odor of marijuana. After a search warrant was obtained, officers discovered marijuana. Defendant was convicted of possession of marijuana. On appeal, the court held that Iowa Code § 453B.9 (1997) did not violate the constitutional prohibition against unreasonable searches and seizures. The primary factor militating in favor of upholding the tax warrant was its characterization as an administrative warrant, designed specifically and solely for the collection of a tax debt. As an administrative warrant, a finding that a crime had been committed was not required. When the court balanced the State's need to collect a tax due on the possession of illicit drugs against the invasiveness of the search, the State's interests prevailed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

State v. Crytser


No. 5-794 / 04-1950


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2006 Iowa App. LEXIS 104



February 1, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Crytser, 713 N.W.2d 247, 2006 Iowa App. LEXIS 509 (Iowa Ct. App., Feb. 1, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Polk County, Robert B. Hanson, Judge. A defendant appeals from sentences imposed following his guilty pleas to ten counts of sexual exploitation of a minor and one count of lascivious acts with a child.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Iowa District Court for Polk County, which sentenced him for 10 counts of sexual exploitation of a minor, Iowa Code § 728.12(3) (2001), and one count of lascivious acts with a child, Iowa Code § 709.8 (2001). Defendant argued that the district court imposed an illegal sentence when it ordered him to serve an additional term of parole or work release after expiration of his period of confinement.


OVERVIEW: The district court sentenced defendant to confinement and further ordered that, upon completion of defendant's confinement, he was sentenced to an additional term of parole or work release not to exceed two years. On appeal, the court rejected defendant's argument that the additional term constituted an illegal sentence because it exceeded the maximum sentence allowed under Iowa Code § 902.9(5), the general indeterminate sentencing statute, and it conflicted with the definitions of "parole" and "work release" found in Iowa Code §§ 904.901 and 906.1. The additional term of parole or work release was imposed pursuant to § 709.8 and was therefore authorized by statute. Section 709.8, which dealt with sentencing for the particular crime of lascivious acts with a child, was more specific than the general sentencing provisions of § 902.9. The court concluded that the two provisions could be given concurrent effect. Even if the two statutes were irreconcilable, the specific provisions of § 709.8 would prevail over the more general provisions of § 902.9. Lastly, the court rejected defendant's argument that § 709.8 was unconstitutionally void.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

2006 Iowa App. LEXIS 62



January 19, 2006, Filed

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at In re Property Seized from Flores, 711 N.W.2d 733, 2006 Iowa App. LEXIS 376 (Iowa Ct. App., Jan. 19, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Polk County, Joel D. Novak, Judge. The State appeals from the district court's adverse ruling in an in rem forfeiture action.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State of Iowa challenged the judgment of the Iowa District Court for Polk County, refusing to grant in rem forfeiture of personal property owned by appellee owner.


OVERVIEW: The forfeiture proceedings stemmed from the owner's participation in an attempted marijuana transaction, where the owner acted as look-out for his cousin. Following the owner's arrest, officers seized the owner's truck. The owner pled guilty to possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver. Although the district court found the truck was subject to forfeiture under Iowa Code § 809A.13(7) (2003) because a substantial connection was proved between the truck and the criminal offense, the district court found forfeiture of the $ 30,000 truck would be "grossly disproportional" to the owner's criminal culpability and would therefore constitute an excessive fine in violation of his constitutional rights. The appellate court ruled that the owner satisfied his burden to demonstrate the "punishment" occasioned by the proposed forfeiture would bear a grossly disproportional relationship with the gravity of his offense and the extent of his culpability. The owner pled guilty to a class D felony, which carried a maximum fine of $ 7,500, and forfeiture of the $ 30,000 truck would result in an economic loss to the owner four times the maximum fine authorized by the Iowa Legislature.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Little


No. 5-651 / 05-0157


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2005 Iowa App. LEXIS 1540



December 21, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Little, 710 N.W.2d 545, 2005 Iowa App. LEXIS 1682 (Iowa Ct. App., Dec. 21, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Washington County, Lucy J. Gamon, District Associate Judge. Nicholas Little appeals his conviction for operating while intoxicated, first offense.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Iowa District Court for Washington County convicted defendant of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated (OWI), first offense. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the trial court erred by both refusing to allow him to use the prescribed medicine defense in Iowa Code § 321J.2(7)(a)-(b) and finding he intended to operate a motor vehicle. He also argued that Iowa Code § 321J.2 was void because it was vague and overbroad. The appellate court disagreed, finding that defendant told the arresting officer he had consumed five to six beers. Even at trial, he admitted to drinking 24 ounces of beer. Because the evidence showed defendant consumed alcohol, he could not use the prescribed medicine defense. Nor was it error to deny defendant to use the automatism defense as his behavior evidenced consciousness, he knew that mixing drugs with alcohol was not a good idea, and he was operating a motor vehicle. Thus, the trial court's finding of general intent was proper. Further, the OWI statute had already been found not to be vague, and protecting the public from drivers impaired by drugs and alcohol was rational basis for the statute.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2005 Iowa App. LEXIS 1547



December 21, 2005, Filed

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Fremont County, Timothy O'Grady, Judge. Donna Carter appeals from a verdict in favor of the defendant, Gary Rowe, on her personal injury claim.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant daughter appealed a verdict entered by a jury in the Iowa District Court for Fremont County in favor of appellee father after the daughter sustained injuries riding one of the father's horses.


OVERVIEW: The daughter was at her parent's house, and after a Thanksgiving meal, went out to ride one of her father's horses. The daughter was thrown off the horse and sustained injuries. The daughter had previously ridden the horse several times without incident and had watched as her own daughter rode the horse earlier in the day. The daughter claimed that Iowa Code § 673.2 was unconstitutional and in violation of the inalienable rights and equal protection under Iowa Const. art. I, § 1 and art. I, § 6. The appellate court rejected the daughter's constitutional challenge to Iowa Code § 673.2 on the grounds that (1) it violated Iowa's inalienable rights clause and (2) it violated Iowa's equal protection clause as the daughter's right to seek recovery for an injury from a horse accident under a theory of mere negligence as opposed to the heightened standard of recklessness was not a protected property right, and § 673.2 did not violate the equal protection clause as all individuals who were injured by domesticated animal activity were treated in a like manner; in other words, they could only recover for reckless behavior.


OUTCOME: The jury verdict was affirmed.

 

507 of 583 DOCUMENTS


In re Det. of Selby


No. 5-627 / 04-0806


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


710 N.W.2d 249; 2005 Iowa App. LEXIS 1497



December 7, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Appanoose County, Annette Scieszinski (motion to dismiss) and James Q. Blomgren (commitment order), Judges. Johnny C. Selby appeals the jury verdict finding him to be a sexually violent predator.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury from the District Court for Appanoose County (Iowa) found defendant to be a sexually violent predator under Iowa Code ch. 229A (2003). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had a history of sexually abusing children since 1985. On appeal, he argued that Iowa Code ch. 229A (2003) was unconstitutional because it violated both due process and equal protection; and, the jury instruction was improper. He essentially claimed that ch. 229A was not narrowly tailored. He argued that the statute violated due process because it permitted commitment through showing that the offender was more likely than not to re-offend at some point within his lifetime. He argued that the likelihood of re-offense must be within a shorter time period, such as within the immediate future. The appellate court found his arguments unconvincing because the present tense language of ch. 229A required that a person be found to be both dangerous and to have a mental abnormality at the time of the proposed commitment and ch. 229A provided for a yearly review of the individual's condition. The present tense language and the annual review provision allowed ch. 229A to comport with due process. The appellate court concluded it was proper to review defendant's equal protection claim under a rational basis analysis, and it found nothing wrong with the jury instruction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

508 of 583 DOCUMENTS


State v. Anderson


No. 5-628 / 04-1086


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2005 Iowa App. LEXIS 1410



November 23, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Anderson, 710 N.W.2d 257, 2005 Iowa App. LEXIS 1700 (Iowa Ct. App., Nov. 23, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Polk County, D. J. Stovall (motion to sever) and Robert B. Hanson (trial), Judges. Brett Anderson appeals from his conviction for four counts of second-degree sexual abuse.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of four counts of second-degree sexual abuse (one count for each victim), in the Iowa District Court for Polk County. Defendant appealed, challenging the sufficiency of the evidence and the trial court's refusal to sever the charges. he also asserted that counsel was ineffective for failing to challenge Iowa Code §§ 702.17, 709.1, and 709.3 as unconstitutionally over-broad and vague.


OVERVIEW: The record showed the victims made explicit allegations, describing defendant's acts of rubbing his penis against their buttocks. Defendant argued that such actions did not meet the statutory definition of a sex act. However, the statutory language of Iowa Code § 709.1 was broad. Contact between an adult and child simply had to be sexual in nature to fall within the definition of sex act. Further, the statute did not restrict the use of artificial or substitute sexual organs (at issue in most of the case law), to the perpetrator. The statute used the less restrictive "one person" and "another person" language when defining sex acts. Thus, the evidence sufficed to support defendants convictions. Secondly, the district court did not err in not granting defendant's motion to sever since prejudice was less likely in a bench trial, and while the separate offenses occurred over a long period of time, they probably would have been admissible to show defendant's motive had there been severance. Finally, Iowa Code §§ 702.17, 709.1, and 709.3 were not unconstitutionally over-broad and vague and counsel did not fail in an essential duty by not raising any challenges thereon.


OUTCOME: We affirm the defendant's convictions. We conclude trial counsel was not ineffective in not challenging the constitutionality of the statutes. We preserve the remaining ineffective assistance claims for possible postconviction proceedings.

State v. Bevard


No. 5-786 / 05-0484


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2005 Iowa App. LEXIS 1344



November 9, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Bevard, 707 N.W.2d 338, 2005 Iowa App. LEXIS 1646 (Iowa Ct. App., Nov. 9, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Clayton County, J.G. Johnson and Joseph Moothart, Judges. Jeremy Creede Bevard appeals the judgment and sentence entered upon his conviction for operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated, first offense.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted for operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated (OWI). He appealed, asserting that the Iowa District Court for Clayton County erred in denying his motion to suppress because the district court incorrectly interpreted Iowa Code § 321.354 (a prohibition as to stopping a vehicle on a highway), and in doing so, violated his constitutional right against unreasonable stops, searches and seizures.


OVERVIEW: The record showed that in the very late hours, an officer observed defendant stop his vehicle at a highway intersection even though defendant had no stop sign or signal to do so and there were no other vehicles approaching from any direction. Defendant then proceeded on at a high rate of speed. The officer then stopped defendant for "stopping on the paved part of highway," in violation of Iowa Code § 321.354. At that time the officer determined that defendant was intoxicated. The appellate court agreed with the district court that the Iowa Supreme Court had previously decided the prohibition found in § 321.354 against stopping a vehicle on the traveled portion of the highway included momentary, as well as extended, stops. Thus, the officer had reasonable cause to believe defendant had committed a traffic offense and reasonable suspicion to conduct an investigatory stop of his vehicle. Accordingly, defendant's motion to suppress was properly denied.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

In re Det. of Selby


No. 5-627 / 04-0806


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2005 Iowa App. LEXIS 1272



October 26, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at In re Det. of Selby, 707 N.W.2d 337, 2005 Iowa App. LEXIS 1598 (Iowa Ct. App., Oct. 26, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Appanoose County, Annette Scieszinski (motion to dismiss) and James Q. Blomgren (commitment order), Judges. Johnny C. Selby appeals the jury verdict finding him to be a sexually violent predator.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In 1985, appellant, a former inmate, admitted committing lascivious acts with a child. In 1989, he was convicted of second degree sexual abuse. In 2002, he pled guilty to indecent contact with a child. In 2003, the State petitioned to have the inmate committed as a sexually violent predator pursuant to Iowa Code ch. 229A. A jury in the Iowa District Court for Appanoose County found he was a sexually violent predator. The former inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the former inmate argued that Iowa Code ch. 229A (2003) violated due process because it failed to contain a temporal limitation for calculating a predator's risk of re-offense. Second, he argued that the statute violated equal protection because it required a standard of proof for commitment different from the standard required to commit similarly situated individuals under Iowa Code ch. 229 (2003). However, the appellate court held that where, as in the former inmate's case, a recent overt act had been found, same was sufficient for a finding of dangerousness. A mental abnormality along with the recent overt act therefore made an individual a present and immediate threat to the community. Thus, as to the application of ch. 229, due process was satisfied because a person had to be found both dangerous and mentally ill at the time of commitment. Secondly, even before adjudication as sexually violent predators, individuals subject to commitment under ch. 229A were not similarly situated to individuals subject to commitment under Iowa Code ch. 229. Thus, it was proper to review the former inmate's equal protection claim under a rational basis analysis.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the lower court's decision.

Cannon v. Bd. of Psychology Exam'rs


No. 5-649 / 05-0026


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2005 Iowa App. LEXIS 1236



October 12, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Cannon v. Bd. of Psychology Exam'rs, 707 N.W.2d 336, 2005 Iowa App. LEXIS 1569 (Iowa Ct. App., Oct. 12, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Polk County, Robert J. Blink, Judge. The petitioner appeals from a district court ruling that upheld the denial of his application for licensure.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, an applicant, applied for licensure with respondent, the Board of Psychology Examiners of the State of Iowa. The Board denied his application on grounds that he had not completed a one year residency at the educational institution which granted his doctoral degree as required by Iowa Admin. Code r. 645-240.3(2)(i). The Iowa District Court for Polk County affirmed the decision. The applicant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The applicant first contended the Board erred in interpreting Iowa Admin. Code r. 645-240.3(2)(i) as requiring a continuous "one year's residency" because the Board was reading a requirement into the rule that did not appear on its face. He asserted the Board's interpretation of the rule was unreasonably restrictive as it effectively foreclosed licensure for all candidates who received degrees from non-traditional, non-American Psychological Association (APA) accredited institutions (as he did). However, an agency was entitled to substantial deference when interpreting its own regulations, and the appellate court did not find that the Board's interpretation of its own rule was irrational, illogical, or wholly unjustifiable. Further, the legislature had clearly vested the Board with the authority to adopt and enforce rules governing educational qualifications. The appellate court also rejected the Board's interpretation deprives him of equal protection under the law. There was no evidence the Board applied a different standard in evaluating his application than it had in evaluating the applications of other individuals who had received degrees from non-APA-accredited schools.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was affirmed.

In the Interest of T.R.


No. 5-598 / 05-1031


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2005 Iowa App. LEXIS 968



August 31, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at In re T.R., 705 N.W.2d 507, 2005 Iowa App. LEXIS 1488 (Iowa Ct. App., 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Benton County, Patrick R. Grady, Judge. A mother appeals from the juvenile court order terminating her parental rights to one child.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A child had previously been adjudicated a child in need of assistance (CINA). A subsequent juvenile court order confirmed one child's return to foster care and formally rescinded her trial placement with appellant mother. Pursuant to a petition filed by appellee State, the Iowa District Court for Benton County filed a ruling terminating the mother's parental rights pursuant to Iowa Code § 232.116(1)(f) (2005) to her child. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother first claimed that the court erred in finding that her child had been removed for the period of time required by the third element of § 232.116(1)(e) as the child had been in a trial home placement with the mother for more than 30 days. She argued that under the statutory language a child had not been removed for the requisite period not only if a trial period at home of 30 days or more had occurred within the last 12 consecutive months but also if a trial period at home of 30 days or more had occurred within the period of 12 of the last 18 months. Reading the claim as applying to the third element of current § 232.116(1)(f), the language "and any trial period at home has been less than 30 days" applied to and qualified only the phrase within which it appeared following the word "or." The appellate court agreed that applying the qualifying language "and any trial period at home has been less than 30 days" to the phrase "for at least 12 of the last 18 months" would effectively read that phrase out of the statute because by its terms that phrase allowed the State to pursue termination even when a child might have been in a parental home for up to 6 of the last 18 months.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court for Polk County (Iowa), which convicted him of possession of marijuana, second offense. Defendant was given a suspended sentence and placed on probation for a period of two years. On appeal, defendant claimed that the district court should have granted his motion to suppress.


OVERVIEW: The officer was observing defendant's car based on a report that the car appeared to be observing a regular cash drop in anticipation of a robbery. The court next found that defendant consented to a search of his pockets by voluntarily removing the items from his pockets. The court found that the officer's testimony on the issue of consent was more credible than that of defendant. Because the specific issue of whether the "dugout" found in defendant's pocket was not addressed by the district court, that issue was not preserved for appellate review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Cromer


No. 5-101 / 04-0814


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2005 Iowa App. LEXIS 236



March 31, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Cromer, 697 N.W.2d 127, 2005 Iowa App. LEXIS 738 (Iowa Ct. App., 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Muscatine County, Patrick J. Madden, Judge. The State of Iowa appeals the district court's grant of a new trial.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a judgment of the Iowa District Court for Muscatine County, which granted defendant's motion for a new trial following a jury verdict finding defendant guilty of third-degree sexual abuse in violation of Iowa Code §§ 709.4(1) and 709.4(4) (2003).


OVERVIEW: The victim found herself heavily intoxicated and she accepted a ride home with defendant and another man. The victim's next memory was waking up naked on a motel bed between defendant and the other man. The court concluded that the district court abused its discretion in granting defendant's motion for new trial. The fact that defendant was subject to criminal sanctions because he incorrectly assessed the victim's mental capacity did not render the statute unconstitutional. The statute did not violate defendant's due process rights. The standard imposed by Iowa Code § 709.4(4) was clear: to avoid the proscribed conduct, defendant should have refrained from performing a sex act with a person who was mentally incapacitated as that term was defined in Iowa Code § 709.1A(1). If he did engage in such conduct, his lack of knowledge of the victim's mental incapacitation caused by his intoxication was no defense. The weight of the evidence supported a jury conclusion that defendant knew of the victim's mental incapacitation, as evidence indicated she was dragged into the hotel room and was unconscious throughout the entire incident.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

Koos v. Willson


No. 5-058 / 04-1308


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2005 Iowa App. LEXIS 243



March 31, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Koos v. Willson, 697 N.W.2d 127, 2005 Iowa App. LEXIS 742 (Iowa Ct. App., 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Dickinson County, Frank B. Nelson, Judge. Jeffrey Koos appeals from an order that disestablished his paternity of Brayde L. Willson-Koos.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant established father challenged a decision of the Iowa District Court for Dickinson County, which disestablished him as the father of appellee mother's child under Iowa Code § 600B.41A and agreed with the claim of appellee putative father, filed in his action to overcome paternity, that he was the child's father.


OVERVIEW: The established father was originally placed on the child's birth certificate. Later, the putative father claimed that he was the father of the child. The trial court took judicial notice of paternity tests and ruled in the putative father's favor. The court reversed. The one court order addressing the blood tests did not follow the terms of Iowa Code § 600B.41(2) (2003). The test results were filed by a party, not by an appointed expert, thus not meeting the requirements for admission without further foundation pursuant to § 600B.41(2). The putative father made no effort to establish a foundation for the tests. Therefore, the trial court erred in taking judicial notice of the tests. The putative father was entitled to petition the court to overcome the established father's paternity, but the court found this right waived. Despite having knowledge of the child's birth and the fact that he might have been the child's father, the putative father took no action to establish his parental rights for over five years. Thus, the established father's paternity should not have been disestablished, and under Iowa Code § 600B.41A(6)(b), the court dismissed the action to overcome paternity.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and dismissed the action to overcome paternity. The court preserved the paternity of the established father and established that the child remained his son and that he was to remain in the established father's primary physical care.

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Story County, Ronald H. Schechtman, Judge. Applicant appeals from district court's dismissal of his application for postconviction relief.
State v. Walker, 574 N.W.2d 280, 1998 Iowa Sup. LEXIS 15 (Iowa, 1998)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State charged defendant with perjury in violation of Iowa Code § 720.2 (1995), and tampering with records in violation of Iowa Code § 715A.5. Following trial, a jury returned a guilty verdict on each count. The convictions and sentences were upheld by the supreme court on direct appeal. Defendant requested postconviction relief; the Iowa District Court for Story County dismissed his application. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant certified, by signing a subpoena's proof of service, that he had personally served a witness. Nevertheless, defendant told the notary that he had not yet served defendant. Appellate counsel was not ineffective for failing to raise these meritless claims.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Black Hawk County, Bruce Zager and Thomas N. Bower, Judges. Wilson Bolden appeals from his convictions and sentences for possession of cocaine and public intoxication.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Iowa District Court for Black Hawk County, which convicted him of possession of a controlled substance and public intoxication, third offense, upon his guilty pleas. He was sentenced to serve a 15-year indeterminate term of imprisonment under the first count and a two-year term of imprisonment under the second count, to run concurrently. He was also ordered to pay various fees.


OVERVIEW: Police officers arrested defendant for public intoxication after he exhibited slurred speech, poor balance, watery/bloodshot eyes, and an odor consistent to that of alcohol emitting from his person. During the search incident to his arrest, the officers located a "crack pipe" in the roll of his stocking cap. On appeal, defendant contended that the trial court failed to establish an adequate factual basis prior to accepting his guilty pleas. Defendant's pleas were supported by a factual basis and defense counsel was not ineffective for failing to raise a meritless issue. The court further found that the plain meaning of "intoxicated" in Iowa Code § 123.46 (2003) clearly applied to defendant's physical state. The public intoxication statute, § 123.46, was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences.

State v. Philpott


No. 4-697/04-0060


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2005 Iowa App. LEXIS 66



January 26, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Philpott, 695 N.W.2d 503, 2005 Iowa App. LEXIS 987 (Iowa Ct. App., 2005)
Affirmed by State v. Philpott, 2005 Iowa Sup. LEXIS 112 (Iowa, Aug. 19, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Floyd County, Joseph P. Moothart, Judge. Carolee Philpott appeals from her conviction for mechanical eavesdropping in violation of Iowa Code section 727.8 (2003).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court for Floyd County (Iowa) convicted defendant of mechanical eavesdropping in violation of Iowa Code § 727.8 (2003). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court denied defendant's motion for a new trial. It determined the statute was not void for vagueness or overbroad because defendant had not established a First Amendment right to tape record communications while she was absent. The court determined Iowa Code § 727.8 (2003) was a general intent statute and equal protection was not violated because no fundamental right or suspect classification was involved, and the State had a rational basis for protecting its citizens from having their communications intercepted by unauthorized persons. The statute required either that the person recording obtain the authority or else be openly present. The statute merely prevented defendant from indiscriminate recording of conversations to which she was not a party. Defendant was not recording her conversations and interactions with coworkers. She failed to turn off the recorder when she left the office. The trial court was correct in not incorporating willfulness from Iowa Code ch. 808B, as it was not an element in Iowa Code § 727.8. Having determined defendant's theory of the case was incorrect, the evidence supported the verdict.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Harms v. City of Sibley


No. 4-477/03-0728


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2004 Iowa App. LEXIS 1279



November 24, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Harms v. City of Sibley, 695 N.W.2d 43, 2004 Iowa App. LEXIS 1545 (Iowa Ct. App., 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Osceola County, John P. Duffy, Judge. Defendants, the City of Sibley, Joe's Ready Mix, Inc., and Arlon Sandbulte appeal from a money judgment entered against them and in favor of Kenneth Harms and Myrna Harms.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the city, a lessor, and a lessee, sought review of the decision of the Iowa District court for Osceola County, which found in favor of plaintiff homeowners, held the city liable under a theory of a taking, and held the lessor and the lessee liable under a theory of nuisance resulting from the construction of a cement ready-mix plant.


OVERVIEW: The city had rezoned property from to allow construction of the plant on property owned by the lessor within the city limits. The lessor leased the property to the lessee and the district court subsequently found that the plant created a compensable nuisance and that the two homeowners were damaged as a result. The city was held liable under the theory of a taking without just compensation by inverse condemnation because the city rezoned to allow the use. On appeal, the court reversed the takings determination, stating that there was no compensable taking by the city pursuant to U.S. Const. amends. V and XIV or Iowa Const. art I, §§ 9 and 18, because the rezoning did not cause a permanent physical invasion of the homeowners' property. The court affirmed the nuisance finding pursuant to Iowa Code §§ 657.1 and 657.2 (2001), stating that the homeowners lived on their land for 35 years prior to the intrusion of the plant and the lessor's plant was the only heavy industrial operation in the neighborhood. Further, the trucks coming and going caused substantial noise, dust, and fumes. There was also a basis for holding the lessor liable for the nuisance in the same manner as the lessor.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the finding that the city committed a taking but affirmed the nuisance finding against the lessor and the lessee.

 

521 of 583 DOCUMENTS


Yohn v. Levik


No. 4-672/04-0006


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2004 Iowa App. LEXIS 1293



November 24, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Yohn v. Levik, 695 N.W.2d 44, 2004 Iowa App. LEXIS 1569 (Iowa Ct. App., 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Winnebago County, John S. Mackey, Judge. A plaintiff appeals from the district court's grant of summary judgment dismissing his petition seeking damages against the defendants for the defendants' action in abating a nuisance on the plaintiff's property.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city gave plaintiff property owner notice to abate a nuisance. The property owner took no action, and the city abated the nuisance by removing certain materials. The property owner sued the city, alleging that there was no nuisance and that the city's action amounted to an unconstitutional taking. The Iowa District Court for Winnebago County granted summary judgment for the city based on immunity. The property owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The district court concluded that the city was performing a discretionary function under the applicable ordinances and was afforded discretionary function immunity under Iowa Code § 670.4(3). The appellate court agreed with the district court, that the city satisfied both prongs of the analysis for such immunity required under the United State's Supreme Court decision in Berkovitz. Under the applicable ordinance, the challenged conduct did involve an element of judgment or discretion and the first part of the Berkovitz test was met. The second issue was whether the city could have considered legitimate policy-based factors in its decision to abate the particular nuisance. Legitimate policy-based considerations were those supported by social, political, or economic policies. The appellate court held the city legitimately could have considered such matters, and economic development policies, and how the continuing existence of a large, visible nuisance would have affected decisions of businesses and people to move to, remain in, or leave the city. Thus, the city's action was the performance of a discretionary function that was entitled to statutory immunity.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

City of Fort Dodge v. Martin


No. 4-513/03-1743


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2004 Iowa App. LEXIS 1296



November 24, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at City of Fort Dodge v. Martin, 695 N.W.2d 43, 2004 Iowa App. LEXIS 1550 (Iowa Ct. App., 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Webster County, Gary L. McMinimee, Judge. Paul Martin appeals the district court's injunctive order preventing him from collecting rents and evicting tenants for failure to pay rent until his properties are inspected and certified by the city of Fort Dodge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landlord appealed an injunction granted by the Iowa District Court for Webster County on appellee city's petition that prohibited him from collecting rents and evicting tenants for failure to pay rent until his properties were inspected and certified by the city.


OVERVIEW: The landowner was the owner of three multiple unit residential rental properties located within the municipal limits of the city. Pursuant to Iowa Code § 364.17(3) (1999) and Fort Dodge, Iowa, Mun. Code, ch. 14.08, the sheriff served the landlord with notification of a housing inspection. The landlord subsequently amended his leases to provide that "the landlord was not allowed to provide entry to third parties to the rental property for any reason without express permission of the tenant." The landlord also informed the tenants that they would bear the cost of any future inspections. The appellate court affirmed the injunction and held that it was a legitimate use of the city's police power to make sure that the landlord was providing dwellings that promoted the health and safety of tenants. The appellate court held that the inspection process was not so oppressive that it amounted to a taking. The appellate court also held that the clause that the landlord added to his leases went against public policy because it was calculated to obstruct inspections of the landlord's rental properties; thus, the clause could not be used to excuse his refusal to access or avoid the injunction.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Iowa District Court for Dallas County, which convicted him of operating a vehicle while intoxicated, first offense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of operating a vehicle while intoxicated, first offense. He was sentenced to 32 days in jail, with all but two days suspended, one-year probation, and fined $ 1,000. Heard v. State


No. 4-530 / 03-1077


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2004 Iowa App. LEXIS 1218



October 27, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Heard v. State, 695 N.W.2d 41, 2004 Iowa App. LEXIS 1488 (Iowa Ct. App., 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Lee (North) County, Mary Ann Brown, Judge. Todd Allen Heard appeals the denial of his postconviction relief application.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate was found guilty of kidnapping, among other things. The inmate requested postconviction relief, claiming he was denied effective assistance of trial counsel. The Iowa District Court for Lee (North) County denied his request. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate escaped from a prison farm, and he entered the home of a local couple. The inmate ordered the wife into another bedroom, where he sexually assaulted her. On appeal, defendant argued that trial counsel rendered ineffective assistance for failing to attack the wife's inconsistent statements. The State asserted that the statements were not inconsistent, and, even assuming they were, the factfinder was alerted to any differences by trial counsel. Moreover, the inmate was not prejudiced. The inmate also argued that his trial counsel was ineffective in failing to challenge Iowa's kidnapping statute as unconstitutionally vague as applied to the facts of his case. Nevertheless, counsel was not ineffective for failing to raise a meritless issue. The appellate court also found no merit in the contention that the trial court imposed punishment for an act that was not punishable when committed. Finally, trial counsel was not ineffective based on his strategical decision to advise the inmate not to testify.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

In the Interest of C.C.


No. 4-374 / 04-0120


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2004 Iowa App. LEXIS 1050



September 9, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at In the Interest of C.C., 2004 Iowa App. LEXIS 1652 (Iowa Ct. App., Sept. 9, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Polk County, William A. Price, District Associate Judge. A minor child argues the State offered insufficient evidence that he committed the delinquent act of indecent exposure.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, appealed the judgment of the Iowa District Court for Polk County that adjudicated him delinquent for indecent exposure.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the State did not prove all the elements of indecent exposure. The court of appeals agreed. The complainant said nothing about whether defendant's conduct offended her. When asked what if anything she saw defendant doing, the complainant responded, "I don't really know for sure." When pressed, she admitted seeing him "a little" and she mentioned she saw him masturbating but she stated that the act took place in front of her brother and not her, and she did not see his penis. After describing defendant's act of masturbation and characterizing it as "weird," the other complainant stated, "I think he was trying to be funny." When asked about his reaction, the complainant stated that he did not think the masturbation was funny. A presumption of offensiveness would have excused the State from proving an element of its case, and that was impermissible. Neither complainant testified that they were offended by defendant's conduct. Therefore, the State failed in its burden of proof.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff couple sued defendants, casino, casino employees, city, and police officers, for unlawful detention, assault, and unreasonable force. The Iowa District Court for Pottawattamie County granted summary judgment in favor of defendants. The couple appealed.


OVERVIEW: The casino employees asked the wife to either leave or submit to a preliminary breath test (PBT). When the wife refused to do either, uniformed off-duty officers were summoned. The claim that the couple was unlawfully detained was rejected as the wife had refused to leave the casino. Also, the court found the officers were entitled to qualified immunity as the officer's actions were reasonable.


OUTCOME: The grant of summary judgment in favor of defendants was affirmed.

 

527 of 583 DOCUMENTS


In re Marriage of Gahagen


No. 4-272 / 03-1731


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2004 Iowa App. LEXIS 926



August 11, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at In re Marriage of Gahagen, 2004 Iowa App. LEXIS 1604 (Iowa Ct. App., Aug. 11, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Scott County, Bobbi M. Alpers, Judge. James Gahagen appeals from the trial court's denial of his motion to modify an order dividing his military pension following the dissolution of his marriage to Mary Ann Gahagen.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a divorce decree, the trial court had ordered that upon appellant husband's retirement from the Army he pay appellee wife 50 percent of the marital share of his "disposable retired pay each month." Later, the Iowa District Court for Scott County denied his motion to modify the order to delete any award to the wife of any portion of the latter amount waived by him in order to receive veterans' disability benefits. The husband appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court denied the husband's motion, concluding that although the order required him to indemnify the wife if he were to receive disability pay, thus reducing her share of his disposable retired pay, the order did not require that he indemnify her with his disability pay. Under 10 U.S.C.S. 1408(a)(4)(B) of the Uniformed Services Former Spouses' Protection Act, 10 U.S.C.S. § 1408, and federal caselaw, a state court could not treat military retirement pay that was waived to receive veterans' disability benefits, as divisible property in a dissolution proceeding. Further, the Iowa Supreme Court had held that while veterans' disability benefits could be considered in the equitable granting of alimony or support, that type of payment could not be considered marital property. However, the trial court did not err in determining that the military pension division order did not require the husband to indemnify the wife with his veterans' disability benefits. It required him to pay any "make-up" amount only if, and to the extent he was able to do so, with a source of funds other than his veterans' disability benefits. Accordingly, the order did not violate the USFSPA.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Abrahamson


No. 4-446 / 03-1907


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2004 Iowa App. LEXIS 886



July 28, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 29, 2004
Reported at State v. Abrahamson, 2004 Iowa App. LEXIS 1777 (Iowa Ct. App., July 28, 2004)
Affirmed by State v. Abrahamson, 696 N.W.2d 589, 2005 Iowa Sup. LEXIS 65 (Iowa, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Lucas County, Richard D. Morr, Judge. Defendants challenge the district court's ruling ordering them to pay room and board costs at the Lucas County Jail.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmates sought review of an order from the Iowa District Court for Lucas County, which ordered them to pay room and board costs, pursuant to Iowa Code § 356.7(1) (2003), for their periods of confinement at a county jail.


OVERVIEW: After the inmates were convicted and released or transferred to other facilities, the sheriff filed applications for restitution and reimbursement to recover from them the costs of room and board for their separate periods of incarceration at the county jail. The inmates challenged the claims. The trial court ordered the inmates to reimburse the sheriff. On appeal, the court held that Iowa Code § 356.7 (2003) was not an unlawful delegation of legislative authority to the county sheriff contrary to Iowa Const. art. III, § 1. The court further found no merit to the inmates' claim that they were treated differently from other prisoners incarcerated in other counties who were subject to lower per diem room and board claims. As there were no guidelines or per diem rates set forth under § 356.7, the charges could vary from county to county. The court found no equal protection violation under § 356.7 as applied to the inmates. Finally, the court found that the sheriff, in setting and requesting reimbursement for room and board, did not deprive the inmates of due process as he provided both notice to the inmates and was equipped with an adequate standard by which to implement § 356.7.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

State v. Winters

COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2004 Iowa App. LEXIS 796



June 23, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Polk County, D.J. Stovall and Douglas F. Staskal, Judges. Defendant Bradley Winters appeals his convictions and sentences on drug related charges.
State v. Winters, 690 N.W.2d 464, 2004 Iowa App. LEXIS 1445 (Iowa Ct. App., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Iowa District Court for Polk County (Iowa), which convicted him of possession of methamphetamine with intent to deliver, in violation of Iowa Code § 124.401(1)(b)(7) (2001), conspiracy to deliver methamphetamine, in violation of § 124.401(1)(b)(7), and failure to possess a tax stamp, in violation of Iowa Code §§ 453B.3 and 453B.12.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's vehicle was stopped after a trooper observed it weaving. Narcotics agents called a canine unit to the scene, and, after the dog alerted, defendant was searched and a small amount of methamphetamine was found on him. A search was conducted on his vehicle and he was subsequently convicted of possession of methamphetamine with intent to deliver, conspiracy to deliver methamphetamine, and failure to possess a tax stamp.
