Also, the delay was attributable to defendant, because it was not possible for him to take depositions of the State's witnesses and have a hearing on all of the motions filed prior to December 9. Further, an agent's testimony was not hearsay pursuant to Iowa R. Evid. 5.801(c); he was simply testifying concerning the reason that he found it necessary to take an initial and responsive action. The warrantless search was justified under Iowa Const. art. I, § 8 by the existence of probable cause coupled with the exigent circumstances of the car being mobile.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

530 of 583 DOCUMENTS


Simons v. Mun. Fire & Police Ret. Sys. of Iowa


No. 4-199 / 03-0834


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2004 Iowa App. LEXIS 797



June 23, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Polk County, Darrell J. Goodhue, Judge. Kenneth Simons appeals the decision of the district court which upheld the ruling of the Board of Trustees Disability Appeals Board to award him ordinary disability benefits, instead of accidental disability benefits.
Simons v. Mun. Fire & Police Ret. Sys. of Iowa, 690 N.W.2d 463, 2004 Iowa App. LEXIS 1414 (Iowa Ct. App., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A medical board determined plaintiff police officer was incapacitated as a result of post-traumatic stress disorder. The police officer applied for accidental disability pension benefits. Defendant, the Municipal Fire and Police Retirement System of Iowa (MFPRS) awarded the police officer only ordinary disability benefits. Its appeals board affirmed the decision as did the Iowa District Court for Polk County. The police officer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The record established the police officer was exposed to several incidents of violent death. In order to receive accidental disability benefits for a mental injury, an officer had to show that his mental injury was caused or aggravated at some definite time and place, and that his mental injury was caused by something more than the day-to-day emotional stress. The appellate court rejected the police officer's claims that the relevant statute, Iowa Code § 411.6(5)(c), denied him equal protection of the law because it created an exception for the "at some definite time and place" requirement for diseases of the heart, lung, or respiratory tract, but not for mental diseases. There was a rational basis to distinguish between the former diseases, which could be difficult or impossible to link to a definite time and place, and post-traumatic stress syndrome, which could possibly be linked to a specific employment incident. Further, the police offer failed to show he had been subjected to more than usual stress for a police officer. Thus, there was substantial evidence to support the board's decision that the officer was entitled to only ordinary disability benefits.


OUTCOME: The decision of the agency board, and the judgment of the trial court, were affirmed.

 

531 of 583 DOCUMENTS


Wurpts v. Iowa Dist. Court


No. 4-232 / 03-0970


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


687 N.W.2d 286; 2004 Iowa App. LEXIS 719



May 26, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Sioux County, Gary E. Wenell, Judge. Kimberly Wurpts appeals the district court decision finding her to be in contempt of court due to visitation violations.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, mother, appealed the Iowa District Court for Sioux County decision finding her to be in contempt of court due to visitation violations. The district court concluded the grandparent visitation order in the case was not unconstitutional because it was combined with the visitation ordered for the father. The mother petitioned for writ of certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The mother argued the grandparent visitation order, based on Iowa Code § 598.35(6), was unconstitutional; thus, she was not in contempt. The instant court agreed. Section 598.35(6) was unconstitutional, as it failed to comport with the Due Process Clause on its face. As § 598.35(6) was unconstitutional, the mother was not found in contempt for failing to provide grandparent visitation. Also, the grandparent visitation order was vague, as it was not clear whether the grandparents were entitled to unlimited visitation as long as the father did not object, or whether they were limited to 25 percent of the father's visitation and only during times when he was unavailable. The father failed to show, beyond a reasonable doubt, that the mother willfully violated a court order. The grandmother made almost all of the arrangements for visitation, and the grandparents picked up the child for visitation. It was unclear whether the grandparents were acting on their own behalf or whether they were acting for the father. There was no evidence beyond a reasonable doubt that the mother was intentionally denying visitation to the father, as he almost never sought visitation on his own behalf.


OUTCOME: The decision of the district court was reversed.

Prouty v. Martin


No. 3-960 / 03-0677


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2004 Iowa App. LEXIS 220



February 11, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Linn County, K. D. Briner, Judge. Plaintiff appeals the district court's denial of her motion for a new trial and its grant of defendants' motion to tax costs.
Prouty v. Martin, 680 N.W.2d 378, 2004 Iowa App. LEXIS 251 (Iowa Ct. App., Feb. 11, 2004).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant motorist challenged a decision of the Iowa District Court for Linn County, which (1) denied her motion for a new trial in connection with her action for damages against appellees, a driver and an owner of a vehicle, and (2) granted a motion to tax costs against the motorist under Iowa Code § 677.10 (2001).


OVERVIEW: The motorist filed this action after being involved in an automobile accident with the driver. The driver and owner filed an offer to confess judgment, which the motorist rejected. At trial, the motorist was awarded damages, but in an amount less than that offered. The trial court entered the judgment and ordered the motorist to pay costs under Iowa Code § 677.10 (2001). The court affirmed. The trial court did not err in denying the motorist's motion for a new trial based on verdict inconsistency. Although the motorist claimed that the verdict was inconsistent because the jury awarded her damages for past medical expenses, but not for past loss of full use of body, case law did not support that this created an inconsistency. Furthermore, the motorist did not present evidence of a functional impairment due to her injury and the verdict was clear that the jury made certain credibility determinations. The court held that Iowa Code ch. 677 did not discriminate between different types of plaintiffs or defendants and it did not violate the Equal Protection Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV, Iowa Const. art. I, § 6. Thus, the ruling taxing costs against the motorist was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Stiltner v. State


No. 3-776 / 02-1499


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2003 Iowa App. LEXIS 1104



December 24, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Stiltner v. State, 796 N.W.2d 456, 2003 Iowa App. LEXIS 1847 (Iowa Ct. App., 2003)
Related proceeding at Stiltner v. Carter, 268 Fed. Appx. 496, 2008 U.S. App. LEXIS 5206 (8th Cir. Iowa, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Davis County, Richard E. Meadows, Jr., (trial) and Annette J. Scieszinski (postconviction relief), Judges. John Stiltner appeals his conviction and sentence for second-degree sexual abuse.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, VACATED IN PART, AND REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court for Davis County (Iowa) convicted defendant for second-degree sexual abuse. The conviction and sentence were affirmed on appeal and defendant's application for postconviction relief was denied by the trial court. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, on appeal, raised ineffective assistance of counsel claims predicated on the trial court's sentence under Iowa Code § 902.12 (1997). Defendant claimed some of the conduct forming the basis of the charge occurred before the effective date of § 902.12. He asserted counsel was ineffective in failing to ascertain whether the acts occurred before the effective date of § 902.12 and failing to argue that application of the statute to him violated the ex post facto clause. He argued that counsel should have asked the court to specify the dates on which the sex acts took place. However, he had not shown that this omission worked to his disadvantage. Had counsel done what defendant said should have been done, a record would have been created for application of § 902.12. As he suffered no prejudice, counsel was not ineffective. The jury verdict did not specify whether pre or post-1996 acts were relied on in finding guilt. Under these circumstances, the appellate court presumed that the jury may have based its verdict on pre-1996 acts. As § 902.12 did not take effect until 1996, application of the statute to defendant was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's denial of postconviction relief with respect to defendant's conviction. Defendant's sentence was vacated and the case was remanded for resentencing.

In re Ward


No. 3-830 / 02-1571


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2003 Iowa App. LEXIS 1106



December 24, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at In re Detention of Ward, 796 N.W.2d 456, 2003 Iowa App. LEXIS 1839 (Iowa Ct. App., 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Jefferson County, Michael R. Mullins, Judge. Respondent appeals following a jury verdict that found him to be a sexually violent predator.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury verdict, the District Court for Jefferson County (Iowa) found respondent to be a sexually violent predator. Respondent appealed.


OVERVIEW: Respondent was committed to the custody of the Iowa Department of Human Services pursuant to Iowa Code § 229A.7(3) (Supp. 2002). On appeal, he argued the jury instructions did not adequately define mental abnormality as requiring the State to show he had serious difficulty in controlling his behavior. Under controlling case law, the appellate court believed the jury instruction given was inadequate because it did not allow for a clear determination by the jury that respondent had serious difficulty in controlling his behavior. Accordingly, his commitment had to be reversed. His lascivious acts conviction was itself the qualifying overt act. Respondent's confinement for a sexually violent offense at the time the petition was filed relieved the State from establishing a recent overt act separate and distinct from the lascivious acts conviction. Because the jury instruction defining mental abnormality did not adequately instruct the jury that it had to find respondent had serious difficulty in controlling his behavior, the appellate court reversed respondent's commitment; if he was retried before release from confinement, the State did not need to plead or prove a recent overt act.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded.

Home Pride Foods of Iowa, Inc. v. Martin


No. 3-507 / 02-1094


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2003 Iowa App. LEXIS 1103



December 24, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Home Pride Foods of Iowa, Inc. v. Martin, 796 N.W.2d 456, 2003 Iowa App. LEXIS 1855 (Iowa Ct. App., 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Polk County, Robert D. Wilson, Judge. Home Pride Foods appeals from adverse jury verdicts for fraud and violations of the Truth in Lending Act.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part; and remanded for new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff food company sued defendant consumer, who cross-complained. The food company appealed from adverse jury verdicts and damage awards from the District Court for Polk County (Iowa), for fraud and violations of the Truth in Lending Act, 15 U.S.C.S. §§ 1601-1649.


OVERVIEW: A food company salesman came to the consumer's house to give a sales presentation for food company's line of frozen foods. The consumer agreed to purchase six months' worth of frozen food for a monthly fee. The food company salesman then offered her a gas grill at no additional cost. The consumer was led to believe that the grill would be free with her food purchase. The grill, however, was not free. When the consumer tried to cancel her contract the food company disallowed it, and when she stopped payments on the grill, she was sued. The jury returned verdicts in favor of the consumer. On appeal, the food company contended the punitive damage award should not be allowed because the jury did not award actual damages. Actual damages were shown. The food company asserted the punitive damages award was so excessive it should be reduced. Because the appellate court could not reconcile the punitive damage judgment with the due process requirements pronounced by case law, it was reversed and remanded. The penalty on the finance charge on the grill was statutorily limited to $ 1,000, so it was remanded to impose a penalty which did not exceed the statutory limit of $ 1,000.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded for a new trial on the punitive damage issue.

 

537 of 583 DOCUMENTS


In the Interest of B.C.


No. 3-694 / 03-0738


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2003 Iowa App. LEXIS 1091



December 10, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at In the Interest of B.C., 796 N.W.2d 455, 2003 Iowa App. LEXIS 1818 (Iowa Ct. App., 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Polk County, Robert A. Hutchison (motion to dismiss) and Paul R. Huscher (trial), Judges. A biological father appeals the juvenile court's refusal to vacate an order terminating his parental rights. Judge Hutchison affirmed; Judge Huscher affirmed in part and reversed in part.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Iowa District Court for Polk County refused to vacate an order terminating appellant biological father's parental rights because the trial court determined that the father was not a necessary party and had no standing to challenge the termination order. The father appealed. Intervenor adoptive parents cross-appealed, contending that their motion to intervene in the proceedings should be granted.


OVERVIEW: A notice directed to the father informing him that a petition to terminate had been filed was published on two occasions in a weekly newspaper. The notice stated that there would be a hearing before the trial court. The trial court entered an order terminating the father's parental rights. The trial court found that the presence of the biological mother, the biological father, and the minor child was waived. The father filed a petition to vacate the judgment. The trial court determined that the father had no standing to challenge the termination order because he was not a necessary party, in that he was neither required to be included on the petition under Iowa Code § 600A.5(3)(a), nor was he a putative father who filed a declaration of paternity in accordance with Iowa Code § 144.12A or an unknown putative father. On appeal, the court reversed, stating that the affidavit that the notice was published twice, standing alone, did not confer personal jurisdiction of the trial court over the father. The court also found that the father was a necessary party to the termination, because he was, at the time the petition was filed, a known, living parent of the child.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's determination and remanded for further proceedings, including a resumption of the termination hearing that was terminated on the trial court's own motion. The court held that the adoptive parents should be allowed to intervene in the termination action. The court affirmed the ruling that the adoptive parents be allowed to intervene in the trial on the petition to vacate if a hearing on that issue was held.

LDMG Corp. v. Webster County Bd. of Adjustment

State v. Giovanazzi


No. 3-617 / 02-1619


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2003 Iowa App. LEXIS 1000



November 17, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Johnson County, Sylvia A. Lewis, Judge. Ann Marie Giovanazzi appeals from her conviction, following jury trial, for operating while intoxicated (OWI), second offense.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her conviction, following a jury trial, for operating while intoxicated (OWI) in violation of Iowa Code § 321J.2 (2001). Defendant contended that the Iowa District Court for Johnson County erred in overruling her motion to dismiss because the district court did not have subject matter jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the district court did not have subject matter jurisdiction because § 321J.2 was not a properly enacted statute. The court affirmed the district court's decision, stating that § 321J.2 derived from several acts of the Iowa General Assembly, each of which contained the enacting clause prescribed by the Iowa Constitution. The general assembly properly authorized the compilation of these acts into the Iowa Code, and each statute in the Iowa Code provided the acts from which that section was derived so as to allow the public to readily verify that the statutes were proper expressions of the authority of the general assembly, duly enacted by that body. Defendant also challenged the legislature's authority to administer and enforce its traffic regulatory power through the Departments of Transportation and Public Safety. The court held that defendant had not met her burden to overcome the presumption that the legislature's delegations of authority to these agencies were accompanied by adequate standards or guidelines that allowed the agencies to accomplish a general purpose and public policy of the legislature without abdicating to them the right to legislate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

2003 Iowa App. LEXIS 834

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Carmody (In re Detention of Carmody), 2003 Iowa App. LEXIS 1758 (Iowa Ct. App., Sept. 24, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Henry County, David B. Hendrickson, Judge. John Carmondy appeals from his adjudication as a sexually violent predator.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Henry County District Court (Iowa) entered a final judgment that ordered respondent sexually-violent predator to be committed after the jury found him to be a sexually-violent predator. The sexually-violent predator appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State alleged the sexually-violent predator, a convicted sex offender, was a sexually violent predator and should be committed. He denied the State's allegations. The matter was tried to a jury. The evidence of whether the sexually-violent predator had serious difficulty in controlling his behavior was conflicting. The trial court instructed the jury, over his objection, that it could find he was a sexually-violent predator, if the State proved certain elements beyond a reasonable doubt. However, nowhere in the instruction did it say the State had to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that he had a serious difficulty controlling his behavior. The jury returned a verdict finding he was a sexually-violent predator. The trial court entered an order committing him. After he appealed, the appellate court found that he did not preserve for review his argument that the sexually-violent predator statute violated his rights under the United States Constitution. However, it also found that the trial court erred, as it should have instructed the jury that it had to find that the State proved he had serious difficulty controlling his behavior and that the error was not harmless.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded for a new trial.

 

542 of 583 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hartsfield


No. 3-375 / 02-0744


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2003 Iowa App. LEXIS 654



August 13, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief dismissed at Hartsfield v. State, 2012 Iowa App. LEXIS 7 (Iowa Ct. App., Jan. 19, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Scott County, David E. Schoenthaler, Judge. Napoleon Hartsfield appeals his convictions and sentences, following a bench trial, for possession of crack cocaine with intent to deliver and failure to affix a drug tax stamp.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty by the Iowa District Court for Scott County of possession of crack cocaine with intent to deliver (Count I), in violation of Iowa Code §§ 124.401(1)(c)(3), 124.206(2)(d), and 703.1 (2001), and failure to affix a drug tax stamp (Count II), in violation of Iowa Code §§ 453B.1(3)(d), 453B.12, and 703.1. Defendant moved for judgment of acquittal, which was denied. Defendant appealed his convictions and sentence.


OVERVIEW: It was the State's burden to prove at trial that defendant was in possession of 10 or more dosage units of crack cocaine in order to prove defendant was a "dealer" and thus in violation of the drug tax stamp statute. A total of 7 rocks of crack were found. The term "dosage unit" was not defined as .1 grams in ch. 453B or in the rules adopted by the director of revenue under Iowa Code § 453B.2. In fact, ch. 453B specifically defined "dosage unit" as the unit of measure in which a substance was dispensed to the ultimate user. The Court of Appeals of Iowa held that a "dosage unit" had to be defined as the unit of measurement in which the substance was dispensed to the ultimate user, in the case at bar, either $ 20 or $ 50 individual rocks of crack cocaine. Because defendant possessed only 7 individual rocks of crack cocaine, he possessed only 7 "dosage units" of the taxable substance. Thus, he did not fit under the definition of a "dealer" found in § 453B.1(3)(d). Therefore, there was insufficient evidence to have found him in violation of the drug tax stamp statute (Count II). The evidence was sufficient to have found him guilty of possession of crack cocaine with intent to deliver.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed in part, reversed in part, and the case was remanded for entry of judgment of acquittal on Count II for lack of sufficient evidence.

State v. Caldwell


No. 3-326 / 02-1405


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2003 Iowa App. LEXIS 672



August 13, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Polk County, Arthur E. Gamble, Judge. Defendant appeals from the judgment and sentence imposed upon his conviction for possession with intent to deliver more than five grams of cocaine base, in violation of Iowa Code section 124.401(1)(b)(3) (2001).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of and the sentence imposed by the District Court for Polk County (Iowa), which convicted him of possession with intent to deliver more than five grams of crack cocaine in violation of Iowa Code § 124.401(1)(b)(3) (2001) and imposed a term of imprisonment of not to exceed 25 years.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that he was deprived of his constitutional right to equal protection under the law because of the sentencing disparity between convictions for possession of powder cocaine and convictions for possession of crack cocaine. He claimed that this was racial discrimination because more African-American people used crack cocaine. Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed, as: (1) he waived his right to contend that Iowa sentencing law was unconstitutional, in that he failed to raise the issue in the trial court; (2) defendant failed to show that his defense counsel was ineffective for failure to assert the claim that the sentencing disparity discriminated against defendant on the basis of race, in that such a claim would have been rejected by the district court; and (3) defendant failed to show that he was prejudiced by his counsel's failure to present the disparity claim, in that Iowa Code § 124.401 was constitutional under a rational basis standard of review, because the increased penalty the legislature imposed for possession of crack cocaine was rationally related to the State's interest in curbing the increasing and widespread use of crack cocaine.


OUTCOME: The district court's judgment was affirmed.

No. 3-111 / 01-2028

2003 Iowa App. LEXIS 353



April 30, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Cedar County, Gary D. McKenrick, Judge. Michael Prince appeals from his convictions and sentences for first-degree and second-degree sexual abuse, in violation of Iowa Code sections 709.1(3), 709.2, and 709.3(2) (2001).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Iowa District Court, Cedar County, which convicted him of first-degree and second-degree sexual abuse.


OVERVIEW: Defendant allegedly committed a sexual assault on a child. As a result of defendant's actions, the child suffered an injury that required surgery. After defendant was convicted of two sexual crimes, he sought review. In affirming, the court determined that Iowa Code § 702.18(1)(c) was not unconstitutionally void for vagueness. Section 702.18(1)(c) adequately defined the terms "surgical repair" and "necessitates the administration of general anesthesia." The court noted that defendant only had standing to challenge the constitutionality of § 702.18(1)(c) as it applied to the facts of his particular case. A doctor testified that the only way to perform the necessary procedure was to use general anesthesia. Because § 702.18(1)(c) was constitutional, counsel was not ineffective for failing to raise the issue before the trial court. The court did not address defendant's arguments concerning counsel's effectiveness regarding an alleged failure to investigate and present certain witnesses. Finally, the court found that defendant's motion for an acquittal was properly denied, as there was sufficient evidence to show that defendant's genitals contacted the victim's anus.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

State v. Fevold


No. 2-996 / 02-0339


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2003 Iowa App. LEXIS 262



February 28, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Fevold, 2003 Iowa App. LEXIS 1150 (Iowa Ct. App., Feb. 28, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Polk County, Douglas F. Staskal, Judge. Defendant appeals from his convictions, following jury trial, for one count of sexual abuse in the second degree and two counts of sexual abuse in the third degree.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED; SENTENCE ON COUNT I VACATED AND REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury of sexual abuse in the second degree and two counts of sexual abuse in the third degree, in the Iowa District Court for Polk County. Defendant appealed, asserting the court trial erred in applying Iowa Code § 902.12(3) (2001) to his sentence for sexual abuse in the second degree, in overruling his objection to improper cross-examination, and that his counsel was ineffective for failing to object to hearsay.


OVERVIEW: Jury Instruction No. 15 instructed that the jury could find defendant guilty of sexual abuse in the second degree, Iowa Code §§ 709.1 and 709.3 (2001), if the State proved he performed a sex act with the child between November 5,1995, and November 4, 1999, and that the child was under 12. The appellate court concluded the trial court erred in applying the 85 percent rule, pursuant to Iowa Code §§ 902.12 and 903A.2, to defendant's sentence. The jury could have found defendant guilty based on an act or acts that occurred prior to July 1, 1996, the effective date of Iowa Code § 902.12, which imposed a mandatory minimum sentence for sexual abuse in the second degree. The application of § 902.12 to defendant violated the Ex Post Facto Clauses of U.S. Const. art. I, § 10 and Iowa Const. art. I, § 21. However, defendant was not prejudiced by the trial court overruling defendant's objection that his cross-examination exceeded the scope of direct examination, as substantially the same evidence was in the record from the testimony of two other witnesses without objection. The record was insufficient to address defendant's claim of ineffective assistance on direct appeal.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed. However, defendant's sentence for sexual abuse in the second degree was vacated, and the matter was remanded for resentencing. Defendant's claims of ineffective assistance of counsel were preserved for postconviction proceedings.

In re Det. of Matlock


No. 2-357 / 01-1094


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2003 Iowa App. LEXIS 107



February 12, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at In re Det. of Matlock, 2003 Iowa App. LEXIS 1269 (Iowa Ct. App., Feb. 12, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Black Hawk County, Todd A. Geer, Judge. Matlock appeals an order of civil commitment as a sexually violent predator, contending he committed no recent overt act and was not confined for a sexually violent offense, rendering his detention unconstitutional.



DISPOSITION: Commitment order reversed, and case remanded for dismissal of petition.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, alleged civilly committed predator (predator), sought review of the decision of the Iowa District Court for Black Hawk County, which found in favor of appellee State, found the predator to be a sexually violent predator pursuant to Iowa Code ch. 229A (1999), and civilly committed him.


OVERVIEW: The predator pled guilty to sexual offenses in 1985 and 1991. He discharged his sentences for both offenses. In 1996, he was convicted of theft. Because he discharged his sentence, the State petitioned to have him found a sexually violent predator, pursuant to Iowa Code ch. 229A (1999). A jury found him to be one, and he was civilly committed. On appeal, the predator contended that the application of the sexually violent predator statute to him was unconstitutional, as his most recent confinement was for a non-sexual offense, and he did not commit a recent overt act as defined in ch. 229A. The court stated that, because the predator was not confined for a sexually violent offense when the State served him with the ch. 229A petition, he was entitled to dismissal of the commitment order on that ground. Further, the predator's incidents of exposing himself while in prison for the theft conviction did not amount to recent overt acts, as the language of Iowa Code § 229A.4(1), (2) (1999) applied to individuals not presently confined in prison. Further, there was not substantial evidence to support the predator's commission of such an act.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

In re Det. of Willis


No. 2-358 / 01-1197

2003 Iowa App. LEXIS 108

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at In re Det. of Willis, 662 N.W.2d 373, 2003 Iowa App. LEXIS 1271 (Iowa Ct. App., 2003)
Post-conviction relief denied at In re Willis, 691 N.W.2d 726, 2005 Iowa Sup. LEXIS 15 (Iowa, 2005)
Related proceeding at Matlock v. Smith, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 20578 (N.D. Iowa, Feb. 15, 2013)
Related proceeding at Willis v. Palmer, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 181072 (N.D. Iowa, Dec. 30, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Henry County, E. Richard Meadows, Jr., Judge. The respondent, Damon Willis, appeals from a jury's finding he is a sexually violent predator under Iowa Code chapter 229A (1999).



DISPOSITION: District court decision reversed, and case remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a jury's finding that he was a sexually violent predator under Iowa Code ch. 229A (1999). He claimed, inter alia: (1) chapter 229A violated substantive due process; (2) the refusal by the Iowa District Court for Henry County of a proposed jury instruction violated due process; (3) the evidence was insufficient to support his commitment; and (4) the court did not have jurisdiction over him.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had not stated how his claim of unconstitutionality was preserved for review. Therefore, the appellate court did not consider his claims concerning the constitutionality of Iowa Code ch. 229A. Defendant next asserted that the district court erred in not including in its instructions the requirement of a finding he had "serious difficulty in controlling behavior." The Iowa Supreme Court interpreted Iowa Code § 229A.2(4) as requiring a showing of a serious difficulty in controlling behavior. The appellate court concluded Barnes controlled its resolution of that issue and required reversal. Defendant also contended that the State did not have jurisdiction over him for the purposes of filing the petition to commit him. He argued that holding the probable cause hearing after his release violated the procedures set forth in Iowa Code ch. 229A. The appellate court concluded defendant's argument misread ch. 229A and was without merit. The probable cause hearing was held the same day defendant was taken into custody. As defendant was not out of custody when the petition was filed, there was no requirement of a recent overt act to trigger the filing of a petition to commit.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed, and the case was remanded for a new trial.

In re Guardianship of Blair


No. 2-950 / 01-1565


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2003 Iowa App. LEXIS 102



January 29, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at In re Guardianship of Blair, 2003 Iowa App. LEXIS 1224 (Iowa Ct. App., Jan. 29, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Linn County, Thomas M. Horan, Judge. The guardians appeal from the parental visitation provisions of a guardianship order. The ward's mother cross-appeals the trial court's denial of a request to terminate the guardianship and its refusal to appoint a new guardian.



DISPOSITION: District court judgment affirmed, and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Iowa District Court for Linn County found that the child in interest had suffered neglect, and an instance of sexual abuse while in the care of appellee mother, and granted guardianship rights to appellants, the child's grandparents. The child was also placed in the grandparent's physical care. In the instant appeal, the grandparents appealed the trial court's parental visitation provisions of a guardianship order. The mother cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother renewed her constitutional challenges to Iowa Code § 633.552 (2001). The appellate court adopted the trial court's findings, that the mother did indeed neglect her child. For example, there was evidence the child suffered sexual contact by his cousin, and continued to suffer urinary difficulties from stress. Other evidence included the mother's pattern of missing the child's medical appointments, and exposing the child to her husband's intoxicated behavior. Meanwhile, the child had flourished under the care of the grandparents. The appellate court held the mother's constitutional challenge to § 633.552 was fatally flawed, because it failed to consider § 633.552 in pari materia with other relevant guardianship provisions which cured the infirmities dictating the outcomes in the United States Supreme Court decisions in Troxel and Santi. A nonparent did bear the burden of persuasion throughout guardianship proceedings. The grandparents met that burden. Further, the appellate court held the trial court's granting the mother the right to visit her child every weekend, and six weeks during the summer should have been more restrictive, and excluded overnight visits.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed, but the visitation issue was remanded to the trial court with instructions to grant the mother more limited, and supervised visitation, excluding overnight visits with the child.

In the Interest of N.F.


No. 2-947 / 02-1674


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2002 Iowa App. LEXIS 1327



December 11, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Clinton County, Arlen J. Van Zee, District Associate Judge. Mother appeals an order terminating her parental rights to two children.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother appealed the judgment of the Clinton County District Court (Iowa), which terminated her parental rights.


OVERVIEW: The mother argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by terminating her parental rights, as the termination violated her constitutional rights. The court of appeals disagreed. The evidence showed that the mother's husband had a chronic, severe, ongoing drug abuse problem. He was unsuccessfully discharged from substance abuse treatment programs. He refused to provide a drug test in July 2001, again in August, and again in September. It appeared to service providers that the husband was "high" when he appeared late for a supervised visit in August. The apparent purpose and intent of the trial court's orders was to encourage and work toward family reunification, but to do so while protecting the children from the danger presented by the husband's ongoing and unresolved substance abuse. It was the mother's insistence on exposing the children to the husband despite his unresolved drug abuse, not her desire and intent to maintain her marital relationship with him, that led the trial court to correctly conclude that the children could not be returned to her, despite almost two years of trial court involvement and the provision of services.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

N & N Sanitation, Inc. v. City of Coralville


No. 2-387 / 01-1211


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2002 Iowa App. LEXIS 1279



November 25, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Johnson County, L. Vern Robinson, Judge. The plaintiffs appeal from the district court's ruling on their action challenging the zoning decision of the City of Coralville.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, sanitation companies, brought an action challenging the zoning decision of defendant city. The Iowa District Court for Johnson County ruled that their business activity of transferring garbage did not fall within the light industrial zone. The sanitation companies appealed.


OVERVIEW: Due to the cheaper Illinois fees for waste-dumping in landfills, the owners of the sanitation company concluded it would be more economical to dump waste in Illinois. To accomplish this, they formed a second business. Garbage at this facility was transferred to semi-trucks, spilling on to the loading docks during the transfer. City officials received complaints about odors at the site. The sanitation company's first argument was that the city's interpretation of its zoning code expanded the restrictive scope of the ordinance beyond its plain meaning. The appellate court disagreed. As garbage, in being garbage, did not conclusively have merely a negligible environmental impact, the appellate court concluded the question of whether a truck terminal for garbage transfer fell under the zoning definition was subject to interpretation. Substantial evidence supported the trial court's conclusion that the ordinance did not include truck terminals where garbage was transferred. The ordinance also did not violate the Commerce Clause by imposing an undue burden on interstate commerce. Finally, the appellate court concluded that the sanitation companies were not denied procedural due process.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Spidle


No. 2-314 / 01-1144


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2002 Iowa App. LEXIS 1190



November 15, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Clinton County, James R. Havercamp. Judge. The defendant appeals his conviction and sentence, following a jury trial, for conspiracy to manufacture methamphetamine in violation of Iowa Code section 124.401(1)(b)(7) (1999).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Iowa District Court for Clinton County convicted defendant for conspiracy to manufacture methamphetamine in violation of Iowa Code § 124.401(1)(b) (1999). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that trial counsel was ineffective in failing to properly object to the admission of certain exhibits and in failing to raise an equal protection challenge to Iowa Code § 124.401(1)(b) (1999). The appellate court found that the trial court would not have abused its discretion in ruling the exhibits were admissible if counsel had made a timely objection. The exhibits were part of the circumstances of the crime, which was admissible in order to show the complete story. The State presented evidence that defendant conspired with the others to manufacture methamphetamine. The items found in a car were directly connected to the manufacturing process and were relevant to the conspiracy charge. Defendant's argument that counsel was ineffective in failing to raise an equal protection challenge to Iowa Code § 124.401 was preserved for postconviction relief proceedings. Iowa Code § 901.10(2) was rationally related to the government's interest to curbing the use of methamphetamine. The legislature had to determine the most appropriate method of punishing criminal activity. The statute did not violate defendant's right to be free from cruel and unusual punishment.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

In the Interest of D.C.-B.


No. 2-606 / 02-0784


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2002 Iowa App. LEXIS 1000



September 25, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at In the Interest of P.C.-B., 2002 Iowa App. LEXIS 1276 (Iowa Ct. App., Nov. 25, 2002)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by M. C-B. v. Iowa Dep't of Human Servs., 2003 U.S. LEXIS 3779 (U.S., May 19, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Floyd County, Gerald W. Magee, Associate Juvenile Judge. The mother appeals a juvenile court order terminating her parental rights to her two minor children.
In re D.C.-B, 2002 Iowa App. LEXIS 335 (Iowa Ct. App., Feb. 20, 2002)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Iowa District Court for Floyd County terminated the parental rights of appellant mother to her two minor children. The mother appealed, contending the trial court erred by: (1) judicially noticing evidence from prior proceedings; (2) determining there was clear and convincing evidence to terminate her parental rights; (3) not applying the exception to termination found in Iowa Code § 232.116(3) (2001)


OVERVIEW: The mother had a history of purposefully injuring herself, and was diagnosed with an attachment disorder. One child developed a severe rash that would clear up when the child was hospitalized, but reappear when the child returned home. On appeal, the mother objected to the admission of testimony from prior proceedings. However, Iowa Code § 232.96(6) allowed the use of hearsay evidence in juvenile proceedings, and the juvenile court could judicially notice exhibits that were part of the prior child in need of assistance proceedings (CINA) regarding the same children. The mother had not addressed her mental health problems, and her parenting skills did not improve because she was resistant to services. Thus, the evidence was sufficient to warrant termination of her rights under Iowa Code § x 232.116(1)(d), (f), and (i). The appellate court rejected the mother's argument that she was denied her right to confront and cross-examine adverse witnesses with regard to the evidence from prior CINA proceedings, again, because the trial court could judicially notice the prior proceedings. Finally, Iowa Code § 232.116 was not unconstitutionally vague and did not violate equal protection.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court, terminating the mother's parental rights, was affirmed.

State v. Zanoni


No. 2-184 / 01-0520


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2002 Iowa App. LEXIS 1021



September 25, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Story County, Michael J. Moon, William J. Pattinson, and Dale E. Ruigh, Judges. Zanoni appeals his conviction and sentence for drug possession, contending the evidence seized from him should have been suppressed and that his sentencing enhancement was in error.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Story County District Court (Iowa), which convicted and sentenced defendant for drug possession.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued, inter alia, that the district court should have suppressed evidence obtained following a stop of his vehicle. Defendant maintained there was neither reasonable suspicion nor probable cause to stop the vehicle. Defendant also contended the sentencing enhancement based on prior offenses was illegal. The appellate court rejected defendant's arguments. The court found that, together with the lateness of the hour, the animated nature of the vehicle occupants' initial conversation, and the hurried way in which they left the scene on seeing the police, a reasonable officer would have reasonably believed a crime was being committed. The court also held that the search did not exceed the scope of a legitimate pat-down search, because the officer conducted the pat down search to secure his safety and the safety of others. After finding a postal scale on defendant, the officer made an expanded search based on the newly added suspicion of drug possession. The court also found, under Iowa Code § 124.501(5), the district court correctly sentenced defendant as a third time offender.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Young


No. 2-180 / 01-0421


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2002 Iowa App. LEXIS 777



July 19, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Polk County, Donna L. Paulsen, Judge. Defendant appeals from the judgment and sentence entered following his guilty pleas to willful injury and robbery in the second degree.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment and sentence entered following his guilty pleas to willful injury and robbery in the second degree. He claimed on appeal his counsel was ineffective for failing to raise constitutional challenges to the imposition by the Iowa District Court for Polk County of victim restitution pursuant to Iowa Code § 910.3B(1) (1999) because the statute was violative of due process of law both facially and as applied.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended § 910.3B(1) violated procedural due process because it deprived the sentencing court of discretion concerning the amount of the award and thus judicial review of the reward was effectively nullified. The appellate court disagreed. The legislature was free to recognize the seriousness of certain crimes and impose greater punishment, or as under that statute, supplement criminal punishment for serious crimes by imposing mandatory restitution. The appellate court found no merit to defendant's claim that § 910.3B(1) was facially violative of his rights to procedural due process of law. Defendant did not suggest how his "as applied" challenge differed from his "facial" challenge to the statute. The appellate court was unable to discern any meaningful distinction between the two in the case at bar and therefore rejected his "as applied" procedural due process challenge for the same reasons. Neither did § 910.3B appear to be in meaningful conflict with federal bankruptcy law. Accordingly, defendant's counsel had no duty to challenge § 910.3B(1) on Supremacy Clause grounds, as such a claim appeared meritless.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Van Wyk


No. 2-320 / 01-1262


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2002 Iowa App. LEXIS 778



July 19, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Marion County, Terry Wilson, District Associate Judge. Dorothy Van Wyk appeals from her conviction, following trial to the court, for tampering with a juror in violation of Iowa Code section 720.4 (1999).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from her conviction, following a trial by the Iowa District Court for Marion County for tampering with a juror in violation of Iowa Code § 720.4 (1999). She contended: (1) the statute required the State to prove the victim was a juror at the time of the incident; (2) the record contained insufficient evidence to convict her under § 720.4; and (3) the statute was unconstitutional as applied to her.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued § 720.4 required the juror still be serving at the time of the retaliation. The trial court held the plain reading of § 720.4 indicated that a juror did not need be still serving on a case, since the section mentioned "retaliation for anything lawfully done." The appellate court agreed with the trial court's reading of the statute. Defendant's argument was at odds with the plain language of that portion of the statute. Defendant alleged there was insufficient evidence to prove: (1) she had a specific intent to intimidate, annoy, or alarm the juror; and (2) her call was without legitimate purpose. She asserted the legitimate purpose for the phone call was to gather information to help her friend with his appeal. Based on the facts and circumstances surrounding the phone call the trial court found that defendant made the phone call with the specific purpose to annoy or alarm the juror and it was done in a manner likely to cause her annoyance. The appellate court concluded there was substantial evidence in the record from which the trial court could have inferred defendant had the specific intent to intimidate the juror in retaliation for the guilty verdict.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

556 of 583 DOCUMENTS


State v. Allen


No. 2-452 / 01-0068


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2002 Iowa App. LEXIS 784



July 19, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Polk County, Scott D. Rosenberg, Judge. Defendant appeals his judgment and sentence for possession of more than five grams of crack cocaine with the intent to deliver and failure to affix a drug tax stamp, in violation of Iowa Code sections 124.401(1)(b)(3) (1999), 453B.3, and 453B.12, following a jury trial.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Polk County District Court (Iowa) with possession of more than five grams of crack cocaine with the intent to deliver and failure to affix a drug tax stamp. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction. The court of appeals disagreed. There was evidence which was persuasive beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant had sufficient dominion and control over the premises to establish constructive possession of the crack cocaine with intent to deliver. Defendant was on the porch when the officers arrived. The baggie of crack cocaine was on the porch and visible. The baggie contained a large amount of crack cocaine. There was evidence defendant was aware of the bag of cocaine and had touched it, as he indicated after his arrest that it might have his fingerprints on it. Defendant was in the company of a friend, who was found to have a large sum of money on his person. Defendant and the friend were the only people at the house when the police arrived. The evidence was sufficient to support a finding that the cocaine on the porch was in defendant's constructive possession, and that he had sufficient dominion and control over the area where the cocaine was found to establish that he possessed the crack cocaine with the intent to deliver.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Watkins


No. 2-089 / 01-0139


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2002 Iowa App. LEXIS 746



July 3, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by State v. Watkins, 2003 Iowa Sup. LEXIS 64 (Iowa, Apr. 2, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Dickinson County, Joseph J. Straub and Frank B. Nelson, Judges. Defendant-appellant Heidi Watkins appeals her conviction, following a bench trial, of child endangerment under Iowa Code sections 726.6(1)(a) (1999) and 726.6(1)(e), and multiple acts of child endangerment under section 726.6A.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was acquitted of murder, but convicted of child endangerment under Iowa Code § 726.6(1)(a), (e) (1999), and multiple acts of child endangerment under Iowa Code § 726.6A., in the Iowa District Court for Dickinson County. Defendant appealed, asserting that the prosecution impermissibly used inconsistent theories in her boyfriend's and her own separate trials and that the evidence was insufficient to sustain her convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed the State argued at her boyfriend's trial that he caused defendant's two-year-old child's death, and then proceeded to argue at her trial that she caused the child's death, thereby violating her due process rights. The appellate court held: (1) the acquittal on the murder charge rendered any challenge as to the consistency of the two murder charges moot, and the prosecutor's comment regarding sexual abuse in his closing argument in defendant's trial was not sufficient to raise a theory of inconsistency, as defendant was not charged with or found guilty of sexual abuse; (2) the denial by the trial court of defendant's motion for a bill of particulars did not violate her due process rights because the charges and the minutes of testimony were adequate to sufficiently apprise defendant of the charges against her; (3) medical evidence pinpointed the injuries as having occurred during the time frame found by the district court, and therefore, there was sufficient evidence to find multiple acts of child endangerment; (4) the diminished capacity defense was unavailable; and (5) Iowa Code § 726.6(1)(a), 726.6(1)(e) (1999), were not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed.

State v. Ayers


No. 2-010 / 01-0365


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2002 Iowa App. LEXIS 516



May 15, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Scott County, John A. Nahra, Judge. Dale Ayers appeals his convictions and sentences for second-degree murder, willful injury, and assault.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Scott County District Court (Iowa) of second degree murder, willful injury, and assault. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence of malice aforethought was insufficient to sustain his conviction of second degree murder. The court of appeals disagreed. The finding of malice in the case was not supported solely by evidence of defendant's anger. Defendant used a club to administer blows to the victim's back and face, and then kicked the victim in the ribs after he had fallen to his knees. Furthermore, defendant testified he intended to hurt the victim with each blow. Therefore, reasonable inferences from that evidence were sufficient to support the jury's finding of malice aforethought. In addition, defendant's counsel was not ineffective for failing to object to the trial court's imposition of restitution under Iowa Code § 910.3B because it did not violate the defendant's due process rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Johnson v. Louis


No. 1-957 / 01-0402


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2002 Iowa App. LEXIS 443



April 24, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Story County, Michael J. Moon, Judge. Plaintiff appeals a district court order denying a postsecondary educational subsidy for her child born out of wedlock.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought a modification of appellee father's child support obligation for her child born out of wedlock. The mother sought an extension of child support until the child graduated from high school, which was after he turned 18, and sought a postsecondary educational subsidy. The Story County District Court (Iowa) granted the child support extension, but denied the postsecondary educational subsidy. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court denied the request for post-secondary education subsidies for the mother's son, as there was no provision for such an educational subsidy under Iowa Code § 600B.25(1) similar to that for children of divorced parents under Iowa Code § 598.21(5A) (2000). On appeal, the mother alleged that the trial court erred in denying her request for a postsecondary educational subsidy. The appellate court agreed with the mother's contention. The district court was correct in its conclusion that § 600B.25(1) did not specifically provide for postsecondary educational subsidies, however, the court found that such a restriction, on the basis of illegitimacy, violated equal protection. The court held that the son born out of wedlock was entitled to the benefits provided by the current statute regarding postsecondary educational subsidies for divorced children, § 598.21(5A). The court remanded for a determination of the proper amount of subsidy to be awarded.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

 

560 of 583 DOCUMENTS


State v. Schweitzer


No. 1-920 / 01-0745


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


646 N.W.2d 117; 2002 Iowa App. LEXIS 613



April 10, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Approved for Publication June 17, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Johnson County, Sylvia A. Lewis, District Associate Judge. The defendant appeals his conviction and sentence following his guilty plea to charges of operating while intoxicated (OWI), second offense, in violation of Iowa Code section 321J.2(2)(b) (1999).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty in the Johnson County District Court (Iowa) to operating while intoxicated (OWI), second offense. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred by concluding that a juvenile adjudication for OWI constituted a prior offense for the purpose of charging and sentencing. The court of appeals disagreed. Iowa Code § 321.213 carved out a specific exception to the general rule set forth in Iowa Code § 232.55 prohibiting a juvenile adjudication from being later used in an adult criminal proceeding. Iowa Code § 321.213, in part, specifically provided that, notwithstanding Iowa Code § 232.55, a final adjudication in a juvenile court that a child violated the provisions of Iowa Code ch. 321J constituted a final conviction for the purposes of Iowa Code §§ 321J.2, 321J.4. Thus, by its own clear wording, juvenile OWI adjudications were considered final convictions for purposes of criminal charges under Iowa Code § 321J.2 and license revocation under Iowa Code § 321J.4. Therefore, the trial court did not err in considering defendant's prior juvenile OWI adjudication.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Armstrong


No. 1-790 / 00-2053


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2002 Iowa App. LEXIS 287



March 13, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied: Armstrong v. Iowa, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 75 (U.S. Jan. 13, 2003).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Polk County, Scott Rosenberg, Judge. The defendant appeals from his convictions for possession of a controlled substance, possession of marijuana, and failure to possess a drug tax stamp.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty by a jury verdict of possession of more than five grams of crack cocaine with the intent to deliver, failure to affix a drug tax stamp, and possession of marijuana in the Iowa District Court for Polk County. The defendant appealed his conviction on the grounds his Sixth Amendment right to confrontation was violated and that insufficient evidence existed to support his convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested at a home where there was suspected drug trafficking. Defendant and the home were searched incident to the arrest, and marijuana and crack cocaine were seized. The drugs were sent off to a laboratory for analysis, and the State used the reports as evidence. Defendant contended that his Sixth Amendment right to confrontation was violated by Iowa Code § 691.2, which allowed the introduction of the lab reports absent any in-court attestation from the preparers as to the reports' reliability. The appellate court agreed with defendant that laboratory reports were inadmissible as an exception to hearsay, if they were introduced without accompanying testimony by their preparer. The documents could otherwise be admitted however, if they possessed particularized guarantees of trustworthiness. The court found that, based on the inherent reliability of the reports, along with the presumption that a regularly enacted statute was constitutional, § 691.2 did not violate the Confrontation Clause. There was sufficient evidence to support defendant's convictions based on the amount of cocaine that was found by defendant when the police searched the house.


OUTCOME: The convictions were affirmed.

 

562 of 583 DOCUMENTS


Tri-State Outdoor Media Group v. Iowa DOT


No. 1-468 / 00-1628


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2002 Iowa App. LEXIS 304



March 13, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Polk County, Gregory A. Hulse, Judge. The petitioner appeals from the district court's ruling on judicial review affirming the respondent's revocation of the petitioner's advertising permit for a billboard and directing its removal pursuant to Iowa Administrative Code rule 761-117.6 when it was modified without a permit.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent Iowa Department of Transportation (DOT) revoked petitioner owner's permit for a billboard and directed the billboard's removal. The owner sought administrative review, then appealed to the Iowa District Court for Polk County, which affirmed the DOT's actions. The owner sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The permit for the billboard sign only allowed a structure with 15 posts, and the sign had 21 posts. There was no application to, or approval by, the DOT for any modification of the billboard sign, as required by Iowa Admin. Code r. 761-117.6(5). The owner contended that the order requiring the removal of the billboard violated its constitutional right to free speech. The appellate court found that: (1) the clear language of Iowa Admin. Code r. 761-117.6(5) did not require that the current permit holder be the entity responsible for the modification in order for the DOT to revoke the permit; (2) once a billboard was modified without prior approval the DOT was required to revoke the permit and require the removal of the billboard; and (3) there was no violation of the owner's right of free speech, as the state met its burden to show that traffic safety and aesthetics were substantial governmental interests, the statute and regulation directly advanced those interests, and the state went no further than necessary to serve these interests.


OUTCOME: The district court's judgment was affirmed.

State v. Focht


No. 1-509 / 99-1694


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2002 Iowa App. LEXIS 111



January 28, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Pottawattamie County, Timothy O'Grady, Judge. Mickey Focht appeals from his conviction and sentence for second-degree robbery.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Iowa District Court for Pottawattamie County, which convicted him of robbery in the second degree, in violation of Iowa Code §§ 711.1(2), .3 (1999). The district court sentenced him to a term of imprisonment not to exceed 10 years, and applied Iowa Code § 902.12(5) requiring defendant to serve 100 percent of the maximum term without parole or work release.


OVERVIEW: A man in a green car drove very close to the victim, then grabbed the victim's purse, and drove away. Defendant cashed two of the victim's checks, and confessed to taking her purse. Defendant testified he confessed to the crime because he was afraid of the police, and that on the date of the crime he was home all day. There was evidence defendant's actions placed the victim in fear of immediate serious injury by driving so close to her. The appellate court found that: (1) there was a rational difference between second degree robbery and extortion in that extortion did not require an immediate threat of physical harm; (2) the application of Iowa Code 902.12 to second degree robbery and failure to apply it to extortion did not violate the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment; (3) defendant's confession was sufficiently corroborated by other evidence; (4) the robbery conviction was supported by sufficient evidence; and (5) defendant failed to show that he was prejudiced by the ineffective assistance of trial counsel.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was affirmed.

State v. Garcia


No. 1-834 / 01-0070


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2002 Iowa App. LEXIS 119



January 28, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Polk County, George W. Bergeson, Judge. Alfredo Garcia appeals his convictions for possession with intent to deliver, and failure to affix a drug stamp.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant challenged the judgment of the Polk County District Court (Iowa), which convicted the defendant of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver, in violation of Iowa Code § 124.401 (1)(d), and failure to affix a drug tax stamp, in violation of Iowa Code §§ 435B.3 and 435B.12 (1999).


OVERVIEW: At trial, the prosecution introduced, over the defendant's objection, a laboratory report analyzing the contents and establishing the weight of the suspected marijuana packages found in the defendant's van. On appeal, the defendant claimed that the district court erred in admitting the laboratory report into evidence. The defendant argued that the admission of the laboratory report without accompanying testimony violated his U.S. Const. amend. VI right to confront witnesses. The appellate court rejected the defendant's contention and affirmed. Iowa Code § 691.2 provided for introduction of the report into evidence. The statute further provided that upon the request of a party or party's attorney, an employee or technician could be called to testify in person. The defendant made no such request. The defendant argued that the court should reexamine the rule in light of a recent Illinois Supreme Court decision, but the court declined. Based on judicial precedent in Iowa, the court concluded that the introduction of laboratory results without accompanying testimony did not violate the defendant's right to confront witnesses.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
