Delaney v. Bd. of Adjustment


No. 1-349 / 00-1034


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2001 Iowa App. LEXIS 504



August 15, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Black Hawk County, Bruce B. Zager, Judge. The plaintiffs appeal from a district court order denying their petition for writ of certiorari challenging the board of adjustment's decision to grant the National Cattle Congress a special permit to allow them to hold stock car races at the former Waterloo Greyhound Park.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant neighboring residents filed an application for writ of certiorari in the District Court for Black Hawk County (Iowa) to challenge the legality and constitutionality of appellee board of adjustment's grant of a special permit application. The district court annulled the writ. The residents filed a motion for enlarged findings and conclusions pursuant to Iowa R. Civ. P. 179(b). The district court denied the motion. The residents appealed.


OVERVIEW: A property owner in a planned industrial zone applied for a special permit to convert the property from a greyhound racetrack to a stock car racetrack. The board on remand at the zoning commission's request considered sound studies as well as comments from the public and unanimously reaffirmed its prior grant of the special permit application over the objections of the nearby residents. On appeal, the court found: (1) the board was not required to determine whether the racetrack was a nuisance, but merely consider the concerns of economic development and health, safety, and welfare of the residents; (2) all the board had to do in response to noise objections in applying the general health, safety, welfare standard was impose restrictions on the dates and times of races, order the construction of a sound barrier, and mandate that race cars have mufflers; (3) the city council was not required to review the special permit rather than the board; and (4) the city zoning ordinance was not unconstitutional because of the powers it granted the board.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed.

In re Det. of Springett


No. 1-162 / 00-0489


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


641 N.W.2d 547; 2001 Iowa App. LEXIS 509



August 15, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 15, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Pottawattamie County, James S. Heckerman (motion to dismiss) and James M. Richardson (trial), Judges. Robert Springett appeals from a jury's finding that he is a sexually violent predator.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was determined by a jury in the District Court for Pottawattamie County (Iowa) to be a sexually violent predator. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued the trial court denied him due process when it refused to instruct the jury a mental abnormality was a volitional impairment that made it difficult, if not impossible, for a person to control his or her behavior; erroneously instructed the jury his Nebraska conviction for first-degree forcible sexual assault was a sexually violent offense; and erroneously allowed the State to introduce the videotaped testimony of one of his victims after he admitted to raping the woman. On appeal, the court found the trial court: (1) did not err in denying defendant's proposed instruction regarding mental abnormality because the proposed instruction was unduly narrow; (2) did not abuse its discretion in concluding first-degree forcible sexual assault is a sexually violent offense; and (3) did not abuse its discretion in allowing the videotaped testimony of one of defendant's victims whom defendant admitted he raped since the testimony was relevant to prove his dangerousness and likelihood of re-offending.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed.

 

567 of 583 DOCUMENTS


State v. Thompson (In re Thompson)


No. 1-185 / 00-0887


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2001 Iowa App. LEXIS 422



June 29, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Wapello County, E. Richard Meadows, Jr., Judge. On appeal from a jury's finding that he is a sexually violent predator, the respondent argues chapter 229A is a punitive statute, violates the federal and state constitutional prohibitions against ex post facto laws, violates the Double Jeopardy Clauses of the state and federal constitutions, violates his right to substantive due process, and violates the Equal Protection Clauses of the state and federal constitutions. The respondent argues he was denied due process when the district court refused to give his requested instruction regarding the meaning of the term "likely to engage in predatory acts of a sexual nature." He also claims he was denied due process when the court refused to give an instruction allowing the jury to consider less restrictive alternatives. The respondent contends [*2] the court incorrectly ruled the proper jury size under chapter 229A is eight people, and he claims the court erred in admitting evidence of his prior bad acts when he was willing to stipulate to his prior convictions.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Iowa District Court for Wapello County found that respondent was a sexually violent predator. Respondent argued that Iowa Code ch. 229A violated the prohibitions against ex post facto laws. He challenged the denial of a requested instruction, and raised numerous other claims.


OVERVIEW: The State filed a petition alleging respondent to be a sexually violent predator under Chapter 229A. Prohibitions against ex post facto laws applied only to penal or criminal actions, as did double jeopardy guarantees. This was a civil proceeding; thus those protections did not apply. There was no substantive due process violation. The legislative scheme of Chapter 229A was rationally related to the State's interest in protecting the public. The State did not have a burden of proving beyond a reasonable doubt that no less-restrictive alternative treatment facilities were available. District court did not err in deciding an eight-person jury was sufficient. Proof of the prior qualifying convictions was essential and therefore relevant to the State's case, and respondent's willingness to stipulate to the convictions did not prevent the State from tendering evidence on the issue.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. Prior opinions addressed and rejected all of the arguments advanced by respondent. Trial court did not abuse its discretion in allowing prior bad acts testimony, jury size was proper, and there were no constitutional violations.

State v. DeVries


No. 1-166 / 00-0576


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2001 Iowa App. LEXIS 330



May 23, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Marshall County, Carl E. Peterson (pretrial motions) and Carl D. Baker (sentencing), Judges. Defendant appeals from his conviction for possession of methamphetamine, third offense. See Iowa Code § 124.401(5) (1999).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was convicted in the Iowa District Court for Marshall County for possession of methamphetamine, third offense. Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant contended the trial court erred in denying his motion to dismiss, in denying his motion to suppress, and in failing to suspend his sentence. Appellant contended in part that the drug laws violated equal protection guarantees by treating addicts as harshly as drug dealers, and by punishing repeated possession of marijuana differently than possession of all other types of drugs. The court of appeals affirmed, because the state had a rational basis for treating marijuana possession differently, and the statute provided penalties for the possession of methamphetamine, not its use. Further, it was not clear that appellant was not also manufacturing methamphetamine. Second, a preponderance of the evidence supported the search incident to arrest exception, as there was no credible evidence that the store's loss prevention employees detained appellant at the request of, or to assist law enforcement officers. Third, regarding sentencing, the possibility that appellant could have benefitted from treatment was outweighed by his failure to benefit from past probations and his continued pattern of criminal behavior.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

State v. Bailey, 1999 Iowa App. LEXIS 134 (Iowa Ct. App., Feb. 24, 1999)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court for Poweshiek County, Iowa, convicted defendant of possession of methamphetamine with intent to deliver, in violation of Iowa Code § 124.401(1)(c)(6). Defendant's appeal was denied. Defendant filed an application for postconviction relief, which was denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A police officer issued traffic citations to defendant, and performed a search incident to the citations. The search revealed methamphetamine and other drug paraphernalia. State v. Terry


No. 1-062 / 99-1617


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2001 Iowa App. LEXIS 260



April 27, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Johnson County, Stephen C. Gerard, II, District Associate Judge. The defendant appeals his convictions and sentences, following jury trials, for interference with official acts.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Johnson County District Court (Iowa), which convicted him for interference with official acts. Defendant's convictions arose out of two separate incidents.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in: (1) failing to grant his motion to dismiss based on the unconstitutional vagueness of Iowa Code § 719.1 (1999) as applied to the facts surrounding the interference with official acts charge; and (2) failing to instruct the jury on the theory of self-defense in the case involving the charge of interference with official acts causing injury. The instant court determined that defendant failed to preserve error on his vagueness challenge by filing his motion to dismiss in a timely manner. Even if defendant had filed the motion to dismiss in a timely manner, the instant court found defendant's constitutional claim to be without merit. Because police officers had reason to believe that defendant was either a witness to or a participant in a crime, they were within their lawful authority to detain defendant to resolve ambiguities in his conduct. Defendant's decision to disobey an officer's order and flee from the scene impeded the officer's duties. Thus, § 719.1 was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to defendant's conduct. The instant court did not address an ineffective assistance of counsel issue raised by defendant.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed.

2001 Iowa App. LEXIS 261

The respondent appeals, and petitioner cross-appeals, from various economic provisions of the parties' dissolution decree. Respondent contends: (1) the district court erred in awarding the petitioner monthly alimony of $ 2000; and (2) the district court's award of attorney fees was excessive. On cross-appeal, petitioner contends the district court erred in ruling that the prenuptial agreement between the parties was valid and enforceable. Both parties request an award of appellate attorney fees.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS MODIFIED.

OVERVIEW: Prior to their marriage, the parties signed a prenuptial agreement. The parties agreed to waive any claim to the other's separately-owned property, whether this property was owned at the time of marriage or acquired during the marriage, as well as any claim for spousal support or alimony in the event of divorce. Fourteen years later, petitioner sought a divorce. The trial court found the agreement valid. However, no appellate attorney fees were awarded.


OUTCOME: The lower court's order was affirmed as modified. The appellate court modified the amount of permanent alimony awarded to petitioner.

In the Interest of K.E.D.


No. 0-830 / 00-0732


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2001 Iowa App. LEXIS 141



February 28, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Linn County, Robert Sosalla, District Associate Judge. Imprisoned individual who was married to the mother when the child in question was born, appeals from an order of the juvenile court denying his request for visitation with the child.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant considered his wife's daughter to be his child, even though he was not the biological father. The child was placed in foster care, and a permanency plan was filed with the juvenile court recommending visitation for the child's biological parents. Appellant filed an objection to the plan, seeking visitation with the child as her legal father. The District Court, Linn County (Iowa) denied appellant's request for visitation.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the appellant contended that the juvenile court erred by denying him reasonable visitation with the minor child based on his status as her legal or established father. The court concluded that visitation with the appellant was not in the best interest of the minor child. Because the appellant was incarcerated, the minor child had not seen or interacted with him for more than 18 months and had no bond with him. Appellant was serving a sentence of 15 to 20 years, and therefore had no reasonable expectation of assuming a meaningful parenting role for the minor child during the period of her minority. Appellant's wife, who was also incarcerated, expressed a desire to divorce the appellant, and no longer wanted the appellant to take part in the child's life. The child's biological father, the only parent in her life who was not incarcerated, had stepped forward and taken an active role in her life. Additionally, the appellant's desire to make the minor child an important part of his life was contradicted by the fact that the appellant had no contact with his own biological children.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. The court held that the juvenile court did not err in denying appellant visitation. The court concluded based on the facts presented that it was not in the minor child's long-tern or immediate best interests to have visitation with the appellant.

Ashworth Farm Pshp. v. City of West Des Moines


No. 0-473 / 99-1292


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2001 Iowa App. LEXIS 5



January 10, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Dallas County, Gary G. Kimes, Judge. On appeal from the district court's ruling affirming a special assessment imposed by the city, the plaintiff argues the assessment exceeds the special benefit conferred, the trial court erred in not considering impact fee analysis evidence, and the assessment was unconstitutional.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner filed an action to challenge appellee city's special assessment district and the amount of appellant's assessment imposed for a four-lane road construction in particular. The Iowa District Court for Dallas County's ruling affirmed the special assessment. Appellant challenged the ruling.


OVERVIEW: Appellant owned a farm that bordered a two-lane road in a residentially developing area of appellee city. Appellee established an assessment district and special assessments for paving and complete reconstruction of the road as four-lane. Appellants challenged the $ 238,187 total assessment. Appellant argued the assessment violated Iowa Code § 384.62 by exceeding 25 percent of the total agreed value of the improved property as an farm. The circuit court upheld the assessment. The appeals court affirmed. The appeals court determined, in part, that (1) there was a strong likelihood the property would soon be homesites, (2) the new road conferred a special benefit on the property less than the increase in value of the property as homesites, (3) the assessment was less than 25 percent of the total homesite value, and (4) Iowa law did not require an impact fee analysis, which was more appropriate for larger areas than single projects. The appeals court concluded the amount assessed was not unfair or inequitable. Appellee's actions to set the special assessment district boundaries, in accord with proper procedures previously established, were not palpably arbitrary or irrational.


OUTCOME: The ruling was affirmed. Appellee's legislative action to determine boundaries for the special assessment district was not arbitrary or irrational; the railroad was a natural southern boundary. Appellant did not overcome the presumption that the assessment was correct. The assessment was not unfair or inequitable, did not exceed the special benefit accrued to the property, and was less than the statutory 25 percent of value limit.

In the Interest of J.J.L.


No. 0-593 / 99-1335


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2001 Iowa App. LEXIS 28



January 10, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:

NO DECISION HAS BEEN MADE ON PUBLICATION OF THIS OPINION. THE OPINION IS SUBJECT TO MODIFICATION OR CORRECTION BY THE COURT AND IS NOT FINAL UNIL THE TIME FOR REHEARING OR FURTHER REVIEW HAS PASSED. AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION MAY BE CITED IN A BRIEF; HOWEVER, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT CONSTITUTE CONTROLLING LEGAL AUTHORITY.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Worth County, Gerald W. Magee, Associate Juvenile Judge. J.J.L. appeals from a juvenile court order adjudicating him a delinquent for committing arson in the first degree.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction in the Iowa District Court for Worth County for first-degree arson, arguing the arson statute violated his right to due process because it was vague and overbroad, and the State did not prove the all of the elements of arson beyond a reasonable doubt.


OVERVIEW: Appellant juvenile placed a gift-wrapped package containing a home-made bomb in an elementary school classroom. The package had one protruding fuse, a cigarette lighter, and a note attached to it. After a teacher discovered the package, law enforcement officials destroyed it. Appellant was convicted for first-degree arson. He appealed, arguing the arson statute, Iowa Code § 712.1 (1999), violated his right to due process because it was vague and overbroad, and the State did not prove the all of the elements of arson beyond a reasonable doubt. Specifically, appellant focused on the purported vagueness of the phrase "combustible material" in the arson statute. The court held a penal statute was vague where it did not define the criminal offense with sufficient definiteness that ordinary people could understand what conduct was prohibited and in a manner that did not encourage arbitrary enforcement. However, the court affirmed, holding the statute was specific enough to provide guidance and fair notice to ordinary citizens of proscribed conduct and the State met its burden of proving every element of the offense to support the conviction.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed, because although combustible material was not defined within the arson statute, the statute was specific enough to provide guidance and fair notice to ordinary citizens of what conduct it proscribed. Further, the State presented compelling evidence of guilt and met each burden of proof to sustain the conviction.

Loder v. Iowa DOT


No. 0-655 / 00-0303


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


622 N.W.2d 513; 2000 Iowa App. LEXIS 65



December 13, 2000, Filed


NOTICE:   [**1] PURSUANT TO IOWA SUPREME COURT RULE 10(F), AS AMENDED MARCH 3, 1981, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION OF THE IOWA COURT OF APPEALS MAY NOT BE CITED BY A COURT OR BY A PARTY IN ANY OTHER ACTION PROCEEDING EXCEPT WHERE THE OPINION ESTABLISHED THE LAW OF THE CASE, RES JUDICATA OR COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL, OR IN A CRIMINAL ACTION OR PROCEEDING INVOLVING THE SAME DEFENDANT OR A DISCIPLINARY ACTION OR PROCEEDING INVOLVING THE SAME RESPONDENT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 26, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Clay County, Frank B. Nelson, Judge. The petitioner appeals from the district court's ruling on judicial review affirming the revocation of the petitioner's driver's license pursuant to Iowa Code section 321J.12 (1997) for a chemical test failure.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner motorist appealed a trial court's decision affirming the administrative revocation of his driver's license, entered by the Iowa District Court for Clay County (Iowa), after a test revealed the presence of marijuana metabolites in his urine following his arrest for operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated and where his sentence was enhanced based on a conviction which had occurred before he was 21 years old.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner motorist was arrested for operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated in violation of Iowa Code § 321J.2 (1997). A requested urine sample revealed marijuana metabolites in his system. Based on the test results showing the metabolites were present, respondent Iowa Department of Transportation gave petitioner notice his license would be revoked for one year under Iowa Code § 321J.12(1). The revocation was enhanced under Iowa Code § 321J.2A because of a prior conviction entered before petitioner was 21 years old. Petitioner contested his license revocation, but it was administratively upheld. He appealed. The trial court upheld the revocation. Petitioner again appealed. The court affirmed. Petitioner's substantive due process rights were not violated because the statute prohibiting driving while having a controlled substance in one's system was rationally related to the governmental goal of protecting other drivers and was a valid exercise of the state's police power. Also, the statute allowing for the sentence to be enhanced did not violate petitioner's ex post facto rights because it did not punish what previously had been an innocent act.


OUTCOME: Trial court's ruling which affirmed the revocation of petitioner's driver's license affirmed because the statutory sections under which petitioner was convicted and sentenced violated neither his substantive due process nor ex post facto rights, and thus, were constitutional.

 

578 of 583 DOCUMENTS


State v. Williams


No. 0-591 / 99-1312


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2000 Iowa App. LEXIS 91



December 13, 2000, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO IOWA SUPREME COURT RULE 10(F), AS AMENDED MARCH 3, 1981, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION OF THE IOWA COURT OF APPEALS MAY NOT BE CITED BY A COURT OR BY A PARTY IN ANY OTHER ACTION PROCEEDING EXCEPT WHERE THE OPINION ESTABLISHED THE LAW OF THE CASE, RES JUDICATA OR COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL, OR IN A CRIMINAL ACTION OR PROCEEDING INVOLVING THE SAME DEFENDANT OR A DISCIPLINARY ACTION OR PROCEEDING INVOLVING THE SAME RESPONDENT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at Williams v. State, 2007 Iowa App. LEXIS 9 (Iowa Ct. App., Jan. 18, 2007)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Williams v. Ault, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 3682 (N.D. Iowa, Jan. 19, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Cerro Gordo County, Paul W. Riffel, Judge. Defendant appeals his convictions for first-degree robbery and first-degree murder.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment from the Iowa District Court for Cerro Gordo County, convicting him of first-degree murder and first-degree robbery.


OVERVIEW: The State filed a two count trial information charging defendant with murder in the first degree and robbery in the first degree. The charges stemmed from the robbery and shooting death of the victim in his home. A jury returned verdicts of guilty on both counts. In affirming, the court determined that defendant suffered no prejudicial error as a result of the district court's refusal to amend the uniform jury instructions. The court determined that photo arrays were not impermissibly suggestive and the identification was reliable. An agent's statement was appropriately offered to show defendant's reaction to the agent's theory about a third person's role in the murder and robbery. The evidence was strong that defendant actually provided crack cocaine to the third person and his girlfriend. In turn, this evidence tended to prove defendant and the third person would be more likely to participate in a crime motivated by the desire to obtain drugs and money. Defendant could not show trial counsel breached an essential duty. Finally, the imposition of a fine of $ 150,000 was not excessive.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. Trial court did not err in refusing to modify jury instructions, photographic lineup was not unduly suggestive, evidence of crack cocaine sales was not more prejudicial than it was probative, counsel did not render ineffective assistance, and fine was not excessive.

 

579 of 583 DOCUMENTS


Napier v. Iowa DOT


No. 0-480 / 99-1380


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2000 Iowa App. LEXIS 92



December 13, 2000, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO IOWA SUPREME COURT RULE 10(F), AS AMENDED MARCH 3, 1981, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION OF THE IOWA COURT OF APPEALS MAY NOT BE CITED BY A COURT OR BY A PARTY IN ANY OTHER ACTION PROCEEDING EXCEPT WHERE THE OPINION ESTABLISHED THE LAW OF THE CASE, RES JUDICATA OR COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL, OR IN A CRIMINAL ACTION OR PROCEEDING INVOLVING THE SAME DEFENDANT OR A DISCIPLINARY ACTION OR PROCEEDING INVOLVING THE SAME RESPONDENT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Chickasaw County, John Bauercamper, Judge. The petitioner appeals from the district court's ruling on judicial review affirming the respondent's revocation of his driver's license for a chemical test refusal under the implied consent law.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the Iowa District Court for Chickasaw County (Iowa) affirming appellee department of transportation's decision revoking his drivers license for refusing to submit to a chemical test after being arrested for driving under the influence of alcohol.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was pulled over by a police officer for a minor traffic infraction. The officer immediately suspected appellant was operating his vehicle under the influence (OWI) and arrested him. Appellant failed to submit to a chemical test and the officer invoked Iowa's implied consent law and issued a notice that his license be revoked, based on his refusal and a prior OWI arrest. Appellee department of transportation held a hearing on the officer's recommendation and concluded appellant's license should be revoked. Appellant challenged appellee's decision, arguing it was not supported by substantial evidence, was unreasonable, arbitrary and capricious, and that Iowa's statutory implied consent scheme violated substantive due process and the constitutional prohibition against unreasonable searches and seizures. The court noted appellee articulated the correct law, judiciously applied the law to the facts it chose to believe, and reached a reasoned conclusion; therefore, its actions were not arbitrary or capricious. The court went on to affirm, holding a person who was properly arrested had no valid U.S. Const. amend. IV objection to submission of body fluid specimens.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed, because appellee articulated the correct law, applied the law to the facts it chose to believe, and reached a reasoned conclusion; therefore, its actions were not arbitrary or capricious. Further, the implied consent law did not violate appellant's constitutional rights because it was a search incident to a valid arrest.

State v. Williams


No. 0-225 / 99-0551


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


2000 Iowa App. LEXIS 117



August 16, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Decision reached on appeal by State v. Williams, 652 N.W.2d 844, 2002 Iowa App. LEXIS 869 (Iowa Ct. App., 2002)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Cerro Gordo County, Paul W. Riffel, Judge. Defendant appeals from his convictions for first-degree murder and first-degree robbery.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Substantial circumstantial evidence supported a finding that defendant was guilty of murder and robbery because the victim's son saw three men enter the victim's house, and identified defendant to be the one carrying a gun; evidence indicated that the gun used to shoot the victim had been in defendant's possession shortly before the shooting and was found hidden in his brother-in-law's house; [2]-The trial court did not err under Iowa R. Crim. P. 10(10)(b) in denying defendant's motion for a change of venue because he failed to show the publicity created such a degree of prejudice in the county that there was a substantial likelihood a fair and impartial trial could not be had there; [3]-It was necessary to remand the case for a hearing to determine whether a conflict of interest existed by virtue of a relationship between defense counsel and an assistant county attorney.


OUTCOME: Affirmed in part and remanded.

 

581 of 583 DOCUMENTS


Collins-Draine v. Knief


No. 0-2006 / 98-789


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


617 N.W.2d 679; 2000 Iowa App. LEXIS 12



July 26, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Approved for Publication October 13, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Black Hawk County, George L. Stigler, Judge. Plaintiffs appeal from a district court ruling, following a bench trial, which dismissed their civil rights and false arrest claims against defendants.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged the ruling of the Iowa District Court for Black Hawk County dismissing their civil rights and false arrest claims against appellees, after a bench trial.


OVERVIEW: Appellee officer requested permission to search appellant daughter's vehicle, after she left a hotel at which drug trafficking had been reported, and permission was granted. Appellee found nothing illegal, but transported her to the police station. Appellant mother went to the police station, with appellant son. Appellants mother and son were detained at the police station for three hours. Appellant daughter was detained there for six hours. Appellants sued appellees for false arrest and violation of civil rights under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The trial court, after a trial, dismissed the complaint and appellants sought review. While the trial court's judgment upholding the initial stop of appellant daughter was upheld as not being patently unreasonable, appellee officer's transportation to the police station and continued detention of her after his unfruitful search of her vehicle was without constitutional authority. Appellee officer's detention of appellants mother and son was also unconstitutional, as he had no reason to suspect them of any wrongdoing, and detention of a citizen because they might warn a suspect was not constitutionally authorized.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of appellants' complaint was reversed because the investigatory stop of appellant daughter became an arrest without probable cause when she was transported to the police station. The finding that the detention of appellants mother and son was too brief to be unconstitutional was not supported by the evidence, nor was any unreasonable seizure, however brief, permitted.

 

582 of 583 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hy-Vee, Inc.


No. 0-232/99-0834


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


616 N.W.2d 669; 2000 Iowa App. LEXIS 10



June 14, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Approved for Publication September 18, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Dubuque County, Richard R. Gleason, District Associate Judge. Defendant appeals its conviction of selling alcoholic beverages to an underage patron under Iowa Code sections 123.49(2)(h) and 123.50(1) (Supp. 1997).



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant retail food store corporation requested review of a judgment of the Iowa District Court for Dubuque County under which it was convicted of selling alcoholic beverages to an underage patron under Iowa Code §§ 123.49(2)(h), 123.50(1) (Supp. 1997).


OVERVIEW: An employee of appellant retail food store corporation sold alcohol to a minor. Appellant was convicted under Iowa Code § 123.49(2)(h), 123.50(1) (Supp. 1997) of selling alcoholic beverages to an underage patron. Those crimes were characterized as serious misdemeanors. The § 123.50(1) conviction was a vicarious criminal conviction as it did not require a finding of appellant's fault. The convictions were reversed and remanded for dismissal. Section 123.50(1) was declared unconstitutional as it could not have survived a three-part public welfare analysis to circumvent due process requirements. Specifically the stigma to the appellant attached with conviction of the serious misdemeanor charge was grave and damaging to its corporate reputation. The violation of § 123.49(2)(h) was reversed because there were no allegations appellant knew or failed to exercise reasonable care to ascertain whether the person was under legal age.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was reversed and remanded for entry of dismissal. There was no evidence of appellant's culpability in the sale to support a conviction under one section. The other section, under which a corporation vicariously committed a grave serious misdemeanor when its employee sold alcohol to minors, was declared unconstitutional. It did not survive a three-part public welfare analysis to circumvent due process.

Iowa Waste Sys. v. Buchanan County


No. 0-163/99-751


COURT OF APPEALS OF IOWA


617 N.W.2d 23; 2000 Iowa App. LEXIS 9



May 31, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Approved for Publication September 18, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Iowa District Court for Buchanan County, L.D. Lybbert, Judge. Iowa Waste Systems appeals a ruling finding Buchanan County and the Buchanan County Sanitary Landfill Commission were not liable for leachate control and management measures Iowa Waste Systems had undertaken after the County terminated its lease to operate the landfill.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landfill lessee and operator requested review of an Iowa District Court for Buchanan County judgment finding appellee county and county and landfill commission not liable to appellant under either implied in fact contract or unjust enrichment for leachate recirculation, and that awarded breach of contract damages to appellee for appellant's inadequate soil cover of waste and failure to restore landfill and borrow areas to farmland.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was a landfill lessee, and became the operator when assigned that landfill operating contract (contract) by a third party. Appellees were county and county landfill commission. Under the contract appellees were to control the leachate. Appellees terminated the contract, so no further waste was dumped. The lease had eight months to run. Appellant refused appellees requested access to come on the land to control the leachate. The court affirmed the judgment for appellees. There was no implied in fact contract that appellees would pay for appellant to recirculate leachate since appellees' actions did not indicate assent to pay appellant for recirculation. There was no unjust enrichment since appellant did not carry burden to show recirculation was a benefit, and appellant did not show an inequity from failure to order unjust enrichment. Appellant was to pay appellee contract damages for failure to intermediately cover the trash with soil in accord with state regulations, and for failure to restore both the trash dump area and the area where from which soil was borrowed for intermediate cover (borrow area) to farmland.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. Appellant's failure at end of landfill operating contract before end of lease to allow appellees on land to fulfill their duty to control leachate did not show appellees' would pay appellant for leachate recirculation; neither did appellant show benefit to appellees or notion of justice for unjust enrichment. Intermediate soil cover required by state and restoration of cover and waste areas to farmland were required.
